# Roadmap — tusq.dev Docs & Website Platform

> **M37 Charter Bound — 2026-04-27 in run_0b366d58febc99be (turn_741c43114034bab7, PM attempt 1) at HEAD `f2a153b`.** Intake charter `intent_1777286540380_ef16` (vision_scan, category `roadmap_exhausted_vision_open`, charter "Derive next bounded roadmap increment from VISION.md. Candidate pool: The Promise, Code And API Surface, Database, Warehouse, And Data Model, Frontend, Design System, And Product UX, Domain Model And Workflows (+25 more). Current roadmap checked through M36: Static Capability Confidence Tier Index Export from Manifest Evidence (~0.5 day) — V1.17 (SHIPPED)."). Independently verified on HEAD `f2a153b` that M36 V1.17 is substantively shipped with all 20 ROADMAP checkboxes flipped to `[x]`; `npm test` exits 0 with "Smoke tests passed" and "Eval regression harness passed (27 scenarios)"; the 20-command CLI surface (init, scan, manifest, compile, serve, review, docs, approve, **auth**, **confidence**, diff, domain, effect, method, policy, redaction, sensitivity, surface, version, help) is intact with `confidence` between `auth` and `diff`. The charter's `roadmap_exhausted_vision_open` classification is correct — the candidate pool from VISION.md still contains unbound material, particularly **§ Data Leakage** (lines 705–707, under § Risks) which has NOT been the primary aggregation-axis source for any shipped milestone (M28/M33 cite § Data, Risk, And Sensitivity for sensitivity-class derivation/aggregation but neither aggregates capabilities by PII-volume tier; M25 derives `pii_fields[]` per capability but no shipped command rolls those array lengths into a per-tier bucket index). Charter honored by binding exactly one new bounded testable milestone — **M37: Static Capability PII Field Count Tier Index Export from Manifest Evidence (~0.5 day) — V1.18 (PROPOSED)** — derived from VISION sources NOT yet primary aggregation-axis source for any shipped milestone: **`.planning/VISION.md` lines 705–707 (`### Data Leakage` under § Risks)** ("Runtime traces, support tickets, docs, and databases can contain customer secrets. Imports must minimize raw value capture, redact aggressively, preserve provenance, and make unsafe source handling visible.") and re-cited cross-axis flag justification: **`.planning/VISION.md` lines 108–114 (`### Data, Risk, And Sensitivity`)** ("PII, payment data, secrets, regulated data, and customer-sensitive fields ... capability risk tags and review recommendations"). Scope: M37 introduces a new top-level noun `pii` with single subcommand `index`, growing the CLI surface from 20 → 21 commands with `pii` inserted alphabetically between `method` and `policy` (`method` vs `pii`: `m` < `p`; `pii` vs `policy`: `pi` < `po` because `i` < `o`). The closed five-value `pii_field_count_tier` bucket-key enum is `none | low | medium | high | unknown`; the closed two-value `aggregation_key` enum is `tier | unknown`; the tier function is PM-frozen (`none if pii_fields.length === 0`, `low if 1 <= length <= 2`, `medium if 3 <= length <= 5`, `high if length >= 6`, `unknown if pii_fields is null/undefined/missing/not-an-array OR contains any non-string element OR contains the empty string`). Boundaries `0/2/5/6` are immutable once M37 ships; any threshold or enum change is a material governance event under its own ROADMAP milestone. The frozen 8-field per-bucket entry shape mirrors M31/M32/M33/M34/M35/M36 (`pii_field_count_tier`, `aggregation_key`, `capability_count`, `capabilities[]`, `approved_count`, `gated_count`, `has_destructive_side_effect`, `has_restricted_or_confidential_sensitivity`); a top-level `warnings[]` array is added (only in `--json`) capturing per-capability `pii_fields`-malformed warnings (non-array, non-string element, or empty-string element). Bucket iteration order is the closed-enum order `none → low → medium → high → unknown` (NOT manifest first-appearance, NOT count-numeric-ascending — the order is a deterministic stable-output convention only and MUST NOT be described as "PII-exposure-ranked," "data-leakage-ranked," or "redaction-priority-ordered"). Within each bucket, capability names follow manifest declared order. The `--tier` filter is case-sensitive lowercase-only; uppercase values like `HIGH` exit 1 (mirroring M35/M36 precedent). Read-only invariants mirror M27/M28/M29/M30/M31/M32/M33/M34/M35/M36 plus the explicit non-persistence rule: `pii_field_count_tier` MUST NOT be persisted into `tusq.manifest.json` (it is reviewer-aid metadata only; persistence is reserved for a deferred M-PII-Persistence-1 milestone). The mutually exclusive alternative forms (`tusq pii-volume index` (hyphenated noun rejected per M33 precedent), `tusq pii-fields index`, `tusq leakage index` (overscopes — leakage includes runtime trace handling, log redaction, and database-egress filtering), `tusq capability index --by pii_field_count_tier` (axis-flag rejected per M27/M30/M31/M32/M33/M34/M35/M36 single-aggregation-axis precedent), extending `tusq redaction review` with a tier filter (would conflate per-capability filter with per-bucket roll-up)) are explicitly rejected. Eval regression scenario `pii-field-count-tier-index-determinism` brings the harness from 27 → **≥28** scenarios. Constraint 30 (proposed) codifies the planning-aid framing and forbids "runtime PII detection / runtime data-leakage prevention / GDPR/HIPAA/PCI/PHI compliance certification / runtime field redaction enforcement / alteration of M25 canonical PII name set / persistence of `pii_field_count_tier` into the manifest / cross-axis statistical aggregation" framings in docs/README/CLI-help. Six Key Risk rows added (misread as runtime PII detector / data-leakage gate / compliance certifier; silent threshold drift on `0/2/5/6`; silent enum drift on the five-value `pii_field_count_tier` OR two-value `aggregation_key`; manifest mutation through index generation; `--out` path traversal into `.tusq/`; closed-enum order mistaken as PII-exposure-precedence + case-folding drift on `--tier`). Deferred successor milestones (M-PII-Category-Index-1 multi-valued aggregation by individual PII category, M-Risk-1 cross-axis risk tier, M-PII-Statistics-1 distribution roll-up with `min`/`max`/`mean`/percentiles/histograms, M-PII-Persistence-1 if persistence is later authorized) ship under their own ROADMAP entries with fresh acceptance contracts. The MCP-descriptor candidate (the long-standing outstanding charter sketch in `.planning/ROADMAP_NEXT_CANDIDATES.md` § "MCP Server Static Descriptor Export") remains unbound this turn — the form-decision A/B/C blocker is unresolved and is reserved for a future PM turn. Independent baseline re-verified on HEAD `f2a153b`: `npm test` exits 0 with "Smoke tests passed" and "Eval regression harness passed (27 scenarios)"; the 20-command CLI surface is intact (M37 is unchecked planned work, not shipped — the 21st command `pii` lands in implementation). The full SYSTEM_SPEC § M37 and command-surface § M37 detail blocks are owned by the dev role's implementation phase per the M27/M28/M29/M30/M31/M32/M33/M34/M35/M36 PM-vs-dev ownership split (PM charters; dev materializes the full spec/algorithm details before any code lands). (3) Milestone is bounded, testable, and does not duplicate existing checked milestones — Bounded: ~0.5 day, single new noun `pii`, single subcommand `index`, four flags, no new dependency. > **M36 Charter Bound — 2026-04-26 in run_8580d828f0e1cc1e (turn_f657958213bbfb9d, PM attempt 1) at HEAD `7c6b47e`.** Intake charter `intent_1777245829806_cf3c` (vision_scan, category `roadmap_exhausted_vision_open`, charter "Derive next bounded roadmap increment from VISION.md. The charter is honored by binding exactly one new bounded testable milestone — **M36: Static Capability Confidence Tier Index Export from Manifest Evidence (~0.5 day) — V1.17 (PROPOSED)** — derived from VISION sources NOT yet primary aggregation-axis source for any shipped milestone: **`.planning/VISION.md` lines 128–141 (`### Source Inventory And Confidence`)** ("tusq.dev should produce an input inventory before it claims understanding ... confidence by domain ... The engine should not pretend all inputs are equal.") and **`.planning/VISION.md` lines 709–711 (`### False Governance Confidence` under § Risks)** ("Labels such as `approved`, `restricted`, `confidential`, or `auth_scheme: bearer` are not magic. The product must distinguish reviewer-aid metadata from runtime enforcement."). Scope: M36 introduces a new top-level noun `confidence` with single subcommand `index`, growing the CLI surface from 19 → 20 commands with `confidence` inserted alphabetically between `auth` and `diff`. The closed four-value `confidence_tier` bucket-key enum is `high | medium | low | unknown`; the closed two-value `aggregation_key` enum is `tier | unknown`; the tier function is PM-frozen at `high if confidence >= 0.85`, `low if confidence < 0.6`, `medium if 0.6 <= confidence < 0.85`, `unknown if confidence is null/missing/non-numeric/NaN/+Infinity/-Infinity/out-of-[0,1]`. Boundaries `0.85` and `0.6` are immutable once M36 ships; any threshold or enum change is a material governance event under its own ROADMAP milestone with a fresh re-approval expectation. The frozen 8-field per-bucket entry shape mirrors M31/M32/M33/M34/M35 (`confidence_tier`, `aggregation_key`, `capability_count`, `capabilities[]`, `approved_count`, `gated_count`, `has_destructive_side_effect`, `has_restricted_or_confidential_sensitivity`); a top-level `warnings[]` array is added (only in `--json`) capturing per-capability out-of-range/non-numeric `confidence` warnings. Bucket iteration order is the closed-enum order `high → medium → low → unknown` (NOT confidence-numeric-descending — the order is a deterministic stable-output convention only and MUST NOT be described as "evidence-strength-ranked," "trust-ranked," "highest-quality-first"). Within each bucket, capability names follow manifest declared order. The `--tier` filter is case-sensitive lowercase-only; uppercase values like `HIGH` exit 1 (mirroring M35 `--scheme` precedent). Read-only invariants mirror M27/M28/M29/M30/M31/M32/M33/M34/M35 plus the explicit non-persistence rule: `confidence_tier` MUST NOT be persisted into `tusq.manifest.json` (it is reviewer-aid metadata only; persistence is reserved for a deferred M-Confidence-Persistence-1 milestone with its own acceptance contract). The mutually exclusive alternative forms (`tusq quality index`, `tusq evidence index`, `tusq capability index --by confidence_tier`, extending `tusq review` with a tier filter) are explicitly rejected: `quality` overscopes (correctness/completeness/freshness/contradiction-resolution); `evidence` is ambiguous (M28/M29/M30/M27 all use "evidence" elsewhere); an `--by` axis flag would couple multiple aggregation modes and violate the M27/M30/M31/M32/M33/M34/M35 single-aggregation-axis precedent; extending `tusq review` would conflate per-capability filter with per-bucket roll-up. Eval regression scenario `confidence-tier-index-determinism` brings the harness from 26 → **≥27** scenarios. Constraint 29 (proposed) codifies the planning-aid framing and forbids "runtime confidence enforcement / evidence-quality scoring engine / automated re-classification / alteration of scanner `confidence` derivation rules / persistence of `confidence_tier` into the manifest / cross-axis statistical aggregation" framings in docs/README/CLI-help. Six Key Risk rows added (misread as runtime gate / quality engine / re-classifier; silent threshold drift on `0.85`/`0.6`; silent enum drift on the four-value `confidence_tier` OR two-value `aggregation_key`; manifest mutation through index generation; `--out` path traversal into `.tusq/`; closed-enum order mistaken as quality-precedence + case-folding drift on `--tier`). Deferred successor milestones (M-Risk-1 cross-axis risk tier, M-Confidence-Statistics-1 distribution roll-up with `min`/`max`/`mean`/percentiles/histograms, M-Confidence-Persistence-1 if persistence into the manifest is later authorized) ship under their own ROADMAP entries with fresh acceptance contracts. M35 is substantively shipped at V1.16. The substantive 19 bullets (CLI noun/subcommand, command implementation, aggregation_key enum, default behavior, per-bucket entry shape, read-only invariants, deterministic output, empty-capabilities exit-0 rule, I/O stream discipline, --help framing, --out path rules, tusq help insertion, smoke matrix, eval regression scenario, Constraint 28, SYSTEM_SPEC § M35, two website docs, npm test continues to exit 0) are all genuinely shipped (`auth` is the 9th alphabetic command between `approve` and `diff` — note: `diff` (`d`) sorts before `compile` (`c`) was a typo in the original charter; the actual current alphabetic placement is `approve → auth → diff` and is correct). **Dev-implementation directive for this run:** close line 629 by (a) deriving `AUTH_SCHEME_INDEX_BUCKET_ORDER` from `AUTH_SCHEMES` (e.g., `Object.freeze(AUTH_SCHEMES.filter((s) => s !== 'unknown'))` or equivalent that puts the named six in `bearer → api_key → session → basic → oauth → none` order), AND (b) adding a synchronous module-init guard that throws if the named-six set + `unknown` ever diverges from `AUTH_SCHEMES`. The guard implementation is bounded (~10 lines), preserves all 26 eval scenarios as exit-0, preserves the 19-command CLI surface, preserves all per-bucket entry shape semantics, and preserves the closed-enum bucket iteration order. After dev closes line 629, qa re-verifies and launch closes V1.16. > **M35 Charter Bound — 2026-04-26 in run_0b373a30d182816a (turn_d7fc926d1c177c66, PM attempt 1) at HEAD `b129ca9`.** This turn binds **M35: Static Capability Auth Scheme Index Export from Manifest Evidence (~0.5 day) — V1.16 (PROPOSED)** as the next bounded roadmap increment, derived from the intake charter `intent_1777242416896_42c9` (vision_scan, category `roadmap_exhausted_vision_open`, charter "Derive next bounded roadmap increment from VISION.md. Candidate pool: The Promise, Code And API Surface, Database, Warehouse, And Data Model, Frontend, Design System, And Product UX, Domain Model And Workflows (+25 more). Current roadmap checked through M34: Static Capability HTTP Method Index Export from Manifest Evidence (~0.5 day) — V1.15 (PROPOSED)."). Challenged the charter explicitly rather than rubber-stamping: the charter correctly identifies that the roadmap is checked through M34 (V1.15 SHIPPED in run_bf8efb6b9c733000 across all four phases planning → implementation → qa → launch with `run_completion_request=true`, then re-affirmed in run_9b4197b36f01ca42 as a stale-checkbox cycle that was correctly absorbed by the prior PM/dev/qa/launch loop) and that the candidate pool from VISION.md still contains unbound material — particularly the **Auth, IAM, Permissions, And Tenant Boundaries** section (lines 56–64), whose "respect the same access rules" promise is operationally answered by a per-`auth_scheme` capability roll-up. The charter is honored by binding exactly one new bounded testable milestone (M35), not by re-running M34, not by leaving the roadmap idle, and not by binding multiple competing candidates in one turn. VISION sources cited: **`.planning/VISION.md` lines 56–64 (`### Auth, IAM, Permissions, And Tenant Boundaries`)** — explicitly within the charter's "+25 more" candidate pool; the section enumerates "user authentication, session boundaries, OAuth and OIDC scopes, generated MCP-server adapters, multi-tenant boundaries, role-based and attribute-based access control" and closes with "The generated AI layer must respect the same access rules the logged-in user would have inside the SaaS portal." The per-`auth_scheme` index is the smallest reviewer-aid that lets an operator see, at a glance, "how many capabilities are behind no auth at all, how many are behind unknown auth, how many are bearer-token-protected" — the central question that operationalizes the section's "respect the same access rules" promise. Plus **`.planning/VISION.md` lines 689–697 (`### Capability Overexposure` under § Risks)** — surfacing per-bucket cross-axis flags `has_destructive_side_effect` and `has_restricted_or_confidential_sensitivity` per auth bucket so reviewers can see if the `none` or `unknown` auth bucket contains destructive or restricted-sensitivity capabilities (the highest-attention combination). Shipped reality M1–M34 covers the compiler/governance half plus the M27 redaction-review reviewer-aid, the M30 surface-plan planner, the M31 per-domain index, the M32 per-side-effect-class index, the M33 per-sensitivity-class index, and the M34 per-HTTP-method index. The per-auth-scheme capability index — the parallel reviewer-aid that buckets capabilities by their `auth_requirements.auth_scheme` value (M29's frozen seven-value enum) — has not shipped. M29 produced the per-capability `auth_scheme` value and a `--auth-scheme` filter on the existing `tusq review` command, but does NOT aggregate capabilities into a per-scheme roll-up; reviewers asking "how many capabilities are in the `none` or `unknown` auth bucket" must currently re-run `tusq review --auth-scheme <value>` once per scheme and manually count. M35 is the smallest first increment that addresses the auth-scheme-visibility dimension of VISION § Auth, IAM, Permissions, And Tenant Boundaries **without** committing the project to runtime authentication enforcement, runtime AAA validation, OAuth/OIDC/SAML compliance certification, generated auth-adapter code, IAM-context derivation, or alteration of M29's `auth_scheme` derivation rules (M29 derives `auth_scheme` from middleware-name regex evidence; M35 buckets capabilities by the manifest's verbatim `auth_scheme` value and MUST NOT touch M29 rules). Scope decision resolved this turn: M35 introduces a new top-level noun `auth` with a single subcommand `index` (mirroring the M27 `redaction review`, M30 `surface plan`, M31 `domain index`, M32 `effect index`, M33 `sensitivity index`, and M34 `method index` precedents). The CLI surface grows from 18 → 19 commands with `auth` inserted alphabetically between `approve` and `compile` (`approve` vs `auth`: `app` < `aut` because `p` < `u`; `auth` vs `compile`: `a` < `c`). The mutually exclusive alternative forms (`tusq iam index`, `tusq scheme index`, `tusq capability index --by auth_scheme`, extending `tusq review --auth-scheme`) are explicitly rejected for V1.16: `iam` overscopes the milestone (IAM includes roles, scopes, tenancy, attributes — not just the auth-scheme dimension); `scheme` is ambiguous against unrelated uses (URL scheme in route field, schema fields from M24); an `--by` axis flag would couple multiple aggregation modes and violate the M27/M30/M31/M32/M33/M34 single-aggregation-axis precedent; extending `tusq review --auth-scheme` would conflate the per-capability filter (one capability per row) with the per-bucket roll-up (one bucket per row). The closed seven-value `auth_scheme` bucket-key enum (`bearer | api_key | session | basic | oauth | none | unknown`) aligns 1:1 with the existing M29 `AUTH_SCHEMES` constant in `src/cli.js` (`['unknown', 'bearer', 'api_key', 'session', 'basic', 'oauth', 'none']`) — note that `unknown` is already a member of M29 AUTH_SCHEMES (unlike M34 where `unknown` was a synthesized catchall outside the canonical five), so M35 has no separate "synthesized catchall" — the seven-value enum IS the bucket-key enum and IS the M29 AUTH_SCHEMES set; extending the bucket-key enum to additional values (e.g., `mtls`, `aws_sigv4`, `digest`, `hmac`, `webhook_signature`) would require a corresponding extension to M29 AUTH_SCHEMES, which is itself a material governance event under its own ROADMAP milestone with a fresh re-approval expectation. The closed two-value `aggregation_key` enum is `scheme | unknown` (parallel to M31 `domain | unknown`, M32 `class | unknown`, M33 `class | unknown`, M34 `method | unknown`). The frozen 8-field per-bucket entry shape (`auth_scheme`, `aggregation_key`, `capability_count`, `capabilities[]`, `approved_count`, `gated_count`, `has_destructive_side_effect`, `has_restricted_or_confidential_sensitivity`) is intentionally name-and-counters-only and intentionally **omits** cross-axis roll-up arrays (`domains_represented[]`, `auth_scopes_represented[]`, `auth_roles_represented[]`, `methods_represented[]`, `side_effect_classes_represented[]`, `sensitivity_classes_represented[]`) and **omits** any derived `risk_tier` or `iam_posture` — both reserved for the deferred M-Risk-1 / M-IAM-Posture-1 milestones with their own enums, their own acceptance contracts, and their own re-approval expectations. Bucket iteration order is the **closed-enum order** `bearer → api_key → session → basic → oauth → none → unknown` (NOT manifest first-appearance — M31's first-appearance rule applies to open-string `domain` values, not to closed enums; NOT IAM-strength-precedence — the closed-enum order is a deterministic stable-output convention only and MUST NOT be described as "strength-ordering," "trust-ranking," "security-ascending," or any phrase implying security semantics; the `unknown` bucket is appended last, mirroring M32/M33/M34). Within each bucket, capability names follow manifest declared order (mirroring M31/M32/M33/M34 within-bucket ordering). Empty buckets MUST NOT appear (a `bearer` bucket appears only if at least one capability has `auth_scheme === "bearer"`). Read-only invariants mirror M27/M28/M29/M30/M31/M32/M33/M34: zero manifest mutation, zero `capability_digest` flips, zero new dependency in `package.json`, byte-identical `tusq compile`/`tusq serve`/`tusq policy verify`/`tusq redaction review`/`tusq surface plan`/`tusq domain index`/`tusq effect index`/`tusq sensitivity index`/`tusq method index` output pre and post-M35. Empty-capabilities exits 0 with `No capabilities in manifest — nothing to index.` (human) and `{ manifest_path, manifest_version, generated_at, schemes: [] }` (`--json`); every error path empties stdout and writes exclusively to stderr. The `--out <path>` flag rejects any path resolving inside `.tusq/` (mirroring M30/M31/M32/M33/M34). The `--scheme <value>` filter limits output to a single bucket (string match against one of the seven enum values: `bearer`, `api_key`, `session`, `basic`, `oauth`, `none`, `unknown`); an unrecognized filter value exits 1 with `Unknown auth scheme:` followed by the value, empty stdout. The `--scheme` flag value matching is **case-sensitive** (lowercase only) — mirroring the manifest's verbatim lowercase `auth_scheme` field convention and the M29 AUTH_SCHEMES constant; uppercase values like `BEARER` or `bearer ` (with whitespace) exit 1 (rather than being lower-cased or trimmed silently) so reviewer scripts cannot accidentally drift from the canonical lowercase form. Eval regression scenario `auth-scheme-index-determinism` brings the harness from 25 → **≥26** scenarios. Constraint 28 (proposed) codifies the planning-aid framing and forbids "runtime authentication enforcement / AAA validation / OAuth/OIDC/SAML compliance certification / auth-adapter code generation / IAM-context derivation / alteration of M29 `auth_scheme` derivation rules / alteration of the M30 `gated_reason: auth_scheme_unknown` or `gated_reason: auth_scheme_oauth_pending_v2` surface-eligibility rules" framings in docs/README/CLI-help. Six Key Risk rows added (misread as runtime auth enforcer / AAA validator / compliance certifier; silent enum drift on `auth_scheme` bucket-key OR `aggregation_key`; manifest mutation through index generation; `--out` path traversal into `.tusq/`; closed-enum order mistaken as IAM-strength-precedence; case-folding drift on `--scheme` filter relative to manifest lowercase convention). The deferred successor milestones (M-IAM-Posture-1 cross-axis IAM-posture roll-up, M-Auth-Adapter-1 generated auth adapter, M-Runtime-Auth-1 runtime auth validator) for actual policy/runtime artifacts remain deferred — each ships under its own ROADMAP entry with a fresh acceptance contract. The MCP-descriptor candidate (the long-standing outstanding charter sketch in `.planning/ROADMAP_NEXT_CANDIDATES.md` § "MCP Server Static Descriptor Export") remains unbound this turn — the form-decision A/B/C blocker is unresolved and is reserved for a future PM turn. Independent baseline re-verified on HEAD `b129ca9`: `npm test` exits 0 with "Smoke tests passed" and "Eval regression harness passed (25 scenarios)"; the 18-command CLI surface (init, scan, manifest, compile, serve, review, docs, approve, diff, domain, effect, method, policy, redaction, sensitivity, surface, version, help) is intact (M35 is unchecked planned work, not shipped — the 19th command `auth` lands in implementation). The full SYSTEM_SPEC § M35 and command-surface § M35 detail blocks are owned by the dev role's implementation phase per the M27/M28/M29/M30/M31/M32/M33/M34 PM-vs-dev ownership split (PM charters; dev materializes the full spec/algorithm details before any code lands). M35 is implementation-ready planned work, not shipped. Did NOT modify `VISION.md` (operator-owned) or `ROADMAP_NEXT_CANDIDATES.md`. Phase transition to implementation requested under the run's auto_approve policy.

The mutually exclusive alternative forms (`tusq verb index` with `verb` as the noun, `tusq http index` with a protocol-prefixed noun, `tusq capability index --by method` with an axis-flag) are explicitly rejected for V1.15: `verb` is ambiguous against grammatical use elsewhere in tusq help text; `http` would suggest broader HTTP-protocol scope (headers, status codes, content types) that this milestone explicitly does not address; an `--by` axis flag would couple multiple aggregation modes into one command and violate the M27/M30/M31/M32/M33 single-aggregation-axis precedent. ## Implementation Milestones

### M1: Docusaurus Project Setup (~0.5 day)
- [x] Initialize Docusaurus 3.x project in `website/` directory
- [x] Configure `docusaurus.config.ts` with site metadata, navbar, footer
- [x] Set up `package.json` with required dependencies
- [x] Configure TypeScript support
- [x] Verify `npm run build` and `npm start` work with default content

### M2: Brand & Theme (~0.5 day)
- [x] Migrate brand colors and fonts from `websites/styles.css` to `website/src/css/custom.css`
- [x] Configure Fraunces + Space Grotesk font loading
- [x] Set up custom color palette in Docusaurus theme config
- [x] Create or migrate any logo/favicon assets to `website/static/img/`

### M3: Homepage Component (~0.5 day)
- [x] Create custom homepage component at `website/src/pages/index.tsx`
- [x] Migrate hero section (eyebrow, headline, lede, CTA)
- [x] Migrate feature cards (What it does / ships / matters)
- [x] Migrate workflow steps section
- [x] Migrate V1 surface grid
- [x] Update CTAs to point to docs (Getting Started) instead of README.md

### M4: Documentation Pages (~1 day)
- [x] Create docs sidebar structure in `sidebars.ts`
- [x] Write Getting Started page (install + 6-command workflow)
- [x] Write CLI Reference page (all 8 commands, flags, exit codes)
- [x] Write Manifest Format page (capability fields, schema, examples)
- [x] Write Configuration page (tusq.config.json reference)
- [x] Write Supported Frameworks page (Express, Fastify, NestJS)
- [x] Write MCP Server page (describe-only behavior, tools/list, tools/call)
- [x] Write FAQ page (from MESSAGING.md claims/non-claims)

### M5: Blog Setup (~0.5 day)
- [x] Configure Docusaurus blog plugin (already built-in)
- [x] Adapt ANNOUNCEMENT.md into a blog post with proper frontmatter
- [x] Adapt RELEASE_NOTES.md into a blog post with proper frontmatter
- [x] Verify blog index and RSS feed generation

### M6: Navigation, 404, and Polish (~0.5 day)

- [x] Verify docs sidebar ordering and grouping

### M20: Opt-In Local Execution Policy Scaffold for MCP serve (~0.5 day)
- [x] Specify `.tusq/execution-policy.json` shape (`schema_version`, `mode: "describe-only" | "dry-run"`, optional `allowed_capabilities`) in SYSTEM_SPEC.md
- [x] Add `tusq serve --policy <path>` flag that activates dry-run validation mode; absent flag preserves V1 describe-only behavior byte-for-byte
- [x] Extend `tools/call` under `mode: "dry-run"` to accept `params.arguments`, validate them against the approved compiled tool's `parameters` schema (required fields enforced, `additionalProperties` respected), and return a structured `dry_run_plan` object
- [x] `dry_run_plan` fields: `method`, `path`, `path_params`, `query`, `body`, `headers`, `auth_context`, `side_effect_class`, `sensitivity_class`, `redaction`, `plan_hash` (SHA-256 of canonical plan content), and `evaluated_at` (ISO-8601 UTC)
- [x] Emit JSON-RPC error `-32602` with `data.validation_errors` (array of `{path, reason}`) when argument validation fails; no plan is produced
- [x] Keep execution fully local/offline — no HTTP request, DB call, or network I/O to the target product under any policy mode
- [x] Policy resolution errors (missing file when `--policy` is set, invalid JSON, unknown `mode`, unsupported `schema_version`) exit 1 at serve startup with an actionable message
- [x] Add smoke coverage for policy-off (describe-only unchanged), policy-on dry-run success, validation failure paths, and plan_hash determinism
- [x] Add eval regression scenarios for dry-run plan structure, approval-gate enforcement (unapproved capabilities remain invisible to `tools/list` and reject in `tools/call`), and validation-error surfaces
- [x] Update CLI help, README, and website CLI-reference docs to describe the `--policy` flag and `.tusq/execution-policy.json` shape; add an `execution-policy.md` docs page

### M21: Execution Policy Scaffold Generator (~0.5 day)
- [x] Add `tusq policy init` command that scaffolds a valid `.tusq/execution-policy.json` with sensible defaults, so operators no longer hand-author the M20 policy file
- [x] Default output path is `.tusq/execution-policy.json`; parent directory created if missing; honor `--out <path>` to write elsewhere
- [x] Default `schema_version: "1.0"` and `mode: "describe-only"` (the safest possible V1.2 default — preserves describe-only behavior even when `tusq serve --policy` is invoked with the generated file)
- [x] Support `--mode <describe-only|dry-run>` to select the generated mode; any other value exits 1 with an actionable message before any file is written
- [x] Support `--reviewer <id>` with the same env-chain fallback used by `tusq approve` (`TUSQ_REVIEWER`, `USER`, `LOGNAME`, then literal `"unknown"`); the reviewer identity is written to the generated `reviewer` field
- [x] Stamp `approved_at` as the ISO-8601 UTC generation timestamp
- [x] Support `--allowed-capabilities <name,name,...>` to set an initial scope filter; omitting the flag leaves `allowed_capabilities` unset (meaning "all approved"); empty or whitespace-only list exits 1
- [x] Support `--force` to overwrite an existing target file; without `--force`, a pre-existing target exits 1 with `Policy file already exists:` and the path; `--dry-run` prints the would-be content to stdout without writing and without requiring `--force`
- [x] Support `--json` for a machine-readable confirmation (path, mode, reviewer, approved_at, allowed_capabilities) intended for automation
- [x] Keep the command fully local/offline — no network I/O, no target-product calls, no MCP handshake; file I/O only
- [x] The generated file MUST pass `loadAndValidatePolicy()` byte-for-byte so `tusq serve --policy <generated path>` succeeds without any further human edits
- [x] Add smoke coverage for default generation, `--mode dry-run`, `--allowed-capabilities`, `--force` overwrite vs exit-1 existing-file path, `--dry-run` no-write behavior, and a round-trip that loads the generated file through `loadAndValidatePolicy()`
- [x] Update CLI help, README, `website/docs/cli-reference.md`, and `website/docs/execution-policy.md` to describe the new `policy init` command and link it from the `tusq serve --policy` walkthrough

### M22: Execution Policy Verifier (~0.5 day)
- [x] Add `tusq policy verify` subcommand that runs the same `loadAndValidatePolicy()` as `tusq serve --policy` but without starting a server, so operators can gate CI and pre-commit hooks on policy validity
- [x] Default `--policy` target is `.tusq/execution-policy.json`; honor `--policy <path>` to validate a non-default file
- [x] Exit 0 on a policy that `loadAndValidatePolicy()` accepts; exit 1 on any validator rejection (missing file, bad JSON, unsupported `schema_version`, unknown `mode`, invalid `allowed_capabilities`)
- [x] Every failure message MUST be byte-for-byte identical to the message `tusq serve --policy` emits at startup for the same input; no wording divergence permitted
- [x] Default stdout summary on success: `Policy valid: <path> (mode: <mode>, reviewer: <reviewer>, allowed_capabilities: <count|unset>)`
- [x] Support `--json` for machine-readable output; on success emit `{valid:true, path, policy: {schema_version, mode, reviewer, approved_at, allowed_capabilities}}`; on failure emit `{valid:false, path, error}` to stdout and still exit 1
- [x] Support `--verbose` to echo the resolved path and validator diagnostics to stderr
- [x] Keep the command fully local/offline — no network I/O, no TCP bind, no MCP handshake, no target-product call, no manifest read in V1.3
- [x] Reuse the existing `loadAndValidatePolicy()` function from the M20 serve path; no standalone re-implementation of validation logic is permitted (the validator is the contract)
- [x] Add smoke coverage for: (a) successful verification of a default `tusq policy init` output, (b) exit-1 on missing file, malformed JSON, unsupported `schema_version`, unknown `mode`, and non-array `allowed_capabilities`, (c) `--json` success and failure shapes, (d) parity fixtures that confirm `tusq policy verify` and `tusq serve --policy` produce the same exit code and the same message for every failure case
- [x] Add one eval regression scenario asserting the round-trip `tusq policy init` → `tusq policy verify` is stable (generator/verifier/validator remain aligned)
- [x] Update CLI help, README, `website/docs/cli-reference.md`, and `website/docs/execution-policy.md` to describe the new `policy verify` subcommand and link it from both the `tusq policy init` and `tusq serve --policy` walkthroughs

### M23: Opt-In Strict Policy Verifier (Manifest-Aware) (~0.5 day)
- [x] Add `--strict` flag to the existing `tusq policy verify` subcommand that cross-references the policy file's `allowed_capabilities` against `tusq.manifest.json` in addition to the M22 policy-file validation
- [x] `--strict` is strictly opt-in; default `tusq policy verify` (no flag) MUST remain byte-for-byte identical to M22 behavior (no manifest I/O, no new failure modes, no inspection of the manifest file even when it exists at the default path)
- [x] Add `--manifest <path>` flag that is consulted ONLY when `--strict` is set; default manifest path is `tusq.manifest.json` in the current working directory
- [x] Under `--strict`, exit 1 with `Manifest not found:` followed by the path when the manifest file does not exist; M22 failure modes still apply first (policy-file validation is evaluated before any manifest I/O)
- [x] Under `--strict`, when `allowed_capabilities` is an array, every listed name MUST (a) exist as a capability in the manifest, (b) have `approved: true`, and (c) NOT have `review_needed: true`
- [x] Under `--strict`, when `allowed_capabilities` is unset (meaning "all approved"), strict mode MUST pass on the alignment check (unset is semantically broader-than-manifest and cannot name a non-existent capability)
- [x] Strict-mode failure messages: `Strict policy verify failed: allowed capability not found in manifest: <name>`; `Strict policy verify failed: allowed capability not approved: <name>`; `Strict policy verify failed: allowed capability requires review: <name>`; each message is emitted once per offending name in deterministic order
- [x] Strict-mode human summary on success: `Strict policy verify passed: <path> (manifest: <manifest-path>, allowed_capabilities: <count|unset>, approved: <count>)`
- [x] Strict-mode `--json` success shape extends the M22 shape with `{manifest_path, manifest_version, approved_allowed_capabilities}`; strict-mode `--json` failure shape extends the M22 shape with `{strict_errors: [{name, reason}]}`
- [x] Keep the command fully local/offline under `--strict` — `--strict` reads ONLY the policy file and the manifest file; no network I/O, no TCP bind, no MCP handshake, no target-product call, no execution of any capability
- [x] Strict mode does NOT validate manifest freshness (`previous_manifest_hash`, `manifest_version` chaining), does NOT verify schema-source quality, does NOT execute a dry-run plan — a PASS is strictly a policy/manifest alignment statement at verify time
- [x] Add smoke coverage for: (a) default `tusq policy verify` behavior is byte-for-byte identical to M22 (no manifest I/O) even when a manifest exists, (b) `--strict` exit 0 on a generated policy whose `allowed_capabilities` are approved in the manifest, (c) `--strict` exit 1 when an allowed capability is absent from the manifest, (d) `--strict` exit 1 when an allowed capability is present but unapproved, (e) `--strict` exit 1 when an allowed capability has `review_needed: true`, (f) `--strict` exit 1 when the manifest file is missing, (g) `--strict --json` success and failure shapes, (h) `--strict` with `allowed_capabilities` unset passes on a populated manifest, (i) `--strict` exit 1 when the manifest file is malformed JSON, (j) `--manifest` supplied without `--strict` exits 1 with `--manifest requires --strict` before any file is read, (k) M22 parity under `--strict`: every existing M22 failure fixture still produces byte-identical messages under `tusq policy verify` with and without `--strict` (strict check never runs when M22 validation fails first)
- [x] Add one eval regression scenario asserting that `tusq policy verify --strict` produces deterministic strict_errors ordering across repeated runs on the same fixture
- [x] Update CLI help, README, `website/docs/cli-reference.md`, and `website/docs/execution-policy.md` to describe the new `--strict` flag, the `--manifest` flag, the strict-mode failure cases, and the explicit narrative that a PASS is a least-privilege alignment statement, not a runtime execution safety guarantee

### M24: Opt-In Fastify Schema Body-Field Extraction (~0.5 day)
- [x] Extend the Fastify route extractor in `src/cli.js` (`extractFastifyRoutes`) to detect a literal `schema: { body: {...} }` options object on a route registration and capture a structured `schema_fields` record on the extracted route alongside the existing boolean `schema_hint`
- [x] `schema_fields.body` captures top-level `properties` (object keyed by field name, values carrying at least `{type}` for `string|number|integer|boolean|object|array`) and `required` (array of field names) as they appear literally in the source; nested property descent below one level is explicitly out of scope for V1.5
- [x] Extraction uses the existing regex + balanced-brace approach; when the `schema` block is not a literal object, when `body` is absent, when any brace is unbalanced, or when any property entry is non-literal, the extractor MUST fall back to emitting NO `schema_fields` (current M15 behavior preserved byte-for-byte)
- [x] `finalizeRouteInference()` and `buildInputSchema()` MUST merge captured `schema_fields.body.properties` into `input_schema.properties` and `schema_fields.body.required` into `input_schema.required`; when a field name collides with an M15-extracted path parameter, the path parameter wins (path params are authoritative, schema body augments)
- [x] When `schema_fields` is captured, `input_schema.additionalProperties` flips from the current permissive `true` to `false` so that downstream agents know the body shape is authoritative; when `schema_fields` is absent, M15 behavior is preserved byte-for-byte (no flip)
- [x] `source` metadata on `input_schema` MUST record the provenance tag `fastify_schema_body` when the extraction succeeded (alongside or in place of the existing `framework_schema_hint` / `request_body` tags) so reviewers can distinguish validator-extracted shape from heuristic shape
- [x] Scanner behavior for Express and NestJS extractors MUST remain byte-for-byte identical — M24 is a Fastify-only increment; Express-validator / Joi / Zod / class-validator inference is explicitly V2 scope
- [x] The three-field confidence model preserves the existing `schema_hint` boolean; `schema_fields` presence is a stronger signal and MUST add an additional +0.04 confidence on top of the existing +0.14 schema-hint bump (capped at 0.95); no other scoring branches change
- [x] Manifest output for routes without a Fastify schema block MUST be byte-for-byte identical to HEAD `35b7c9c`; a smoke test asserts this invariant against the existing `tests/fixtures/express-sample` and `tests/fixtures/nest-sample` manifests
- [x] Scanner and manifest generation remain fully local/offline — no network I/O, no library import of `fastify` or any validator framework, no evaluation of source code; the extractor reads files only via the existing `fs.readFile` loop
- [x] Deterministic parse: running `tusq scan` + `tusq manifest` twice on the same repo MUST produce byte-identical `input_schema.properties` ordering; property key order is source-literal (preserve declaration order), not alphabetized
- [x] Add smoke coverage for: (a) Fastify route with a `schema.body` block containing `properties` and `required` produces an `input_schema` with the declared fields merged in and `additionalProperties: false`; (b) Fastify route with `schema` present but no `body` key produces byte-identical output to HEAD `35b7c9c`; (c) Fastify route with a non-literal `schema` expression (e.g. `schema: sharedSchema`) produces byte-identical output to HEAD `35b7c9c`; (d) Fastify route combining a body schema and a path parameter surfaces both in `input_schema.properties` with the path param winning on name collision; (e) Express and NestJS fixtures produce byte-identical manifests before and after M24 implementation; (f) repeated manifest generations produce byte-identical property ordering; (g) `source` metadata tags a schema-body-derived shape as `fastify_schema_body`
- [x] Add one eval regression scenario asserting that a Fastify fixture with a body schema produces an `input_schema` with expected `properties` keys in declaration order and `additionalProperties: false`, and that the scenario is deterministic across three repeated runs
- [x] Update CLI help (no surface change — but `tusq help` text and `website/docs/manifest-format.md` MUST document the `fastify_schema_body` source tag and the `additionalProperties: false` flip) and `website/docs/frameworks.md` (add a "Fastify schema-body extraction (opt-in, static)" subsection describing the extraction rules, the fall-back semantics, and the explicit V1.5 boundary that only Fastify schemas and only the `body` key under the schema are consulted)

### M25: Static PII Field-Name Redaction Hints (~0.5 day)
- [x] Extend manifest generation in `src/cli.js` so that every generated capability populates `capability.redaction.pii_fields` by statically matching `input_schema.properties` keys against a fixed canonical set of well-known PII field names; no value inspection, no AST parsing, no regex over source code
- [x] Implement a pure helper function (e.g., `extractPiiFieldHints(properties)`) that accepts the `input_schema.properties` object and returns an array of original-case field names whose **normalized** form (`toLowerCase()` then strip `_` and `-`) matches the canonical PII set; the returned array preserves the iteration order of `input_schema.properties` (source-literal declaration order established under M15/M24)
- [x] The canonical PII set is explicitly enumerated in `src/cli.js` as a hard-coded frozen set; V1.6 covers: `email`, `emailaddress`, `useremail`; `phone`, `phonenumber`, `mobile`, `mobilephone`, `telephone`; `ssn`, `socialsecuritynumber`, `taxid`, `nationalid`; `firstname`, `lastname`, `fullname`, `middlename`; `streetaddress`, `zipcode`, `postalcode`; `dateofbirth`, `dob`, `birthdate`; `creditcard`, `cardnumber`, `cvv`, `cvc`, `bankaccount`, `iban`; `password`, `passphrase`, `apikey`, `accesstoken`, `refreshtoken`, `authtoken`, `secret`; `ipaddress`
- [x] Matching is whole-key only on normalized form: a field named `email_template_id` MUST NOT match `email`; a field named `user_email` MUST match because its normalized form is `useremail`; the match is case-insensitive and underscore/hyphen-insensitive
- [x] Populate `capability.redaction.pii_fields` with the extractor's return value; when no keys match, `pii_fields` MUST be `[]` (byte-identical to M12/M24 default behavior); other `redaction` fields (`log_level`, `mask_in_traces`, `retention_days`) MUST remain `null` in V1.6 (no auto-population under M25)
- [x] `capability.sensitivity_class` MUST NOT be auto-escalated under M25; it stays `"unknown"` until an explicit V2 sensitivity-inference increment is shipped (auto-escalating on PII match would overclaim and create silent governance drift)
- [x] `extractPiiFieldHints` applies uniformly to every capability regardless of source framework (Express, Fastify, NestJS) — the hint is derived from `input_schema.properties`, which is already normalized across frameworks by M15/M24
- [x] Scanner and manifest generation remain fully local/offline — no network I/O, no library import for PII detection (no `pii-detector`, no `presidio`, no regex library), no evaluation of source code, no data-dictionary fetch; the extractor is a pure in-memory function over an already-built `input_schema.properties` object
- [x] Deterministic output: `redaction.pii_fields` order is the iteration order of `input_schema.properties` (source-literal declaration order); repeated `tusq scan` + `tusq manifest` runs on the same repo MUST produce byte-identical `pii_fields` arrays; no alphabetization, no randomization
- [x] Manifest output for capabilities whose `input_schema.properties` contains no canonical PII keys MUST be byte-for-byte identical to HEAD `541abcd`; eval scenario and smoke test assert this invariant against the pii-hint-sample fixture (GET /catalog, no body) and the Express fixture (all capabilities produce pii_fields: [])
- [x] An M25-driven `capability.redaction.pii_fields` change flips the per-capability `capability_digest` (M13 already hashes `redaction` into the digest); the M13 approval-gate semantics propagate verbatim — a reviewer MUST explicitly re-approve the capability for it to re-appear in `tools/list`, preserving the governance boundary

### M26: Static PII Category Labels for Redaction Hints (~0.5 day)
- [x] Extend manifest generation in `src/cli.js` so that every generated capability populates `capability.redaction.pii_categories` by labeling each entry of the M25 `pii_fields` array with its canonical PII category; the array has the same length and same order as `pii_fields`; no value inspection, no new source-text scanning, no new dependency
- [x] Add a `PII_CATEGORY_BY_NAME` frozen lookup object in `src/cli.js` mapping every normalized entry in the M25 `PII_CANONICAL_NAMES` set to exactly one of nine category keys: `"email"`, `"phone"`, `"government_id"`, `"name"`, `"address"`, `"date_of_birth"`, `"payment"`, `"secrets"`, `"network"` — the mapping is total and disjoint; M25 and M26 freeze together
- [x] Implement a pure helper function (e.g., `extractPiiFieldCategories(piiFields)`) that accepts the M25-emitted `redaction.pii_fields` array and returns a parallel categories array; iteration is in `pii_fields` order; lookup uses the same normalization rule as M25 (`toLowerCase()` + strip `_`/`-`); throws synchronously if a `pii_fields` entry does not map to a known category (defensive guard against M25/M26 set drift)
- [x] Populate `capability.redaction.pii_categories` with the extractor's return value on every capability; when `pii_fields` is empty, `pii_categories` MUST be `[]` (never absent); other `redaction` fields (`log_level`, `mask_in_traces`, `retention_days`) MUST not be derived from categories and keep existing defaults (`"full"`, `false`, `null`) unless explicitly edited by a reviewer
- [x] `capability.sensitivity_class` MUST NOT be auto-escalated under M26; Constraint 16 propagates verbatim (stays `"unknown"` until an explicit V2 increment)
- [x] `scoreConfidence()` MUST NOT be modified — category presence is a redaction signal, not a confidence signal
- [x] `extractPiiFieldCategories` applies uniformly to every capability regardless of source framework (Express, Fastify, NestJS) — the extractor runs wherever `extractPiiFieldHints` already runs
- [x] Scanner and manifest generation remain fully local/offline — no network I/O, no retention-policy file fetch, no library import for category or retention inference (no `pii-detector`, no `presidio`, no compliance library); the extractor is a pure in-memory function over M25's `pii_fields` array plus the frozen lookup
- [x] Deterministic output: `pii_categories` order equals `pii_fields` order (source-literal declaration order from M15/M24/M25); repeated runs MUST produce byte-identical arrays
- [x] Every capability sees a one-time `capability_digest` flip on the first post-M26 scan (both non-PII capabilities that gain `pii_categories: []` and PII capabilities that gain a populated array); M13 approval-gate semantics propagate verbatim — reviewers MUST re-approve affected capabilities via `tusq approve` for them to re-appear in `tools/list`; RELEASE_NOTES MUST document the broad re-approval implication before M26 is consumed downstream
- [x] Add smoke coverage for: (a) Fastify fixture route with `pii_fields: ["email", "password"]` produces `pii_categories: ["email", "secrets"]` in the same order; (b) case/underscore/hyphen variants of a category-triggering name produce the correct category (`user_email` → `"email"`, `USER_EMAIL` → `"email"`); (c) capability with `pii_fields: []` produces `pii_categories: []` (array, never absent); (d) mixed-category fixture (e.g., `email` + `ssn` + `credit_card`) produces `pii_categories: ["email", "government_id", "payment"]`; (e) Express and NestJS fixtures emit `pii_categories` alongside `pii_fields` with matching length and order; (f) repeated manifest generations produce byte-identical `pii_categories` ordering; (g) `sensitivity_class` stays `"unknown"` on every capability; (h) `retention_days`, `log_level`, `mask_in_traces` keep existing defaults (`null`, `"full"`, `false`) on every capability; (i) `tusq policy verify --strict` is unchanged by M26
- [x] Add one eval regression scenario (`pii-category-label-determinism`) asserting that a fixture exercising multiple PII categories produces the expected `pii_categories` array in declaration order and that the scenario is deterministic across three repeated runs; total eval scenarios becomes **9**
- [x] Update CLI help (no surface change — `tusq help` text remains identical) and `website/docs/manifest-format.md` (extend the M25 "PII Field-Name Redaction Hints" subsection with the V1.7 category mapping table, the one-to-one correspondence rule with `pii_fields`, the empty-array behavior when `pii_fields` is empty, the no-auto-population rule for `retention_days`/`log_level`/`mask_in_traces`, the no-auto-escalation rule for `sensitivity_class`, and the Constraint 18 framing boundary). `README.md` already mentions `redaction.pii_fields` in the manifest surface description; add one line for `redaction.pii_categories`.

### M27: Reviewer-Facing PII Redaction Review Report (~0.5 day)
- [x] Add a new CLI noun `redaction` with exactly one subcommand, `tusq redaction review`, that reads the local `tusq.manifest.json` and emits a deterministic, per-capability reviewer-facing summary of the M25 `redaction.pii_fields` and M26 `redaction.pii_categories` arrays alongside a frozen per-category advisory text
- [x] Default `--manifest` path is `tusq.manifest.json` in the current working directory; `--manifest <path>` overrides; a missing manifest file exits 1 with `Manifest not found:` followed by the resolved path before any output is written
- [x] A malformed manifest (JSON parse error, missing top-level `capabilities` array) exits 1 with an actionable error message and does NOT emit a partial review report
- [x] Add a `PII_REVIEW_ADVISORY_BY_CATEGORY` frozen lookup object in `src/cli.js` mapping every one of the nine M26 category keys (`email`, `phone`, `government_id`, `name`, `address`, `date_of_birth`, `payment`, `secrets`, `network`) to exactly one single-line reviewer-advisory string; the mapping is total and disjoint; any addition or wording change is a material governance event that MUST land under its own ROADMAP milestone
- [x] Implement a pure helper function (e.g., `buildRedactionReviewReport(manifest, options)`) that accepts the parsed manifest and a filter option bag and returns a deterministic in-memory report structure; iteration order is capabilities in the manifest's declared `capabilities` array order, and within each capability `pii_fields`/`pii_categories` arrays in their existing parallel order; zero hashing of manifest content; zero side effects
- [x] Human-readable default output: one section per capability listing `name`, `approved` status, `sensitivity_class` (unchanged from manifest), a `Redaction:` sub-block listing `pii_fields`, `pii_categories`, and the mapped frozen advisory string for each category (once per distinct category per capability, in category-appearance order); capabilities with `pii_fields: []` display a single-line "No canonical PII field-name matches — reviewer action: none required from M27" entry; the output is plain text only (no ANSI escapes) so operators piping to file get byte-identical text
- [x] `--json` output: emits `{manifest_path, manifest_version, generated_at, capabilities: [{name, approved, sensitivity_class, pii_fields, pii_categories, advisories: [{category, text}]}]}`; advisories within a capability appear once per distinct category in category-appearance order; repeated runs produce byte-identical JSON (no wall-clock timestamps inside per-capability entries; `generated_at` is a single top-level ISO-8601 UTC field reused from the manifest's own `generated_at`, not a fresh re-stamp, so the output is content-deterministic for the same manifest input)
- [x] `--capability <name>` filters the report to a single capability; an unknown name exits 1 with `Capability not found:` followed by the name; the filter MUST NOT partial-match; zero output precedes the error
- [x] `--help` prints the M27 command shape, flag list, exit codes, and an explicit "This is a reviewer aid, not a runtime enforcement gate" callout; help text is byte-identical to the `tusq redaction review --help` output across runs
- [x] Keep the command fully local/offline — no network I/O, no TCP bind, no MCP handshake, no target-product call, no manifest write, no `src/` scan, no capability execution; the command reads only the manifest file path and writes only to stdout/stderr
- [x] MUST NOT mutate `tusq.manifest.json` under any flag combination; MUST NOT touch `.tusq/execution-policy.json`, `tusq-tools/*.json`, `.tusq/scan.json`, `redaction.retention_days`, `redaction.log_level`, `redaction.mask_in_traces`, or `sensitivity_class`; MUST NOT change the behavior of `tusq scan`, `tusq manifest`, `tusq compile`, `tusq serve`, `tusq approve`, `tusq diff`, `tusq docs`, or `tusq policy verify` (strict or default)
- [x] Every capability in the manifest contributes exactly one section to the report, including unapproved capabilities and capabilities with `review_needed: true`; M27 is read-only and never filters by approval state (reviewers need to see everything, especially the unapproved items)
- [x] Deterministic output: running `tusq redaction review` twice on the same manifest MUST produce byte-identical stdout (human and `--json` modes); repeated runs MUST NOT introduce any wall-clock field inside per-capability entries; top-level `generated_at` is sourced from the manifest's own `generated_at` field (not re-stamped)
- [x] Update `tusq help` to add the `redaction` noun and the `review` subcommand exactly once; `tusq redaction` (no subcommand) prints a short enumerate-subcommands block identical in shape to `tusq policy`; unknown subcommands exit 1 with `Unknown subcommand:` followed by the name
- [x] Add smoke coverage for: (a) default review on a manifest with M25/M26 PII capabilities produces exit 0 and the expected per-category advisory lines; (b) `--json` round-trips through JSON.parse and preserves capability/advisory order; (c) `--capability <name>` filters to one capability on success; (d) `--capability <unknown>` exits 1; (e) missing manifest exits 1 with `Manifest not found:`; (f) malformed-JSON manifest exits 1 before any stdout; (g) running twice on the same manifest produces byte-identical stdout in both modes; (h) M27 does not mutate the manifest file (file mtime and content are unchanged after a review run); (i) `sensitivity_class` in the report equals the manifest's `sensitivity_class` verbatim (no escalation); (j) capabilities with `pii_fields: []` render the "no canonical PII field-name matches" line; (k) mixed-category capability (e.g., `email` + `credit_card` + `ssn`) renders three distinct advisory lines in category-appearance order
- [x] Add one eval regression scenario (`redaction-review-determinism`) asserting that running `tusq redaction review --json` three times on the same manifest produces byte-identical stdout and that the advisory-text ordering matches `pii_categories` appearance order; total eval scenarios become **10**
- [x] Empty-manifest handling: when `capabilities` is a valid-but-empty array (`capabilities: []`), the command MUST exit 0 in both default and `--json` modes; human output emits a single explicit line `No capabilities in manifest — nothing to review.` to stdout (no section, no advisory rows, no warnings); `--json` output emits `{manifest_path, manifest_version, generated_at, capabilities: []}` with the top-level fields still copied verbatim from the manifest; this is distinct from a malformed/missing `capabilities` array (exit 1) and MUST NOT be silently conflated with that error path
- [x] I/O stream discipline: every error message path (`Manifest not found:`, `Invalid manifest JSON:`, `Invalid manifest: missing capabilities array`, `Capability not found:`, `Unknown subcommand:`, `Unknown flag:`) writes exclusively to stderr; stdout MUST be empty on every exit-1 path (no partial report, no JSON object with an `error` field, no trailing newline) so operators who pipe stdout to a file get a zero-byte output file when the command fails; a smoke assertion captures both streams and verifies `stdout === ""` on every error case
- [x] Optional top-level manifest field fallback: when the input manifest lacks `manifest_version` (or `generated_at`), the report still emits the field with value `null` (not `undefined`, not omitted) in `--json` mode and with the literal string `unknown` in human mode; this matches the existing manifest shape for older fixtures that predate M13 and prevents implementation drift into "skip the field" or "re-stamp with current wall-clock time" — both of which would break the content-deterministic invariant
- [x] Advisory byte-exact invariant: the frozen `PII_REVIEW_ADVISORY_BY_CATEGORY` wording uses the em-dash character (U+2014) in every entry as shown in SYSTEM_SPEC § M27; any transliteration to ASCII hyphen-minus (U+002D), en-dash (U+2013), or a different punctuation character is a material governance event that MUST land under its own ROADMAP milestone with a RELEASE_NOTES entry; the smoke fixture locks the exact byte sequence of each advisory string at merge time and stdout is UTF-8-encoded
- [x] Update CLI help, README, `website/docs/cli-reference.md`, and `website/docs/manifest-format.md` to describe the new `redaction review` subcommand, the frozen advisory set, the read-only-reviewer-aid framing, and the explicit narrative that a review report is NOT a runtime enforcement gate, NOT a compliance certification, and NOT a substitute for reviewer judgment

No source modification this turn.
- [x] Add `classifySensitivity(capability)` pure deterministic function in `src/cli.js` implementing the frozen six-rule first-match-wins decision table: R1 preserve→restricted, R2 admin/destructive verb or admin-namespaced route→restricted, R3 pii_categories non-empty→confidential, R4 write verb + financial-context route/param→confidential, R5 auth_required or narrow write→internal, R6 default→public

### M29: Static Auth Requirements Inference from Manifest Evidence (~0.5 day) — SHIPPED V1.10

> **Reconciliation note (turn_df1112d797428a6b, run_3c9aac455742ac3e, 2026-04-26):** All 17 sub-items below were flipped from `[ ]` → `[x]` because every one is verifiable against shipped code, docs, and tests on HEAD a6a3c744. > - `--auth-scheme` flag pre-check at `src/cli.js:812-817`, validation at `:849`, intersection with `--sensitivity` at `:886`, usage string at `:2220` (`Usage: tusq review [--format json] [--strict] [--sensitivity <class>] [--auth-scheme <scheme>]`).

> - SYSTEM_SPEC § M29 at `.planning/SYSTEM_SPEC.md:2954` with the seven-value enum, the six-rule decision table, scope/role extraction rules, zero-evidence guard invariant, byte-identity invariant, and non-attestation boundary.
> - Constraint 22 (reviewer-aid framing) present in SYSTEM_SPEC Constraints section (search "Constraint 22" in SYSTEM_SPEC.md).
> - Eval regression harness now totals 16 scenarios (`npm test` output: `Eval regression harness passed (16 scenarios)`); the M29-specific scenarios are present in `tests/evals/governed-cli-scenarios.json`.
> - `website/docs/manifest-format.md` and `website/docs/cli-reference.md` both reference `auth_requirements` / `--auth-scheme` (verified by grep).
> - `npm test` exits 0 on HEAD a6a3c744; no new dependency added (`passport`, `jsonwebtoken`, `oauth2-server` absent from `package.json`); 13-command CLI surface preserved exactly (`init, scan, manifest, compile, serve, review, docs, approve, diff, policy, redaction, version, help`).
> - **Caveat carried forward as QA OBJ-001 (medium, non-blocking):** R6 (`auth_required === false` → `auth_scheme: 'none'`) is dead code in the automated pipeline because the scanner never sets `auth_required: false`; the rule remains correct for manually edited manifests. This is a code-coverage observation, not a defect — no rule-table mutation is permitted under M29 (the table is immutable; any change is a fresh ROADMAP milestone).

- [x] Add `classifyAuthRequirements(capability)` pure deterministic function in `src/cli.js` that returns a structured `auth_requirements` record with the closed shape `{ auth_scheme, auth_scopes, auth_roles, evidence_source }`. `auth_scheme` is one of the closed seven-value enum `{bearer, api_key, session, basic, oauth, none, unknown}` — no other value, no nullable. `evidence_source` is one of the closed five-value enum `{middleware_name, route_prefix, auth_required_flag, sensitivity_class_propagation, none}`.
- [x] Implement the frozen six-rule first-match-wins `auth_scheme` decision table: R1 middleware_name matches `/bearer|jwt|access[_-]?token/i` → `bearer`; R2 middleware_name matches `/api[_-]?key|x-api-key/i` → `api_key`; R3 middleware_name matches `/session|cookie|passport-local/i` → `session`; R4 middleware_name matches `/basic[_-]?auth/i` → `basic`; R5 middleware_name matches `/oauth|oidc|openid/i` → `oauth`; R6 `auth_required === false` AND no admin/restricted route prefix → `none`; default (no evidence) → `unknown`. The decision table is immutable once M29 ships; any rule change is a material governance event under its own ROADMAP milestone.
- [x] Implement the frozen scope/role extraction rules: scopes are extracted from middleware-annotation literals matching `/scopes?:\s*\[([^\]]+)\]/` over the capability's source-literal middleware list; roles are extracted from `/role[s]?:\s*\[([^\]]+)\]/` over the same surface. Both arrays MUST preserve declaration order, MUST be deduplicated case-sensitively, and MUST be empty arrays (never null, never absent) when zero matches are found. The extractor reads only the already-built capability record fields — no regex over arbitrary source files.
- [x] Capabilities with zero static evidence (no middleware names, no route prefix, no `auth_required` flag, no `sensitivity_class` signal) MUST receive `auth_requirements: { auth_scheme: "unknown", auth_scopes: [], auth_roles: [], evidence_source: "none" }` — never silently default to `"none"`. The zero-evidence guard is the first check in `classifyAuthRequirements` before the rule table runs.
- [x] `auth_requirements` is included in the content fields hashed into `capability_digest` (M13). When `auth_requirements` changes (any field including `auth_scopes`/`auth_roles` array contents), `capability_digest` flips and `approved` resets to `false`; re-approval is required via `tusq approve`. The diff queue under `tusq diff` surfaces the `auth_requirements` change as a non-empty review queue entry.
- [x] Update `tusq review` to display `auth_requirements` per capability and accept an optional `--auth-scheme <scheme>` filter that limits output to capabilities matching the specified scheme. Unrecognized filter values exit 1 with empty stdout before any output (matching M28's `--sensitivity` validation pattern). The filter is mutually compatible with `--sensitivity` (both can be set in one invocation; they intersect AND-style).
- [x] Update `tusq docs` to include `auth_requirements` in each per-capability section.
- [x] Verify `tusq diff` surfaces `auth_requirements` changes (no diff-command change required if the digest flips, but assert the diff queue is non-empty on a controlled scope addition).
- [x] `tusq compile` output MUST be byte-identical regardless of `auth_requirements` value — golden-file smoke assertion compares compiled tool output for two capabilities identical except for `auth_requirements`.
- [x] `tusq approve` gate logic MUST remain unchanged. `tusq serve` MCP surface (`tools/list`, `tools/call`, `dry_run_plan`) MUST be unchanged — `auth_requirements` MUST NOT appear in any serve response shape. `tusq policy verify` (default and `--strict`) and `tusq redaction review` MUST be unchanged.
- [x] Add 8-case smoke matrix (AC-8): (1) middleware_name="requireBearerToken" → `bearer`; (2) middleware_name="checkApiKey" → `api_key`; (3) middleware_name="sessionGuard" → `session`; (4) middleware_name="basicAuth" → `basic`; (5) middleware_name="oauthMiddleware" → `oauth`; (6) `auth_required=false`, route=/public/health → `none`; (7) middleware annotation declares `scopes:["read:user","write:user"]` → `auth_scopes` preserves order and dedupes; (8) zero-evidence empty record → `unknown` with empty arrays.
- [x] Add ≥3 new top-level eval regression scenarios to `tests/evals/governed-cli-scenarios.json`: (1) bearer-token middleware detection precedence over generic `auth_required`; (2) scopes-array extraction with mixed-order declaration verifying preserved order and deduplication; (3) zero-evidence `unknown` bucket with empty `auth_scopes`/`auth_roles` arrays. Total eval scenarios become **≥16**.
- [x] Add Constraint 22 to SYSTEM_SPEC.md Constraints section: "auth_requirements is reviewer-aid framing forbidding runtime-AAA-enforcement, automated-AAA-certification, and OAuth/OIDC/SAML/SOC2 compliance attestation framing."
- [x] Add M29 section to SYSTEM_SPEC.md with the verbatim seven-value enum, the frozen six-rule decision table, the frozen scope/role extraction rules, the zero-evidence unknown bucket invariant, the AC-7 compile byte-identity invariant, and the explicit non-attestation boundary: "auth_requirements is reviewer-aid framing only. tusq does not authenticate or authorize requests at runtime, does not certify SOC2/ISO27001/OAuth2/OIDC/SAML compliance, and does not validate token signatures or scope grants."
