### M30: Static Embeddable-Surface Plan Export from Manifest Evidence (~0.75 day) — V1.11 (PROPOSED)

> **Charter origin (run_24ccd92f593d8647, turn_33f4e15b33cf141c, PM, HEAD 307bdfd, 2026-04-26):** This milestone binds the long-pending vision-derived candidate "Static Embeddable-Surface Plan Export" (previously housed in `.planning/ROADMAP_NEXT_CANDIDATES.md` § "Vision-Derived Charter Candidate: Static Embeddable-Surface Plan Export (V2 First Step)") into a frozen ROADMAP entry. VISION source: `.planning/VISION.md` line 27 ("embeddable chat, widget, command-palette, and voice surfaces" under **The Promise**); lines 193–224 (Brand-Matched Chat Interface, Brand-Matched Voice Interface, Embeddable Widgets And Command Surfaces). Shipped reality M1–M29 covers only the compiler/governance half — none of the four embeddable surfaces have any implementation today. M30 is the smallest first increment that addresses the vision goal **without** committing the project to runtime chat/voice/widget rendering. Scope decision resolved this turn: M30 introduces a new top-level noun `surface` with a single subcommand `plan` (mirroring the M27 `redaction review` precedent). The CLI surface grows from 13 → 14 commands. The mutually exclusive alternative form `tusq plan surface` under a future planning hub is explicitly rejected for V1.11; a future planning hub may subsume `surface plan` later under its own ROADMAP milestone if and when it is chartered.

- [x] Add new top-level noun `surface` with single subcommand `plan` to the CLI surface; `tusq surface` (no subcommand) prints a short enumerate-subcommands block identical in shape to `tusq policy` and `tusq redaction`; unknown subcommands exit 1 with `Unknown subcommand:` followed by the name and empty stdout. CLI surface grows from 13 commands to **14** (init, scan, manifest, compile, serve, review, docs, approve, diff, policy, redaction, surface, version, help).
- [x] Implement `tusq surface plan` as a pure read-only deterministic command that reads the manifest path and writes only to stdout/stderr (or to `--out <path>` if supplied); no network I/O, no `.tusq/` write, no manifest mutation, no `tusq compile`/`tusq serve`/`tusq policy verify`/`tusq redaction review` behavior change.
- [x] Add the frozen four-value `surface` enum: `chat | palette | widget | voice`. The enum is immutable once M30 ships; any addition (e.g., `email`, `slack-bot`) is a material governance event under its own ROADMAP milestone with a fresh re-approval expectation. The `--surface <chat|palette|widget|voice|all>` flag accepts only these five tokens (the four enum values plus `all`); any other token exits 1 with `Unknown surface:` followed by the value, empty stdout.
- [x] Default behavior: `tusq surface plan` (no `--surface`) is equivalent to `--surface all` and emits one plan section per surface in the frozen order `chat → palette → widget → voice` (deterministic, never sorted by capability count or any wall-clock value).
- [x] Per-surface plan shape (deterministic JSON under `--json`):
  - `surface`: one of the four enum values (string)
  - `eligible_capabilities[]`: capability names (strings) whose `approved === true` AND whose per-surface eligibility rule passes; iteration order is the manifest's `capabilities[]` declared order
  - `gated_capabilities[]`: array of `{ name, reason }` objects for every capability in the manifest excluded from this surface; `reason` is one of the closed six-value enum below; iteration order is manifest declared order
  - `entry_points`: per-surface keyed object derived deterministically from M9 domain + verb data (chat → `{ intents: [{ capability, intent_label }] }`; palette → `{ actions: [{ capability, action_label }] }`; widget → `{ action_widgets: [{ capability }], insight_widgets: [{ capability }] }` split by side-effect class; voice → `{ voice_intents: [{ capability, intent_label }] }` constrained to non-destructive read/update verbs)
  - `redaction_posture`: per eligible capability, copy-forward of the M27 advisory set (verbatim, no recomputation, no new advisory text)
  - `auth_posture`: per eligible capability, copy-forward of the M29 `auth_requirements` record (verbatim; no recoercion of `unknown` → `none`)
  - `brand_inputs_required[]`: frozen named-list per surface (chat: `["brand.tone","brand.color_primary","brand.color_secondary","brand.font_family"]`; palette: `["brand.color_primary","brand.font_family"]`; widget: `["brand.color_primary","brand.color_accent","brand.layout_density","brand.radius"]`; voice: `["brand.tone","voice.persona","voice.greeting"]`); names only, no values, no template strings, no placeholder lookups against any brand profile file
  - top-level `manifest_path`, `manifest_version`, `generated_at` copied verbatim from the input manifest (with the M27 fallback: `null` in `--json` mode and `unknown` in human mode when the manifest lacks the field)
- [x] Closed six-value gating-reason enum: `unapproved | restricted_sensitivity | confidential_sensitivity | destructive_side_effect | auth_scheme_unknown | auth_scheme_oauth_pending_v2`. The enum is immutable once M30 ships; any addition is a material governance event under its own ROADMAP milestone. An implementation-time error (synchronous throw) MUST fire if `classifyGating(capability, surface)` ever returns a value outside this set.
- [x] Per-surface eligibility rules (frozen first-match-wins precedence; first reason that gates a capability for a surface is the recorded reason):
  - `chat`: `approved === true` AND `sensitivity_class ∈ {public, internal}` AND `auth_requirements.auth_scheme !== "unknown"` AND `auth_requirements.auth_scheme !== "oauth"` (oauth deferred to V2 runtime adapter); destructive side-effect verbs ARE allowed (chat surface supports confirmation flows)
  - `palette`: `approved === true` AND `sensitivity_class ∈ {public, internal}` AND `auth_requirements.auth_scheme !== "unknown"` AND `auth_requirements.auth_scheme !== "oauth"` AND side-effect class ≠ `destructive` (palette is the lowest-risk surface)
  - `widget`: `approved === true` AND `auth_requirements.auth_scheme !== "unknown"` AND `auth_requirements.auth_scheme !== "oauth"`; widget split is determined by side-effect class (`destructive`/`writes` → `action_widgets`; `read-only` → `insight_widgets`); confidential/restricted sensitivity is permitted for widgets because widgets are typically embedded inside the SaaS portal (same-session proxy semantics)
  - `voice`: `approved === true` AND `sensitivity_class ∈ {public, internal}` AND `auth_requirements.auth_scheme !== "unknown"` AND `auth_requirements.auth_scheme !== "oauth"` AND side-effect class ≠ `destructive` (voice surface bans destructive verbs in V1.11; voice destructive flows are reserved for a future V2 confirmation-flow milestone)
- [x] Read-only invariants (mirroring M27 Constraint 20 / M28 Constraint 21 / M29 Constraint 22):
  - `tusq.manifest.json` mtime/content unchanged after every `tusq surface plan` invocation (smoke assertion)
  - No write to `.tusq/`; no write to any path other than `--out <path>` when supplied (smoke assertion)
  - `capability_digest` MUST NOT flip on any capability (smoke assertion: hash before vs after is byte-identical)
  - `tusq compile` output is byte-identical pre and post-M30 for every fixture (golden-file smoke assertion)
  - `tusq serve` `tools/list` and `tools/call` and `dry_run_plan` responses are byte-identical pre and post-M30 (golden-file smoke assertion)
  - `tusq policy verify` (default and `--strict`) and `tusq redaction review` are byte-identical pre and post-M30
- [x] Deterministic output: running `tusq surface plan` twice on the same manifest MUST produce byte-identical stdout in both human and `--json` modes; iteration order is fixed (surface enum in chat→palette→widget→voice order, capabilities in manifest declared order); no wall-clock fields inside per-surface entries; top-level `generated_at` is copy-forward from the manifest, never re-stamped.
- [x] Empty-capabilities valid-exit-0 rule (mirroring M27): when `capabilities: []` is a valid empty array, the command MUST exit 0 in both default and `--json` modes; human mode emits the single explicit line `No capabilities in manifest — nothing to plan.` to stdout (no surface section, no warnings); `--json` mode emits `{manifest_path, manifest_version, generated_at, surfaces: []}` with the top-level fields copied verbatim. This is distinct from a missing/non-array `capabilities` (exit 1 with `Invalid manifest: missing capabilities array`).
- [x] I/O stream discipline (mirroring M27): every error message path (`Manifest not found:`, `Invalid manifest JSON:`, `Invalid manifest: missing capabilities array`, `Unknown surface:`, `Unknown subcommand:`, `Unknown flag:`, `Cannot write to --out path:`) writes exclusively to stderr; stdout MUST be empty on every exit-1 path (no partial plan, no JSON object with an `error` field, no trailing newline). Smoke assertion captures both streams and verifies `stdout === ""` on every error case.
- [x] `--help` prints the M30 command shape, the four-value `surface` enum (plus `all`), the four flags (`--surface`, `--manifest`, `--out`, `--json`), exit codes, and an explicit "This is a planning aid, not a runtime surface generator" callout; help text is byte-identical across runs.
- [x] `--out <path>`: when supplied, writes the plan output (human or JSON depending on `--json`) to the path and emits no stdout on success; if the path is unwritable, exits 1 with `Cannot write to --out path:` followed by the path on stderr and empty stdout. The path MUST NOT be inside `.tusq/`; an attempt to write inside `.tusq/` exits 1 with `--out path must not be inside .tusq/` on stderr.
- [x] Update `tusq help` to add the `surface` noun and the `plan` subcommand exactly once; the `surface` line is inserted alphabetically between `serve` and `redaction` in the help enumeration so the help block remains stably ordered.
- [x] Add smoke coverage for: (a) default `tusq surface plan` on a manifest with mixed sensitivity/auth/side-effect capabilities produces exit 0 and the expected per-surface eligibility/gating split; (b) `--surface chat`/`--surface palette`/`--surface widget`/`--surface voice` each emit one surface section; (c) `--surface all` emits all four in the frozen order; (d) `--surface unknown` exits 1 with `Unknown surface:` and empty stdout; (e) missing `--manifest` path exits 1 with `Manifest not found:`; (f) malformed-JSON manifest exits 1 with `Invalid manifest JSON:` before any stdout; (g) running twice produces byte-identical stdout in both modes; (h) M30 does not mutate the manifest (mtime/content unchanged); (i) `capability_digest` does not flip on any capability after a plan run (asserted by hash compare); (j) `tusq compile` golden-file output is byte-identical pre and post-M30; (k) `tusq serve tools/list` golden-file output is byte-identical; (l) empty-capabilities manifest emits the documented human line and `surfaces: []` JSON; (m) `--out <path>` writes to the path and emits no stdout on success; (n) `--out` to an unwritable path exits 1; (o) every gating reason resolves to exactly one of the six closed reason codes; (p) destructive verb is gated for `palette` and `voice` but allowed for `chat` and `widget action_widgets`.
- [x] Add one eval regression scenario `surface-plan-determinism` to `tests/evals/governed-cli-scenarios.json` asserting that `tusq surface plan --json` produces byte-identical stdout across three runs on the same manifest and that the gating-reason enum is closed (every gated capability's reason is one of the six values). Total eval scenarios become **≥21** (current 20 + 1 new).
- [x] Add Constraint 23 to SYSTEM_SPEC.md Constraints section: "`tusq surface plan` is a planning aid that describes what an embeddable surface **would** look like for the current manifest. It does NOT generate runnable chat/widget/palette/voice code, does NOT host any runtime, does NOT execute capabilities, does NOT read or write any brand profile, and does NOT certify brand or accessibility compliance. Subsequent milestones (chat-only generator, palette-only generator, widget-only generator, voice-only generator) ship under their own ROADMAP entries with fresh acceptance contracts and fresh re-approval expectations."

>

The CLI surface grows from 14 → 15 commands. The mutually exclusive alternative form `tusq plan domain` under a future planning hub is explicitly rejected for V1.12; a future planning hub may subsume `domain index` later under its own ROADMAP milestone if and when it is chartered.

- [x] Add new top-level noun `domain` with single subcommand `index` to the CLI surface; `tusq domain` (no subcommand) prints a short enumerate-subcommands block identical in shape to `tusq surface`, `tusq policy`, and `tusq redaction`; unknown subcommands exit 1 with `Unknown subcommand:` followed by the name and empty stdout. CLI surface grows from 14 commands to **15** (init, scan, manifest, compile, serve, review, docs, approve, diff, policy, redaction, surface, domain, version, help).

- [x] Add the frozen two-value `aggregation_key` enum: `domain | unknown`. The enum is immutable once M31 ships; any addition is a material governance event under its own ROADMAP milestone with a fresh re-approval expectation. The `unknown` bucket aggregates every capability whose `domain` field is `null`, missing, or empty-string (mirrors the M28 zero-evidence `unknown` guard precedent).
- [x] Default behavior: `tusq domain index` (no `--domain`) emits one entry per distinct domain in the manifest's `capabilities[]` *first-appearance* order, deterministic, never alphabetized. The `unknown` bucket (if any capability lacks a domain) is appended last. The `--domain <name>` flag limits output to a single bucket (string match against the manifest-declared domain value or the literal `unknown`); an unrecognized filter value exits 1 with `Unknown domain:` followed by the value, empty stdout.
- [x] Per-domain index entry shape (deterministic JSON under `--json`):
  - `domain`: string (the manifest-declared domain value, or the literal `"unknown"` for the zero-evidence bucket)
  - `aggregation_key`: one of the two enum values (`"domain"` or `"unknown"`)
  - `capability_count`: integer (number of capabilities in this bucket)
  - `capabilities[]`: array of capability names (strings) in manifest declared order
  - `approved_count`: integer (number of capabilities in this bucket where `approved === true`)
  - `gated_count`: integer (`capability_count - approved_count`)
  - `has_destructive_side_effect`: boolean (true iff any capability in this bucket has `side_effect_class === "destructive"`)
  - `has_restricted_or_confidential_sensitivity`: boolean (true iff any capability in this bucket has `sensitivity_class ∈ {"restricted", "confidential"}`)
  - `has_unknown_auth`: boolean (true iff any capability in this bucket has `auth_requirements.auth_scheme === "unknown"`)
  - top-level `manifest_path`, `manifest_version`, `generated_at` copied verbatim from the input manifest (with the M27 fallback: `null` in `--json` mode and `unknown` in human mode when the manifest lacks the field)
- [x] Read-only invariants (mirroring M27 Constraint 20 / M28 Constraint 21 / M29 Constraint 22 / M30 Constraint 23):

  - No write to `.tusq/`; no write to any path other than `--out <path>` when supplied (smoke assertion)
  - `capability_digest` MUST NOT flip on any capability (smoke assertion: hash before vs after is byte-identical)
  - `tusq compile` output is byte-identical pre and post-M31 for every fixture (golden-file smoke assertion)
  - `tusq serve` `tools/list` and `tools/call` and `dry_run_plan` responses are byte-identical pre and post-M31 (golden-file smoke assertion)
  - `tusq policy verify` (default and `--strict`), `tusq redaction review`, and `tusq surface plan` are byte-identical pre and post-M31
- [x] Deterministic output: running `tusq domain index` twice on the same manifest MUST produce byte-identical stdout in both human and `--json` modes; iteration order is fixed (manifest first-appearance order, with `unknown` appended last); no wall-clock fields inside per-domain entries; top-level `generated_at` is copy-forward from the manifest, never re-stamped.
- [x] Empty-capabilities valid-exit-0 rule (mirroring M27/M30): when `capabilities: []` is a valid empty array, the command MUST exit 0 in both default and `--json` modes; human mode emits the single explicit line `No capabilities in manifest — nothing to index.` to stdout (no domain section, no warnings); `--json` mode emits `{manifest_path, manifest_version, generated_at, domains: []}` with the top-level fields copied verbatim. ### M32: Static Capability Side-Effect Index Export from Manifest Evidence (~0.5 day) — V1.13 (PROPOSED)

> **Charter origin (run_ae841429202c5bb7, turn_b5d4f652077b62be, PM, HEAD `f858d36`, 2026-04-26):** This milestone is the next bounded roadmap increment derived from VISION.md under intake intent `intent_1777234191976_e06a` (vision_scan, category `roadmap_exhausted_vision_open`). The intake charter explicitly required "concrete unchecked M32 items," not another candidate-housing turn or a re-verification of M31. VISION sources cited:
>
> - **`.planning/VISION.md` lines 40–46 (`### Code And API Surface`)** — explicitly named in the charter's candidate pool ("Code And API Surface"); the section enumerates "REST routes, GraphQL resolvers, RPC/gRPC methods, webhooks, jobs, queues, and cron tasks; request and response schemas from types, DTOs, validators, route definitions, and framework metadata; status codes, error patterns, retry semantics, and normalized failure modes; **read, write, destructive, financial, security-sensitive, and admin-only side effects**; API contracts such as OpenAPI specs, GraphQL schemas, Postman collections, gRPC proto files, SDK definitions, and webhook specs." Item 4 — "read, write, destructive, financial, security-sensitive, and admin-only side effects" — is the specific dimension M32 surfaces as a per-side-effect-class index of the manifest's existing `side_effect_class` evidence.
> - **`.planning/VISION.md` lines 689–697 (`### Capability Overexposure`)** — under **Risks**, "An AI surface that exposes too many capabilities or destructive workflows... governance must show what is exposed at any moment and require approval for changes." A side-effect-class roll-up is the smallest reviewer-aid that lets an operator see "how many destructive capabilities do I have, how many are approved, and which domains do they sit in" at a glance — directly addressing the overexposure risk.
>
> Shipped reality M1–M31 covers the compiler/governance half plus the M27 redaction-review reviewer-aid, the M30 surface-plan planner, and the M31 per-domain capability index. The per-side-effect-class capability index — the parallel reviewer-aid that buckets capabilities by their `side_effect_class` value (the primary "is this safe to call without confirmation" signal codified in the M9 governance model at SYSTEM_SPEC line 625) — has not shipped. M32 is the smallest first increment that addresses the side-effect-visibility dimension of VISION § Code And API Surface item 4 **without** committing the project to risk-tier derivation, runtime side-effect enforcement, side-effect-driven approval gating, or side-effect-driven surface eligibility (the latter is M30's responsibility under the closed `gated_reason: destructive_side_effect` rule, which M32 MUST NOT duplicate or alter). Scope decision resolved this turn: M32 introduces a new top-level noun `effect` with a single subcommand `index` (mirroring the M27 `redaction review`, M30 `surface plan`, and M31 `domain index` precedents). The CLI surface grows from 15 → 16 commands. The mutually exclusive alternative forms (`tusq side-effect index` with a hyphenated noun, `tusq risk index` with a derived risk-tier enum, `tusq capability index --by side_effect`) are explicitly rejected for V1.13: hyphenated nouns introduce a new CLI parsing pattern that no other tusq noun uses; derived risk-tier composition adds policy that belongs in its own future M-Risk milestone; an `--by` axis flag would couple multiple aggregation modes into one command and violate the M27/M30/M31 single-aggregation-axis precedent.

- [x] Add new top-level noun `effect` with single subcommand `index` to the CLI surface; `tusq effect` (no subcommand) prints a short enumerate-subcommands block identical in shape to `tusq surface`, `tusq policy`, `tusq redaction`, and `tusq domain`; unknown subcommands exit 1 with `Unknown subcommand:` followed by the name and empty stdout. CLI surface grows from 15 commands to **16** (init, scan, manifest, compile, serve, review, docs, approve, diff, domain, **effect**, policy, redaction, surface, version, help) with `effect` inserted alphabetically between `domain` and `policy`.
- [x] Implement `tusq effect index` as a pure read-only deterministic command that reads the manifest path and writes only to stdout/stderr (or to `--out <path>` if supplied); no network I/O, no `.tusq/` write, no manifest mutation, no `tusq compile`/`tusq serve`/`tusq policy verify`/`tusq redaction review`/`tusq surface plan`/`tusq domain index` behavior change.
- [x] Add the frozen four-value `side_effect_class` bucket-key enum: `read | write | destructive | unknown`. The enum is immutable once M32 ships; any addition is a material governance event under its own ROADMAP milestone with a fresh re-approval expectation. The `unknown` bucket aggregates every capability whose `side_effect_class` field is `null`, missing, empty-string, or any value outside the closed three-value classifier set (mirrors the M28 zero-evidence `unknown` guard precedent and the M31 `unknown` domain-bucket precedent). NOTE: this enum is the bucket key, not a re-classification of capabilities — capabilities retain their existing `side_effect_class` value verbatim; the bucket-key value matches the capability's `side_effect_class` value 1:1, with `unknown` synthesized only for the zero-evidence catchall.
- [x] Add the frozen two-value `aggregation_key` enum: `class | unknown` (parallel to M31's `domain | unknown`). The enum is immutable once M32 ships; any addition is a material governance event under its own ROADMAP milestone with a fresh re-approval expectation. The `unknown` aggregation-key marks the zero-evidence bucket; the `class` aggregation-key marks every other bucket (read/write/destructive).
- [x] Default behavior: `tusq effect index` (no `--effect`) emits one entry per distinct `side_effect_class` value present in the manifest's `capabilities[]`, in the **closed enum order** `read → write → destructive` (NOT manifest first-appearance order — the closed enum imposes a deterministic global order; M31's first-appearance rule applies to open-string `domain` values, not to closed enums). The `unknown` bucket (if any capability lacks a valid `side_effect_class`) is appended last. Empty buckets MUST NOT appear (a `read` bucket appears only if at least one capability has `side_effect_class === "read"`). The `--effect <value>` flag limits output to a single bucket (string match against one of the four enum values: `read`, `write`, `destructive`, `unknown`); an unrecognized filter value exits 1 with `Unknown effect:` followed by the value, empty stdout.
- [x] Per-bucket index entry shape (deterministic JSON under `--json`):
  - `side_effect_class`: string (one of `"read"`, `"write"`, `"destructive"`, or the literal `"unknown"` for the zero-evidence bucket)
  - `aggregation_key`: one of the two enum values (`"class"` or `"unknown"`)
  - `capability_count`: integer (number of capabilities in this bucket)
  - `capabilities[]`: array of capability names (strings) in manifest declared order
  - `approved_count`: integer (number of capabilities in this bucket where `approved === true`)
  - `gated_count`: integer (`capability_count - approved_count`)
  - `has_restricted_or_confidential_sensitivity`: boolean (true iff any capability in this bucket has `sensitivity_class ∈ {"restricted", "confidential"}`)
  - `has_unknown_auth`: boolean (true iff any capability in this bucket has `auth_requirements.auth_scheme === "unknown"`)
  - top-level `manifest_path`, `manifest_version`, `generated_at` copied verbatim from the input manifest (with the M27 fallback: `null` in `--json` mode and `unknown` in human mode when the manifest lacks the field)
  - **deliberately omitted** (parallel to M31's omission of cross-cutting fields): no `domains_represented[]`, no `auth_schemes_represented[]`, no `pii_categories_present[]`, no `risk_tier`. Cross-axis roll-ups belong in their own future M-Risk milestone with a fresh acceptance contract.
- [x] Read-only invariants (mirroring M27 Constraint 20 / M28 Constraint 21 / M29 Constraint 22 / M30 Constraint 23 / M31 Constraint 24):
  - `tusq.manifest.json` mtime/content unchanged after every `tusq effect index` invocation (smoke assertion)
  - No write to `.tusq/`; no write to any path other than `--out <path>` when supplied (smoke assertion)
  - `capability_digest` MUST NOT flip on any capability (smoke assertion: hash before vs after is byte-identical)
  - `tusq compile` output is byte-identical pre and post-M32 for every fixture (golden-file smoke assertion)
  - `tusq serve` `tools/list` and `tools/call` and `dry_run_plan` responses are byte-identical pre and post-M32 (golden-file smoke assertion)
  - `tusq policy verify` (default and `--strict`), `tusq redaction review`, `tusq surface plan`, and `tusq domain index` are byte-identical pre and post-M32
- [x] Deterministic output: running `tusq effect index` twice on the same manifest MUST produce byte-identical stdout in both human and `--json` modes; bucket iteration order is fixed by the closed enum (read → write → destructive, then unknown last); within each bucket, capabilities iterate in manifest declared order; no wall-clock fields inside per-bucket entries; top-level `generated_at` is copy-forward from the manifest, never re-stamped.
- [x] Empty-capabilities valid-exit-0 rule (mirroring M27/M30/M31): when `capabilities: []` is a valid empty array, the command MUST exit 0 in both default and `--json` modes; human mode emits the single explicit line `No capabilities in manifest — nothing to index.` to stdout (no bucket section, no warnings); `--json` mode emits `{manifest_path, manifest_version, generated_at, effects: []}` with the top-level fields copied verbatim. This is distinct from a missing/non-array `capabilities` (exit 1 with `Invalid manifest: missing capabilities array`).
- [x] I/O stream discipline (mirroring M27/M30/M31): every error message path (`Manifest not found:`, `Invalid manifest JSON:`, `Invalid manifest: missing capabilities array`, `Unknown effect:`, `Unknown subcommand:`, `Unknown flag:`, `Cannot write to --out path:`) writes exclusively to stderr; stdout MUST be empty on every exit-1 path (no partial index, no JSON object with an `error` field, no trailing newline). Smoke assertion captures both streams and verifies `stdout === ""` on every error case.
- [x] `--help` prints the M32 command shape, the four-value `side_effect_class` bucket-key enum, the two-value `aggregation_key` enum, the four flags (`--effect`, `--manifest`, `--out`, `--json`), exit codes, and an explicit "This is a planning aid, not a runtime side-effect enforcer or risk-tier classifier" callout; help text is byte-identical across runs.
- [x] `--out <path>`: when supplied, writes the index output (human or JSON depending on `--json`) to the path and emits no stdout on success; if the path is unwritable, exits 1 with `Cannot write to --out path:` followed by the path on stderr and empty stdout. The path MUST NOT be inside `.tusq/`; an attempt to write inside `.tusq/` exits 1 with `--out path must not be inside .tusq/` on stderr (mirroring M30/M31).
- [x] Update `tusq help` to add the `effect` noun and the `index` subcommand exactly once; the `effect` line is inserted alphabetically between `domain` and `policy` in the help enumeration so the help block remains stably ordered (alphabetical position: `... approve, diff, domain, **effect**, policy, redaction, surface, ...`).
- [x] Add smoke coverage for: (a) default `tusq effect index` on a manifest with mixed read/write/destructive capabilities produces exit 0 and the expected per-bucket entries in closed-enum order (read → write → destructive); (b) `--effect read` / `--effect write` / `--effect destructive` / `--effect unknown` each emit exactly one matching entry; (c) `--effect bogus` exits 1 with `Unknown effect:` and empty stdout; (d) missing `--manifest` path exits 1 with `Manifest not found:`; (e) malformed-JSON manifest exits 1 with `Invalid manifest JSON:` before any stdout; (f) running twice produces byte-identical stdout in both modes; (g) M32 does not mutate the manifest (mtime/content unchanged); (h) `capability_digest` does not flip on any capability after an index run (asserted by hash compare); (i) `tusq compile` golden-file output is byte-identical pre and post-M32; (j) `tusq serve tools/list` golden-file output is byte-identical; (k) `tusq surface plan` and `tusq domain index` outputs are byte-identical pre and post-M32; (l) empty-capabilities manifest emits the documented human line and `effects: []` JSON; (m) `--out <path>` writes to the path and emits no stdout on success; (n) `--out` to an unwritable path exits 1; (o) `--out .tusq/anything.json` exits 1 with `--out path must not be inside .tusq/` on stderr; (p) capability with `side_effect_class: null` (or missing/empty-string/unknown-value) is bucketed into `unknown` and the `unknown` bucket appears last; (q) `aggregation_key` is exactly one of the two closed values for every emitted bucket; (r) empty buckets (e.g., manifest has only read capabilities) MUST NOT appear in output; (s) within each bucket, capability names appear in manifest declared order (NOT alphabetized); (t) `has_restricted_or_confidential_sensitivity` flag is true iff at least one capability in bucket has `sensitivity_class ∈ {restricted, confidential}` (asserted on a fixture with mixed sensitivity values); (u) `has_unknown_auth` flag is true iff at least one capability in bucket has `auth_requirements.auth_scheme === "unknown"` (asserted on a fixture with mixed auth schemes).
- [x] Add one eval regression scenario `effect-index-determinism` to `tests/evals/governed-cli-scenarios.json` asserting that `tusq effect index --json` produces byte-identical stdout across three runs on the same manifest, that the `side_effect_class` bucket-key enum is closed (every bucket's value is one of the four values), that the `aggregation_key` enum is closed (every bucket's value is one of the two values), and that bucket iteration order is the frozen closed-enum order (read → write → destructive, then unknown). Total eval scenarios become **≥23** (current 22 + 1 new).
- [x] Add Constraint 25 to SYSTEM_SPEC.md Constraints section: "`tusq effect index` is a planning aid that surfaces what side-effect classes the manifest exposes and the shape of each bucket. It does NOT enforce side-effect policy at runtime, does NOT derive a composite risk tier, does NOT generate confirmation-flow code, does NOT certify destructive-action safety, and does NOT alter the M30 `gated_reason: destructive_side_effect` surface-eligibility rule. Subsequent milestones (M-Risk-1 composite risk-tier classifier, M-Confirm-1 destructive-action confirmation-flow generator) ship under their own ROADMAP entries with fresh acceptance contracts and fresh re-approval expectations. The four-value `side_effect_class` bucket-key enum (`read | write | destructive | unknown`) and the two-value `aggregation_key` enum (`class | unknown`) are frozen; any addition is a material governance event."
- [x] Add M32 section to SYSTEM_SPEC.md with: purpose statement, command shape, frozen four-value `side_effect_class` bucket-key enum, frozen two-value `aggregation_key` enum, frozen per-bucket entry shape (8 fields), closed-enum bucket iteration order rule (read → write → destructive → unknown), within-bucket manifest-declared-order rule, empty-capabilities and stdout-discipline rules, read-only invariants, and the explicit non-runtime-enforcer/non-risk-classifier boundary statement.
- [x] Update `website/docs/cli-reference.md` to document the new `tusq effect index` command, the four-value bucket-key enum, the two-value aggregation_key enum, the four flags, exit codes, the empty-capabilities behavior, and the explicit "planning aid, not a runtime side-effect enforcer or risk-tier classifier" callout.
- [x] Update `website/docs/manifest-format.md` with a "Side-Effect Index" subsection explaining how the manifest's `side_effect_class` field drives per-bucket aggregation, how `null`/missing/empty-string/unknown-value classes are aggregated under `unknown`, that bucket iteration follows the closed-enum order (NOT manifest first-appearance — distinct from M31's domain rule), that within each bucket capability names follow manifest declared order, and that the side-effect index is read-only and never mutates the manifest.
- [x] `npm test` continues to exit 0; no new dependency added to `package.json` (no schema generator, no markdown renderer, no graph library, no risk-scoring library); 16-command CLI surface preserved exactly (init, scan, manifest, compile, serve, review, docs, approve, diff, domain, effect, policy, redaction, surface, version, help); only the new `tusq effect index` command is added; every existing command's stdout, stderr, and exit code is byte-identical pre and post-M32.

### M33: Static Capability Sensitivity Index Export from Manifest Evidence (~0.5 day) — V1.14 (PROPOSED)

> **Charter origin (run_4506c41d74e23e8e, turn_8803f8edb25d1a0e, PM, HEAD `2dcec80`, 2026-04-26):** This milestone is the next bounded roadmap increment derived from VISION.md under intake intent `intent_1777237013665_c189` (vision_scan, category `roadmap_exhausted_vision_open`). The intake charter explicitly required "concrete unchecked M33 items," not another candidate-housing turn or a re-verification of M32. VISION sources cited:
>
> - **`.planning/VISION.md` lines 108–114 (`### Data, Risk, And Sensitivity`)** — within the charter's "+25 more" candidate pool; the section enumerates "PII, payment data, secrets, regulated data, and customer-sensitive fields; retention, redaction, logging, and trace-safety hints; **capability risk tags and review recommendations**; provenance back to the source files and runtime evidence used to infer each claim." The `capability risk tags and review recommendations` clause is the specific dimension M33 surfaces as a per-sensitivity-class index of the manifest's existing M28-classified `sensitivity_class` evidence.
> - **`.planning/VISION.md` lines 56–64 (`### Auth, IAM, Permissions, And Tenant Boundaries`)** — the section closes with "The generated AI layer must respect the same access rules the logged-in user would have inside the SaaS portal," motivating the cross-axis flags `has_destructive_side_effect` and `has_unknown_auth` per sensitivity bucket so reviewers can see, at a glance, whether a `restricted` or `confidential` bucket contains capabilities with unknown auth scheme or destructive side effects (the highest-attention combinations).
>
> Shipped reality M1–M32 covers the compiler/governance half plus the M27 redaction-review reviewer-aid, the M30 surface-plan planner, the M31 per-domain capability index, and the M32 per-side-effect-class capability index. The per-sensitivity-class capability index — the parallel reviewer-aid that buckets capabilities by their `sensitivity_class` value (M28's frozen five-value enum, the primary "is this safe to expose without elevated review" signal codified in the M9 governance model) — has not shipped. M33 is the smallest first increment that addresses the sensitivity-visibility dimension of VISION § Data, Risk, And Sensitivity **without** committing the project to runtime sensitivity enforcement, automatic data-class enforcement, GDPR/HIPAA/SOC2/PCI compliance certification, alteration of M28's sensitivity_class derivation rules, or alteration of the M30 `gated_reason: restricted_sensitivity` / `gated_reason: confidential_sensitivity` surface-eligibility rules (the latter two are M30's responsibility under closed enums that M33 MUST NOT duplicate or alter). Scope decision resolved this turn: M33 introduces a new top-level noun `sensitivity` with a single subcommand `index` (mirroring the M27 `redaction review`, M30 `surface plan`, M31 `domain index`, and M32 `effect index` precedents). The CLI surface grows from 16 → 17 commands. The mutually exclusive alternative forms (`tusq sensitivity-class index` with a hyphenated noun, `tusq risk index` with a derived risk-tier enum, `tusq capability index --by sensitivity_class`) are explicitly rejected for V1.14: hyphenated nouns introduce a new CLI parsing pattern that no other tusq noun uses; derived risk-tier composition adds policy that belongs in its own future M-Risk-1 milestone; an `--by` axis flag would couple multiple aggregation modes into one command and violate the M27/M30/M31/M32 single-aggregation-axis precedent.

- [x] Add new top-level noun `sensitivity` with single subcommand `index` to the CLI surface; `tusq sensitivity` (no subcommand) prints a short enumerate-subcommands block identical in shape to `tusq effect`, `tusq surface`, `tusq policy`, `tusq redaction`, and `tusq domain`; unknown subcommands exit 1 with `Unknown subcommand:` followed by the name and empty stdout. CLI surface grows from 16 commands to **17** (init, scan, manifest, compile, serve, review, docs, approve, diff, domain, effect, policy, redaction, **sensitivity**, surface, version, help) with `sensitivity` inserted alphabetically between `redaction` and `surface` (`sensitivity` vs `surface`: `s-e` < `s-u`).
- [x] Implement `tusq sensitivity index` as a pure read-only deterministic command that reads the manifest path and writes only to stdout/stderr (or to `--out <path>` if supplied); no network I/O, no `.tusq/` write, no manifest mutation, no `tusq compile`/`tusq serve`/`tusq policy verify`/`tusq redaction review`/`tusq surface plan`/`tusq domain index`/`tusq effect index` behavior change.
- [x] Add the frozen five-value `sensitivity_class` bucket-key enum: `public | internal | confidential | restricted | unknown`. The enum is immutable once M33 ships; any addition is a material governance event under its own ROADMAP milestone with a fresh re-approval expectation. The bucket-key enum aligns 1:1 with the existing `SENSITIVITY_CLASSES` constant in `src/cli.js` (`['unknown', 'public', 'internal', 'confidential', 'restricted']`); the `unknown` bucket aggregates every capability whose `sensitivity_class` field is `null`, missing, empty-string, or any value outside the closed four-value classifier set (mirroring M28's zero-evidence `unknown` guard, M31's `unknown` domain bucket, and M32's `unknown` effect bucket). NOTE: this enum is the bucket key, not a re-classification of capabilities — capabilities retain their existing M28-derived `sensitivity_class` value verbatim; the bucket-key value matches the capability's `sensitivity_class` value 1:1, with `unknown` synthesized only for the zero-evidence catchall. M33 MUST NOT modify, override, or augment the M28 classifier.
- [x] Add the frozen two-value `aggregation_key` enum: `class | unknown` (parallel to M31's `domain | unknown` and M32's `class | unknown`). The enum is immutable once M33 ships; any addition is a material governance event under its own ROADMAP milestone with a fresh re-approval expectation. The `unknown` aggregation-key marks the zero-evidence bucket; the `class` aggregation-key marks every other bucket (public/internal/confidential/restricted).
- [x] Default behavior: `tusq sensitivity index` (no `--sensitivity`) emits one entry per distinct `sensitivity_class` value present in the manifest's `capabilities[]`, in the **closed enum order** `public → internal → confidential → restricted` (NOT manifest first-appearance order — the closed enum imposes a deterministic global order; M31's first-appearance rule applies to open-string `domain` values, not to closed enums; mirroring M32's closed-enum order convention). The `unknown` bucket (if any capability lacks a valid `sensitivity_class`) is appended last. Empty buckets MUST NOT appear (an `internal` bucket appears only if at least one capability has `sensitivity_class === "internal"`). The `--sensitivity <value>` flag limits output to a single bucket (string match against one of the five enum values: `public`, `internal`, `confidential`, `restricted`, `unknown`); an unrecognized filter value exits 1 with `Unknown sensitivity:` followed by the value, empty stdout.
- [x] Per-bucket index entry shape (deterministic JSON under `--json`):
  - `sensitivity_class`: string (one of `"public"`, `"internal"`, `"confidential"`, `"restricted"`, or the literal `"unknown"` for the zero-evidence bucket)

  - **deliberately omitted** (parallel to M31's omission of cross-cutting fields and M32's omission of cross-axis roll-up arrays): no `domains_represented[]`, no `auth_schemes_represented[]`, no `pii_categories_present[]`, no `side_effect_classes_represented[]`, no `risk_tier`. Total eval scenarios become **≥24** (current 23 + 1 new).
- [x] Add Constraint 26 to SYSTEM_SPEC.md Constraints section: "`tusq sensitivity index` is a planning aid that surfaces what sensitivity classes the manifest exposes and the shape of each bucket. It does NOT enforce sensitivity policy at runtime, does NOT enforce data-class access control, does NOT certify GDPR/HIPAA/SOC2/PCI compliance, does NOT generate retention policy, does NOT modify the M28 `sensitivity_class` derivation rules, and does NOT alter the M30 `gated_reason: restricted_sensitivity` or `gated_reason: confidential_sensitivity` surface-eligibility rules. Subsequent milestones (M-Risk-1 composite risk-tier classifier, M-Compliance-1 regulatory-tag emitter) ship under their own ROADMAP entries with fresh acceptance contracts and fresh re-approval expectations. The five-value `sensitivity_class` bucket-key enum (`public | internal | confidential | restricted | unknown`) and the two-value `aggregation_key` enum (`class | unknown`) are frozen; any addition is a material governance event."
- [x] Add M33 section to SYSTEM_SPEC.md with: purpose statement, command shape, frozen five-value `sensitivity_class` bucket-key enum, frozen two-value `aggregation_key` enum, frozen per-bucket entry shape (8 fields), closed-enum bucket iteration order rule (`public → internal → confidential → restricted → unknown`), within-bucket manifest-declared-order rule, empty-capabilities and stdout-discipline rules, read-only invariants, and the explicit non-runtime-enforcer/non-compliance-certifier boundary statement.
- [x] Update `website/docs/cli-reference.md` to document the new `tusq sensitivity index` command, the five-value bucket-key enum, the two-value aggregation_key enum, the four flags, exit codes, the empty-capabilities behavior, and the explicit "planning aid, not a runtime sensitivity enforcer or compliance certifier" callout.
- [x] Update `website/docs/manifest-format.md` with a "Sensitivity Index" subsection explaining how the manifest's `sensitivity_class` field (derived by the M28 classifier) drives per-bucket aggregation, how `null`/missing/empty-string/unknown-value classes are aggregated under `unknown`, that bucket iteration follows the closed-enum order (NOT manifest first-appearance — distinct from M31's domain rule; NOT risk-precedence — explicitly a stable-output convention), that within each bucket capability names follow manifest declared order, and that the sensitivity index is read-only and never mutates the manifest.
- [x] `npm test` continues to exit 0; no new dependency added to `package.json` (no schema generator, no markdown renderer, no graph library, no risk-scoring library, no compliance-validation library); 17-command CLI surface preserved exactly (init, scan, manifest, compile, serve, review, docs, approve, diff, domain, effect, policy, redaction, sensitivity, surface, version, help); only the new `tusq sensitivity index` command is added; every existing command's stdout, stderr, and exit code is byte-identical pre and post-M33.

### M34: Static Capability HTTP Method Index Export from Manifest Evidence (~0.5 day) — V1.15 (PROPOSED)

> Charter origin: bound 2026-04-26 in run_bf8efb6b9c733000 (turn_8656b25a486eaa6d, PM attempt 1) at HEAD `8921229` from intake charter `intent_1777239733034_e0fb` (vision_scan, category `roadmap_exhausted_vision_open`). VISION sources cited:
> - **`.planning/VISION.md` lines 40–46 (`### Code And API Surface`)** — within the charter's named candidate pool; item 1 enumerates "REST routes, GraphQL operations, queue handlers, and similar entry points." The HTTP method (verb) is the first-class attribute of every REST route and the most operator-recognizable axis of capability surface area; the per-method index lets a reviewer answer at a glance "how many DELETE / POST / PUT / PATCH endpoints am I exposing, and are any of them behind unknown auth or in the destructive side-effect bucket."
> - **`.planning/VISION.md` lines 689–697 (`### Capability Overexposure` under § Risks)** — "An AI surface that exposes too many capabilities or destructive workflows ... governance must show what is exposed at any moment and require approval for changes." The per-bucket cross-axis flags `has_destructive_side_effect` and `has_unknown_auth` directly address this risk by surfacing destructive-verb buckets and unknown-auth buckets at the bucket level.
>
> Shipped reality M1–M33 covers the compiler/governance half plus the M27 redaction-review reviewer-aid, the M30 surface-plan planner, the M31 per-domain index, the M32 per-side-effect-class index, and the M33 per-sensitivity-class index. The per-HTTP-method capability index — the parallel reviewer-aid that buckets capabilities by their `method` value (the canonical HTTP verb attached to every capability since M1) — has not shipped. M34 is the smallest first increment that addresses the HTTP-method-visibility dimension of VISION § Code And API Surface **without** committing the project to runtime HTTP-method routing, REST-convention validation, idempotency certification, automatic destructive-verb classification, or alteration of the M32 `side_effect_class` derivation rules (M32 derives `side_effect_class` from `method` plus other signals; M34 buckets capabilities by the manifest's verbatim `method` value and MUST NOT touch M32 rules). Scope decision resolved this turn: M34 introduces a new top-level noun `method` with a single subcommand `index` (mirroring the M27 `redaction review`, M30 `surface plan`, M31 `domain index`, M32 `effect index`, and M33 `sensitivity index` precedents). The CLI surface grows from 17 → 18 commands. The mutually exclusive alternative forms (`tusq verb index` with `verb` as the noun, `tusq http index` with a protocol-prefixed noun, `tusq capability index --by method` with an axis-flag) are explicitly rejected for V1.15: `verb` is ambiguous against grammatical use elsewhere in tusq help text; `http` would suggest broader HTTP-protocol scope (headers, status codes, content types) that this milestone explicitly does not address; an `--by` axis flag would couple multiple aggregation modes into one command and violate the M27/M30/M31/M32/M33 single-aggregation-axis precedent.

- [x] Add new top-level noun `method` with single subcommand `index` to the CLI surface; `tusq method` (no subcommand) prints a short enumerate-subcommands block identical in shape to `tusq sensitivity`, `tusq effect`, `tusq surface`, `tusq policy`, `tusq redaction`, and `tusq domain`; unknown subcommands exit 1 with `Unknown subcommand:` followed by the name and empty stdout. CLI surface grows from 17 commands to **18** (init, scan, manifest, compile, serve, review, docs, approve, diff, domain, effect, **method**, policy, redaction, sensitivity, surface, version, help) with `method` inserted alphabetically between `effect` and `policy` (`method` vs `policy`: `m` < `p`; `method` vs `effect`: `e` < `m`).
- [x] Implement `tusq method index` as a pure read-only deterministic command that reads the manifest path and writes only to stdout/stderr (or to `--out <path>` if supplied); no network I/O, no `.tusq/` write, no manifest mutation, no `tusq compile`/`tusq serve`/`tusq policy verify`/`tusq redaction review`/`tusq surface plan`/`tusq domain index`/`tusq effect index`/`tusq sensitivity index` behavior change.
- [x] Add the frozen five-value `http_method` bucket-key enum: `GET | POST | PUT | PATCH | DELETE | unknown`. The enum is immutable once M34 ships; any addition is a material governance event under its own ROADMAP milestone with a fresh re-approval expectation. The enum covers the canonical REST verbs that tusq's scanner already emits in the manifest's `method` field; HEAD, OPTIONS, TRACE, CONNECT, and any non-standard or empty/missing verb aggregate into `unknown` (mirroring M28 / M29 / M31 / M32 / M33 zero-evidence guards). The bucket-key value matches the capability's `method` value 1:1 (verbatim uppercase), with `unknown` synthesized only for the zero-evidence catchall (manifest `method` is `null`, missing, empty-string, or any value outside `GET`/`POST`/`PUT`/`PATCH`/`DELETE`). M34 MUST NOT modify, override, or augment the upstream scanner's `method` field; the enum is a bucket-key, not a re-classifier.
- [x] Add the frozen two-value `aggregation_key` enum: `method | unknown` (parallel to M31's `domain | unknown`, M32's `class | unknown`, M33's `class | unknown`). The enum is immutable once M34 ships; any addition is a material governance event under its own ROADMAP milestone with a fresh re-approval expectation. The `unknown` aggregation-key marks the zero-evidence bucket; the `method` aggregation-key marks every other bucket (GET/POST/PUT/PATCH/DELETE).
- [x] Default behavior: `tusq method index` (no `--method`) emits one entry per distinct `method` value present in the manifest's `capabilities[]`, in the **closed enum order** `GET → POST → PUT → PATCH → DELETE` (NOT manifest first-appearance order — the closed enum imposes a deterministic global order; M31's first-appearance rule applies to open-string `domain` values, not to closed enums; mirroring M32 / M33 closed-enum order conventions). The `unknown` bucket (if any capability lacks a valid `method`) is appended last. Empty buckets MUST NOT appear (a `DELETE` bucket appears only if at least one capability has `method === "DELETE"`). The `--method <value>` flag limits output to a single bucket (string match against one of the five enum values: `GET`, `POST`, `PUT`, `PATCH`, `DELETE`, plus the literal `unknown`); an unrecognized filter value exits 1 with `Unknown method:` followed by the value, empty stdout. Filter matching is **case-sensitive** uppercase only (mirroring the manifest's verbatim uppercase `method` field convention); lowercase values like `get` or `delete` exit 1 (rather than being upper-cased silently) so reviewer scripts cannot accidentally drift from the canonical uppercase form.
- [x] Per-bucket index entry shape (deterministic JSON under `--json`):
  - `http_method`: string (one of `"GET"`, `"POST"`, `"PUT"`, `"PATCH"`, `"DELETE"`, or the literal `"unknown"` for the zero-evidence bucket)
  - `aggregation_key`: one of the two enum values (`"method"` or `"unknown"`)
  - `capability_count`: integer (number of capabilities in this bucket)
  - `capabilities[]`: array of capability names (strings) in manifest declared order
  - `approved_count`: integer (number of capabilities in this bucket where `approved === true`)
  - `gated_count`: integer (`capability_count - approved_count`)
  - `has_destructive_side_effect`: boolean (true iff any capability in this bucket has `side_effect_class === "destructive"`)
  - `has_unknown_auth`: boolean (true iff any capability in this bucket has `auth_requirements.auth_scheme === "unknown"`)
  - top-level `manifest_path`, `manifest_version`, `generated_at` copied verbatim from the input manifest (with the M27 fallback: `null` in `--json` mode and `unknown` in human mode when the manifest lacks the field)
  - **deliberately omitted** (parallel to M31 / M32 / M33 omissions): no `domains_represented[]`, no `auth_schemes_represented[]`, no `side_effect_classes_represented[]`, no `sensitivity_classes_represented[]`, no `idempotency_class`, no `risk_tier`. Cross-axis roll-ups belong in their own future M-Risk-1 / M-Idempotency-1 milestones with fresh acceptance contracts.
- [x] Read-only invariants (mirroring M27 Constraint 20 / M28 Constraint 21 / M29 Constraint 22 / M30 Constraint 23 / M31 Constraint 24 / M32 Constraint 25 / M33 Constraint 26):
  - `tusq.manifest.json` mtime/content unchanged after every `tusq method index` invocation (smoke assertion)
  - No write to `.tusq/`; no write to any path other than `--out <path>` when supplied (smoke assertion)
  - `capability_digest` MUST NOT flip on any capability (smoke assertion: hash before vs after is byte-identical)
  - `tusq compile` output is byte-identical pre and post-M34 for every fixture (golden-file smoke assertion)
  - `tusq serve` `tools/list` and `tools/call` and `dry_run_plan` responses are byte-identical pre and post-M34 (golden-file smoke assertion)
  - `tusq policy verify` (default and `--strict`), `tusq redaction review`, `tusq surface plan`, `tusq domain index`, `tusq effect index`, and `tusq sensitivity index` are byte-identical pre and post-M34
- [x] Deterministic output: running `tusq method index` twice on the same manifest MUST produce byte-identical stdout in both human and `--json` modes; bucket iteration order is fixed by the closed enum (`GET → POST → PUT → PATCH → DELETE`, then `unknown` last); within each bucket, capabilities iterate in manifest declared order; no wall-clock fields inside per-bucket entries; top-level `generated_at` is copy-forward from the manifest, never re-stamped.
- [x] Empty-capabilities valid-exit-0 rule (mirroring M27/M30/M31/M32/M33): when `capabilities: []` is a valid empty array, the command MUST exit 0 in both default and `--json` modes; human mode emits the single explicit line `No capabilities in manifest — nothing to index.` to stdout (no bucket section, no warnings); `--json` mode emits `{manifest_path, manifest_version, generated_at, methods: []}` with the top-level fields copied verbatim. This is distinct from a missing/non-array `capabilities` (exit 1 with `Invalid manifest: missing capabilities array`).
- [x] I/O stream discipline (mirroring M27/M30/M31/M32/M33): every error message path (`Manifest not found:`, `Invalid manifest JSON:`, `Invalid manifest: missing capabilities array`, `Unknown method:`, `Unknown subcommand:`, `Unknown flag:`, `Cannot write to --out path:`) writes exclusively to stderr; stdout MUST be empty on every exit-1 path (no partial index, no JSON object with an `error` field, no trailing newline). Smoke assertion captures both streams and verifies `stdout === ""` on every error case.
- [x] `--help` prints the M34 command shape, the six-value `http_method` bucket-key enum (five canonical + `unknown`), the two-value `aggregation_key` enum, the four flags (`--method`, `--manifest`, `--out`, `--json`), exit codes, and an explicit "This is a planning aid, not a runtime HTTP-method router, REST-convention validator, or idempotency classifier" callout; help text is byte-identical across runs.
- [x] `--out <path>`: when supplied, writes the index output (human or JSON depending on `--json`) to the path and emits no stdout on success; if the path is unwritable, exits 1 with `Cannot write to --out path:` followed by the path on stderr and empty stdout. The path MUST NOT be inside `.tusq/`; an attempt to write inside `.tusq/` exits 1 with `--out path must not be inside .tusq/` on stderr (mirroring M30/M31/M32/M33).
- [x] Update `tusq help` to add the `method` noun and the `index` subcommand exactly once; the `method` line is inserted alphabetically between `effect` and `policy` in the help enumeration so the help block remains stably ordered (alphabetical position: `... effect, **method**, policy, redaction, sensitivity, surface, version, help`).
- [x] Add smoke coverage for: (a) default `tusq method index` on a manifest with mixed GET/POST/PUT/PATCH/DELETE capabilities produces exit 0 and the expected per-bucket entries in closed-enum order (GET → POST → PUT → PATCH → DELETE); (b) `--method GET` / `--method POST` / `--method PUT` / `--method PATCH` / `--method DELETE` / `--method unknown` each emit exactly one matching entry; (c) `--method bogus` exits 1 with `Unknown method:` and empty stdout; (c2) `--method get` (lowercase) exits 1 with `Unknown method:` and empty stdout (case-sensitive enforcement); (d) missing `--manifest` path exits 1 with `Manifest not found:`; (e) malformed-JSON manifest exits 1 with `Invalid manifest JSON:` before any stdout; (f) running twice produces byte-identical stdout in both modes; (g) M34 does not mutate the manifest (mtime/content unchanged); (h) `capability_digest` does not flip on any capability after an index run (asserted by hash compare); (i) `tusq compile` golden-file output is byte-identical pre and post-M34; (j) `tusq serve tools/list` golden-file output is byte-identical; (k) `tusq surface plan`, `tusq domain index`, `tusq effect index`, and `tusq sensitivity index` outputs are byte-identical pre and post-M34; (l) empty-capabilities manifest emits the documented human line and `methods: []` JSON; (m) `--out <path>` writes to the path and emits no stdout on success; (n) `--out` to an unwritable path exits 1; (o) `--out .tusq/anything.json` exits 1 with `--out path must not be inside .tusq/` on stderr; (p) capability with `method: null` (or missing/empty-string/HEAD/OPTIONS/non-canonical-value) is bucketed into `unknown` and the `unknown` bucket appears last; (q) `aggregation_key` is exactly one of the two closed values for every emitted bucket; (r) empty buckets (e.g., manifest has only GET capabilities) MUST NOT appear in output; (s) within each bucket, capability names appear in manifest declared order (NOT alphabetized); (t) `has_destructive_side_effect` flag is true iff at least one capability in bucket has `side_effect_class === "destructive"` (asserted on a fixture with mixed side-effect values); (u) `has_unknown_auth` flag is true iff at least one capability in bucket has `auth_requirements.auth_scheme === "unknown"` (asserted on a fixture with mixed auth schemes).
- [x] Add one eval regression scenario `method-index-determinism` to `tests/evals/governed-cli-scenarios.json` asserting that `tusq method index --json` produces byte-identical stdout across three runs on the same manifest, that the `http_method` bucket-key enum is closed (every bucket's value is one of the six values: `GET`/`POST`/`PUT`/`PATCH`/`DELETE`/`unknown`), that the `aggregation_key` enum is closed (every bucket's value is one of the two values), and that bucket iteration order is the frozen closed-enum order (`GET → POST → PUT → PATCH → DELETE`, then `unknown`). Total eval scenarios become **≥25** (current 24 + 1 new).
- [x] Add Constraint 27 to SYSTEM_SPEC.md Constraints section: "`tusq method index` is a planning aid that surfaces what HTTP methods the manifest exposes and the shape of each bucket. It does NOT route HTTP methods at runtime, does NOT validate REST conventions (idempotency, safety, cacheability), does NOT certify idempotency class, does NOT automatically classify destructive verbs (DELETE is a bucket label, not a destructive-side-effect attestation), does NOT modify the M32 `side_effect_class` derivation rules (which use `method` as one of several inputs), and does NOT alter the M30 `gated_reason: destructive_side_effect` surface-eligibility rule. Subsequent milestones (M-Risk-1 composite risk-tier classifier, M-Idempotency-1 idempotency-class derivation, M-RestConv-1 REST-convention conformance check) ship under their own ROADMAP entries with fresh acceptance contracts and fresh re-approval expectations. The five-value `http_method` bucket-key enum (`GET | POST | PUT | PATCH | DELETE`) plus the `unknown` zero-evidence catchall (six total) and the two-value `aggregation_key` enum (`method | unknown`) are frozen; any addition is a material governance event. The `--method` filter is case-sensitive uppercase-only; lowercase or mixed-case filter values exit 1 with `Unknown method:`."
