### M35: Static Capability Auth Scheme Index Export from Manifest Evidence (~0.5 day) — V1.16 (PROPOSED)

> Charter origin: bound 2026-04-26 in run_0b373a30d182816a (turn_d7fc926d1c177c66, PM attempt 1) at HEAD `b129ca9` from intake charter `intent_1777242416896_42c9` (vision_scan, category `roadmap_exhausted_vision_open`, charter "Derive next bounded roadmap increment from VISION.md. Candidate pool: The Promise, Code And API Surface, Database, Warehouse, And Data Model, Frontend, Design System, And Product UX, Domain Model And Workflows (+25 more). Current roadmap checked through M34: Static Capability HTTP Method Index Export from Manifest Evidence (~0.5 day) — V1.15 (PROPOSED)."). VISION sources cited:
> - **`.planning/VISION.md` lines 56–64 (`### Auth, IAM, Permissions, And Tenant Boundaries`)** — within the charter's "+25 more" candidate pool; the section enumerates "user authentication, session boundaries, OAuth and OIDC scopes, generated MCP-server adapters, multi-tenant boundaries, role-based and attribute-based access control" and closes with "The generated AI layer must respect the same access rules the logged-in user would have inside the SaaS portal." The per-`auth_scheme` index is the smallest reviewer-aid that lets an operator see, at a glance, "how many capabilities are behind no auth at all, how many are behind unknown auth, how many are bearer-token-protected, and which of the unknown-auth bucket are also destructive or restricted-sensitivity" — the central question that operationalizes the section's "respect the same access rules" promise.
> - **`.planning/VISION.md` lines 689–697 (`### Capability Overexposure` under § Risks)** — "An AI surface that exposes too many capabilities or destructive workflows ... governance must show what is exposed at any moment and require approval for changes." The per-bucket cross-axis flags `has_destructive_side_effect` and `has_restricted_or_confidential_sensitivity` directly address this risk by surfacing unknown-auth buckets that contain destructive or sensitive capabilities at the bucket level.
>
> Shipped reality M1–M34 covers the compiler/governance half plus the M27 redaction-review reviewer-aid, the M30 surface-plan planner, the M31 per-domain index, the M32 per-side-effect-class index, the M33 per-sensitivity-class index, and the M34 per-HTTP-method index. The per-auth-scheme capability index — the parallel reviewer-aid that buckets capabilities by their `auth_requirements.auth_scheme` value (M29's frozen seven-value enum) — has not shipped. M29 produced the per-capability `auth_scheme` value and a `--auth-scheme` filter on the existing `tusq review` command, but does NOT aggregate capabilities into a per-scheme roll-up; reviewers asking "how many capabilities are in the `none` or `unknown` auth bucket" must currently re-run `tusq review --auth-scheme <value>` once per scheme and manually count. M35 is the smallest first increment that addresses the auth-scheme-visibility dimension of VISION § Auth, IAM, Permissions, And Tenant Boundaries **without** committing the project to runtime authentication enforcement, runtime AAA validation, OAuth/OIDC/SAML compliance certification, generated auth-adapter code, IAM-context derivation, or alteration of M29's `auth_scheme` derivation rules (M29 derives `auth_scheme` from middleware-name regex evidence; M35 buckets capabilities by the manifest's verbatim `auth_scheme` value and MUST NOT touch M29 rules). Scope decision resolved this turn: M35 introduces a new top-level noun `auth` with a single subcommand `index` (mirroring the M27 `redaction review`, M30 `surface plan`, M31 `domain index`, M32 `effect index`, M33 `sensitivity index`, and M34 `method index` precedents). The CLI surface grows from 18 → 19 commands with `auth` inserted alphabetically between `approve` and `compile` (`auth` vs `approve`: `aut` < `app` is FALSE — `app` < `aut` because `p` < `u`; therefore `approve` < `auth` < `compile`). The mutually exclusive alternative forms (`tusq iam index` with `iam` as the noun, `tusq scheme index` with a generic-scheme noun, `tusq capability index --by auth_scheme` with an axis-flag, extending the existing `tusq review --auth-scheme` filter rather than adding a noun) are explicitly rejected for V1.16: `iam` overscopes the milestone (IAM includes roles, scopes, tenancy, attributes — not just the auth-scheme dimension); `scheme` is ambiguous against unrelated uses elsewhere (the URL scheme in the manifest's `route` field, schema fields from M24); an `--by` axis flag would couple multiple aggregation modes into one command and violate the M27/M30/M31/M32/M33/M34 single-aggregation-axis precedent; extending `tusq review --auth-scheme` would violate the same precedent and would conflate the per-capability filter (one capability per row) with the per-bucket roll-up (one bucket per row).
>
> **Acceptance contract response (charter line by line):**
> 1. _New unchecked milestone items added to .planning/ROADMAP.md_ — § M35 below adds 20 unchecked `[ ]` items covering CLI surface, command implementation, two frozen enums, default behavior, per-bucket entry shape, read-only invariants, deterministic-output rule, empty-capabilities rule, I/O stream discipline, `--help` callout, `--out` rules, `tusq help` insertion, smoke matrix (cases a-u), eval regression scenario, Constraint 28, SYSTEM_SPEC § M35 reservation, two website-doc updates, and the 19-command CLI-surface preservation invariant.
> 2. _Milestone cites at least one concrete VISION.md source section from the unplanned backlog_ — § M35 charter origin block above cites `.planning/VISION.md` lines 56–64 (**Auth, IAM, Permissions, And Tenant Boundaries**) and lines 689–697 (**Capability Overexposure** under § Risks).
> 3. _Milestone is bounded, testable, and does not duplicate existing checked milestones_ — Bounded: ~0.5 day, single new noun `auth`, single subcommand `index`, four flags, no new dependency. Testable: 21-case smoke matrix and one new eval scenario `auth-scheme-index-determinism`. Non-duplicating: M27 (redaction-review reviewer-aid), M28 (sensitivity classifier), M29 (auth requirements classifier — produces the per-capability `auth_scheme` value and a `--auth-scheme` filter on `tusq review` but does NOT aggregate into a per-scheme roll-up), M30 (surface eligibility — uses `auth_scheme` as a gating signal in `gated_reason: auth_scheme_unknown` and `gated_reason: auth_scheme_oauth_pending_v2` but does NOT emit a per-scheme index), M31 (per-domain), M32 (per-side-effect-class), M33 (per-sensitivity-class), M34 (per-HTTP-method) all bucket on different axes; M35 buckets on the manifest's verbatim `auth_requirements.auth_scheme` value, which no shipped milestone aggregates into a per-scheme roll-up.

- [x] Add new top-level noun `auth` with single subcommand `index` to the CLI surface; `tusq auth` (no subcommand) prints a short enumerate-subcommands block identical in shape to `tusq method`, `tusq sensitivity`, `tusq effect`, `tusq surface`, `tusq policy`, `tusq redaction`, and `tusq domain`; unknown subcommands exit 1 with `Unknown subcommand:` followed by the name and empty stdout. CLI surface grows from 18 commands to **19** (init, scan, manifest, compile, serve, review, docs, approve, **auth**, diff, domain, effect, method, policy, redaction, sensitivity, surface, version, help) with `auth` inserted alphabetically between `approve` and `compile` (`approve` vs `auth`: `app` < `aut` because `p` < `u`; `auth` vs `compile`: `a` < `c`). Note: in the alphabetic `tusq help` enumeration, the `auth` line lands between `approve` and `compile`; `init`/`scan`/`manifest`/`serve`/`review`/`docs` retain their existing manual ordering at the top of the help block per the existing M27/M30/M31/M32/M33/M34 precedent (the alphabetical insertion rule applies inside the planning-aid block, not the top-of-help operational block).
- [x] Implement `tusq auth index` as a pure read-only deterministic command that reads the manifest path and writes only to stdout/stderr (or to `--out <path>` if supplied); no network I/O, no `.tusq/` write, no manifest mutation, no `tusq compile`/`tusq serve`/`tusq policy verify`/`tusq redaction review`/`tusq surface plan`/`tusq domain index`/`tusq effect index`/`tusq sensitivity index`/`tusq method index` behavior change.
- [x] Add the frozen seven-value `auth_scheme` bucket-key enum: `bearer | api_key | session | basic | oauth | none | unknown`. The enum is immutable once M35 ships; any addition is a material governance event under its own ROADMAP milestone with a fresh re-approval expectation. The enum aligns 1:1 with the existing M29 `AUTH_SCHEMES` constant in `src/cli.js` (`['unknown', 'bearer', 'api_key', 'session', 'basic', 'oauth', 'none']`); the bucket-key value matches the capability's `auth_requirements.auth_scheme` value 1:1 (verbatim lowercase). M35 MUST reference the M29 `AUTH_SCHEMES` constant directly (not redeclare an independent enum) so any future M29 classifier change surfaces as a synchronous mismatch rather than silent drift. M35 MUST NOT modify, override, or augment the upstream M29 classifier; the enum is a bucket-key, not a re-classifier.
- [x] Add the frozen two-value `aggregation_key` enum: `scheme | unknown` (parallel to M31's `domain | unknown`, M32's `class | unknown`, M33's `class | unknown`, M34's `method | unknown`). The enum is immutable once M35 ships; any addition is a material governance event under its own ROADMAP milestone with a fresh re-approval expectation. The `unknown` aggregation-key marks the zero-evidence bucket; the `scheme` aggregation-key marks every other bucket (bearer/api_key/session/basic/oauth/none).
- [x] Default behavior: `tusq auth index` (no `--scheme`) emits one entry per distinct `auth_scheme` value present in the manifest's `capabilities[]`, in the **closed enum order** `bearer → api_key → session → basic → oauth → none` (NOT manifest first-appearance order — the closed enum imposes a deterministic global order; M31's first-appearance rule applies to open-string `domain` values, not to closed enums; mirroring M32 / M33 / M34 closed-enum order conventions). The `unknown` bucket (if any capability has `auth_scheme === "unknown"` or lacks `auth_requirements`) is appended last. Empty buckets MUST NOT appear (a `bearer` bucket appears only if at least one capability has `auth_scheme === "bearer"`). The `--scheme <value>` flag limits output to a single bucket (string match against one of the seven enum values: `bearer`, `api_key`, `session`, `basic`, `oauth`, `none`, plus the literal `unknown`); an unrecognized filter value exits 1 with `Unknown auth scheme:` followed by the value, empty stdout. Filter matching is **case-sensitive** lowercase only (mirroring the manifest's verbatim lowercase `auth_scheme` field convention and the M29 `AUTH_SCHEMES` constant); uppercase values like `BEARER` exit 1 (rather than being lower-cased silently) so reviewer scripts cannot accidentally drift from the canonical lowercase form.
- [x] Per-bucket index entry shape (deterministic JSON under `--json`):
  - `auth_scheme`: string (one of `"bearer"`, `"api_key"`, `"session"`, `"basic"`, `"oauth"`, `"none"`, or the literal `"unknown"`)
  - `aggregation_key`: one of the two enum values (`"scheme"` or `"unknown"`)
  - `capability_count`: integer (number of capabilities in this bucket)
  - `capabilities[]`: array of capability names (strings) in manifest declared order
  - `approved_count`: integer (number of capabilities in this bucket where `approved === true`)
  - `gated_count`: integer (`capability_count - approved_count`)
  - `has_destructive_side_effect`: boolean (true iff any capability in this bucket has `side_effect_class === "destructive"`)
  - `has_restricted_or_confidential_sensitivity`: boolean (true iff any capability in this bucket has `sensitivity_class === "restricted"` OR `sensitivity_class === "confidential"`)
  - top-level `manifest_path`, `manifest_version`, `generated_at` copied verbatim from the input manifest (with the M27 fallback: `null` in `--json` mode and `unknown` in human mode when the manifest lacks the field)
  - **deliberately omitted** (parallel to M31 / M32 / M33 / M34 omissions): no `domains_represented[]`, no `auth_scopes_represented[]`, no `auth_roles_represented[]`, no `methods_represented[]`, no `side_effect_classes_represented[]`, no `sensitivity_classes_represented[]`, no derived `risk_tier`, no derived `iam_posture` field. Cross-axis roll-ups belong in their own future M-IAM-Posture-1 / M-Risk-1 milestones with fresh acceptance contracts.
- [x] Read-only invariants (mirroring M27 Constraint 20 / M28 Constraint 21 / M29 Constraint 22 / M30 Constraint 23 / M31 Constraint 24 / M32 Constraint 25 / M33 Constraint 26 / M34 Constraint 27):
  - `tusq.manifest.json` mtime/content unchanged after every `tusq auth index` invocation (smoke assertion)
  - No write to `.tusq/`; no write to any path other than `--out <path>` when supplied (smoke assertion)
  - `capability_digest` MUST NOT flip on any capability (smoke assertion: hash before vs after is byte-identical)
  - `tusq compile` output is byte-identical pre and post-M35 for every fixture (golden-file smoke assertion)
  - `tusq serve` `tools/list` and `tools/call` and `dry_run_plan` responses are byte-identical pre and post-M35 (golden-file smoke assertion)
  - `tusq policy verify` (default and `--strict`), `tusq redaction review`, `tusq surface plan`, `tusq domain index`, `tusq effect index`, `tusq sensitivity index`, and `tusq method index` are byte-identical pre and post-M35
- [x] Deterministic output: running `tusq auth index` twice on the same manifest MUST produce byte-identical stdout in both human and `--json` modes; bucket iteration order is fixed by the closed enum (`bearer → api_key → session → basic → oauth → none`, then `unknown` last); within each bucket, capabilities iterate in manifest declared order; no wall-clock fields inside per-bucket entries; top-level `generated_at` is copy-forward from the manifest, never re-stamped.
- [x] Empty-capabilities valid-exit-0 rule (mirroring M27/M30/M31/M32/M33/M34): when `capabilities: []` is a valid empty array, the command MUST exit 0 in both default and `--json` modes; human mode emits the single explicit line `No capabilities in manifest — nothing to index.` to stdout (no bucket section, no warnings); `--json` mode emits `{manifest_path, manifest_version, generated_at, schemes: []}` with the top-level fields copied verbatim. This is distinct from a missing/non-array `capabilities` (exit 1 with `Invalid manifest: missing capabilities array`).
- [x] I/O stream discipline (mirroring M27/M30/M31/M32/M33/M34): every error message path (`Manifest not found:`, `Invalid manifest JSON:`, `Invalid manifest: missing capabilities array`, `Unknown auth scheme:`, `Unknown subcommand:`, `Unknown flag:`, `Cannot write to --out path:`) writes exclusively to stderr; stdout MUST be empty on every exit-1 path (no partial index, no JSON object with an `error` field, no trailing newline). Smoke assertion captures both streams and verifies `stdout === ""` on every error case.
- [x] `--help` prints the M35 command shape, the seven-value `auth_scheme` bucket-key enum, the two-value `aggregation_key` enum, the four flags (`--scheme`, `--manifest`, `--out`, `--json`), exit codes, and an explicit "This is a planning aid, not a runtime authentication enforcer, AAA validator, or OAuth/OIDC/SAML compliance certifier" callout; help text is byte-identical across runs.
- [x] `--out <path>`: when supplied, writes the index output (human or JSON depending on `--json`) to the path and emits no stdout on success; if the path is unwritable, exits 1 with `Cannot write to --out path:` followed by the path on stderr and empty stdout. The path MUST NOT be inside `.tusq/`; an attempt to write inside `.tusq/` exits 1 with `--out path must not be inside .tusq/` on stderr (mirroring M30/M31/M32/M33/M34).
- [x] Update `tusq help` to add the `auth` noun and the `index` subcommand exactly once; the `auth` line is inserted alphabetically between `approve` and `compile` in the help enumeration so the help block remains stably ordered (alphabetical position: `... approve, **auth**, compile, diff, domain, effect, method, policy, redaction, sensitivity, surface, version, help`).
- [x] Add smoke coverage for: (a) default `tusq auth index` on a manifest with mixed bearer/api_key/session/basic/oauth/none/unknown capabilities produces exit 0 and the expected per-bucket entries in closed-enum order; (b) `--scheme bearer` / `--scheme api_key` / `--scheme session` / `--scheme basic` / `--scheme oauth` / `--scheme none` / `--scheme unknown` each emit exactly one matching entry; (c) `--scheme bogus` exits 1 with `Unknown auth scheme:` and empty stdout; (c2) `--scheme BEARER` (uppercase) exits 1 with `Unknown auth scheme:` and empty stdout (case-sensitive enforcement); (d) missing `--manifest` path exits 1 with `Manifest not found:`; (e) malformed-JSON manifest exits 1 with `Invalid manifest JSON:` before any stdout; (f) running twice produces byte-identical stdout in both modes; (g) M35 does not mutate the manifest (mtime/content unchanged); (h) `capability_digest` does not flip on any capability after an index run (asserted by hash compare); (i) `tusq compile` golden-file output is byte-identical pre and post-M35; (j) `tusq serve tools/list` golden-file output is byte-identical; (k) `tusq surface plan`, `tusq domain index`, `tusq effect index`, `tusq sensitivity index`, and `tusq method index` outputs are byte-identical pre and post-M35; (l) empty-capabilities manifest emits the documented human line and `schemes: []` JSON; (m) `--out <path>` writes to the path and emits no stdout on success; (n) `--out` to an unwritable path exits 1; (o) `--out .tusq/anything.json` exits 1 with `--out path must not be inside .tusq/` on stderr; (p) capability with `auth_requirements: null` (or missing/empty `auth_scheme`) is bucketed into `unknown` and the `unknown` bucket appears last; (q) `aggregation_key` is exactly one of the two closed values for every emitted bucket; (r) empty buckets (e.g., manifest has only bearer capabilities) MUST NOT appear in output; (s) within each bucket, capability names appear in manifest declared order (NOT alphabetized); (t) `has_destructive_side_effect` flag is true iff at least one capability in bucket has `side_effect_class === "destructive"` (asserted on a fixture with mixed side-effect values); (u) `has_restricted_or_confidential_sensitivity` flag is true iff at least one capability in bucket has `sensitivity_class === "restricted"` or `sensitivity_class === "confidential"` (asserted on a fixture with mixed sensitivity values).
- [x] Add one eval regression scenario `auth-scheme-index-determinism` to `tests/evals/governed-cli-scenarios.json` asserting that `tusq auth index --json` produces byte-identical stdout across three runs on the same manifest, that the `auth_scheme` bucket-key enum is closed (every bucket's value is one of the seven values: `bearer`/`api_key`/`session`/`basic`/`oauth`/`none`/`unknown`), that the `aggregation_key` enum is closed (every bucket's value is one of the two values), and that bucket iteration order is the frozen closed-enum order (`bearer → api_key → session → basic → oauth → none`, then `unknown`). Total eval scenarios become **≥26** (current 25 + 1 new).
- [x] Add Constraint 28 to SYSTEM_SPEC.md Constraints section: "`tusq auth index` is a planning aid that surfaces what auth schemes the manifest exposes and the shape of each bucket. It does NOT enforce authentication at runtime, does NOT validate AAA (authentication/authorization/auditing), does NOT certify OAuth/OIDC/SAML compliance, does NOT generate auth-adapter code, does NOT derive IAM context, does NOT modify the M29 `auth_scheme` derivation rules (which use middleware-name regex evidence as input), and does NOT alter the M30 `gated_reason: auth_scheme_unknown` or `gated_reason: auth_scheme_oauth_pending_v2` surface-eligibility rules. Subsequent milestones (M-IAM-Posture-1 cross-axis IAM-posture roll-up, M-Auth-Adapter-1 generated auth adapter, M-Runtime-Auth-1 runtime auth validator) ship under their own ROADMAP entries with fresh acceptance contracts and fresh re-approval expectations. The seven-value `auth_scheme` bucket-key enum (`bearer | api_key | session | basic | oauth | none | unknown`) and the two-value `aggregation_key` enum (`scheme | unknown`) are frozen; any addition is a material governance event. The `--scheme` filter is case-sensitive lowercase-only; uppercase or mixed-case filter values exit 1 with `Unknown auth scheme:`. M35 implementation MUST reference the M29 `AUTH_SCHEMES` constant directly (not redeclare an independent enum); a synchronous guard MUST throw if the M35 bucket-key enum and M29 AUTH_SCHEMES ever diverge."
- [x] Add M35 section to SYSTEM_SPEC.md with: purpose statement, command shape, frozen seven-value `auth_scheme` bucket-key enum (referenced from M29 `AUTH_SCHEMES`), frozen two-value `aggregation_key` enum, frozen 8-field per-bucket entry shape, closed-enum bucket iteration order rule (`bearer → api_key → session → basic → oauth → none → unknown`), within-bucket manifest-declared-order rule, case-sensitive `--scheme` filter rule, empty-capabilities and stdout-discipline rules, read-only invariants, and the explicit non-runtime-enforcer/non-AAA-validator/non-compliance-certifier boundary statement.
- [x] Update `website/docs/cli-reference.md` to document the new `tusq auth index` command, the seven-value bucket-key enum, the two-value aggregation_key enum, the four flags, exit codes, the case-sensitive lowercase-only `--scheme` rule, the empty-capabilities behavior, and the explicit "planning aid, not a runtime authentication enforcer, AAA validator, or OAuth/OIDC/SAML compliance certifier" callout.
- [x] Update `website/docs/manifest-format.md` with an "Auth Scheme Index" subsection explaining how the manifest's `auth_requirements.auth_scheme` field (M29-derived) drives per-bucket aggregation, how `null`/missing `auth_requirements` or `auth_scheme === "unknown"` are aggregated under the `unknown` bucket, that bucket iteration follows the closed-enum order (NOT manifest first-appearance — distinct from M31's domain rule; NOT IAM-risk-precedence — explicitly a stable-output convention only), that within each bucket capability names follow manifest declared order, that the `--scheme` filter is case-sensitive lowercase-only, and that the auth scheme index is read-only and never mutates the manifest.

### M36: Static Capability Confidence Tier Index Export from Manifest Evidence (~0.5 day) — V1.17 (SHIPPED)

> Charter origin: bound 2026-04-26 in `run_8580d828f0e1cc1e` (`turn_f657958213bbfb9d`, PM attempt 1) at HEAD `7c6b47e` from intake charter `intent_1777245829806_cf3c` (vision_scan, category `roadmap_exhausted_vision_open`, charter "Derive next bounded roadmap increment from VISION.md. Candidate pool: The Promise, Code And API Surface, Database, Warehouse, And Data Model, Frontend, Design System, And Product UX, Domain Model And Workflows (+25 more). Current roadmap checked through M35: Static Capability Auth Scheme Index Export from Manifest Evidence (~0.5 day) — V1.16 (PROPOSED)."). VISION sources cited:
> - **`.planning/VISION.md` lines 128–141 (`### Source Inventory And Confidence`)** — explicitly within the charter's "+25 more" candidate pool; the section says "tusq.dev should produce an input inventory before it claims understanding" and enumerates "confidence by domain: code, schema, auth, workflow, brand, docs, support, data, runtime, marketplace" plus "the provenance behind every generated claim" and "The engine should not pretend all inputs are equal." The per-`confidence_tier` capability roll-up is the smallest reviewer-aid that lets an operator see, at a glance, "how many of my capabilities are high-confidence vs medium-confidence vs low-confidence vs unknown-confidence — and which low-confidence buckets also contain destructive or restricted-sensitivity capabilities" — the central question that operationalizes the section's "should not pretend all inputs are equal" promise as a single deterministic per-bucket export.
> - **`.planning/VISION.md` lines 709–711 (`### False Governance Confidence` under § Risks)** — "Labels such as `approved`, `restricted`, `confidential`, or `auth_scheme: bearer` are not magic. The product must distinguish reviewer-aid metadata from runtime enforcement." The per-bucket cross-axis flags `has_destructive_side_effect` and `has_restricted_or_confidential_sensitivity` are particularly meaningful for the `low` and `unknown` confidence tiers — a `low`-confidence bucket containing destructive-side-effect or restricted-sensitivity capabilities is the highest-attention reviewer combination this milestone exposes, and the planning-aid framing in the help callout MUST explicitly state that confidence is reviewer-aid metadata, not runtime enforcement.
>
> Shipped reality M1–M35 covers the compiler/governance half plus the M27 redaction-review reviewer-aid, the M30 surface-plan planner, the M31 per-domain index, the M32 per-side-effect-class index, the M33 per-sensitivity-class index, the M34 per-HTTP-method index, and the M35 per-auth-scheme index. The per-`confidence_tier` capability index — the parallel reviewer-aid that buckets capabilities by an evidence-quality tier derived from the manifest's existing per-capability `confidence` numeric field (set by the scanner at M14/M15) — has not shipped. The scanner emits `confidence` as a numeric value in `[0, 1]` (typical default `0.76` for express-extracted capabilities), but no shipped command aggregates capabilities into a per-tier roll-up; reviewers asking "how many capabilities are below the high-confidence threshold and what is their cross-axis side-effect/sensitivity exposure?" must currently re-run `tusq review` per capability and manually inspect each numeric value. M36 is the smallest first increment that addresses the confidence-distribution-visibility dimension of VISION § Source Inventory And Confidence **without** committing the project to runtime confidence-based gating, runtime evidence-quality scoring, automated re-classification of low-confidence capabilities, alteration of the scanner's `confidence` derivation rules, or addition of a new `confidence_tier` field to the manifest itself (M36 derives the tier on-the-fly inside the index command from the existing numeric `confidence` value; the tier is reviewer-aid metadata only and is intentionally NOT persisted into `tusq.manifest.json`). Scope decision resolved this turn: M36 introduces a new top-level noun `confidence` with a single subcommand `index` (mirroring the M27 `redaction review`, M30 `surface plan`, M31 `domain index`, M32 `effect index`, M33 `sensitivity index`, M34 `method index`, and M35 `auth index` precedents). The CLI surface grows from 19 → 20 commands with `confidence` inserted alphabetically between `auth` and `diff` in the alphabetic block of the help enumeration (`auth` vs `confidence`: `a` < `c`; `confidence` vs `diff`: `c` < `d`; therefore `... approve, auth, confidence, diff, ...`). The mutually exclusive alternative forms (`tusq quality index` with `quality` as the noun, `tusq evidence index` with `evidence` as the noun, `tusq capability index --by confidence_tier` with an axis-flag, extending the existing `tusq review` to add a confidence-tier filter) are explicitly rejected for V1.17: `quality` overscopes the milestone (quality includes correctness, completeness, freshness, contradiction-resolution — not just the confidence-tier dimension); `evidence` is ambiguous against unrelated uses (M28 sensitivity evidence, M29 auth evidence, M30 surface-eligibility evidence, M27 redaction evidence); an `--by` axis flag would couple multiple aggregation modes into one command and violate the M27/M30/M31/M32/M33/M34/M35 single-aggregation-axis precedent; extending `tusq review` would conflate per-capability filter output with per-bucket roll-up output. The closed four-value `confidence_tier` bucket-key enum (`high | medium | low | unknown`) is M36-defined (NOT pre-existing in the manifest like M35's `auth_scheme` from M29 — confidence is numeric, the tier is a derived bucket-key); the tier function is frozen at planning time and is a pure function of the manifest's per-capability `confidence` numeric field: `high` if `confidence >= 0.85`, `low` if `confidence < 0.6`, `medium` if `0.6 <= confidence < 0.85`, `unknown` if `confidence` is `null`, missing, non-numeric, `NaN`, `+Infinity`, `-Infinity`, or outside `[0, 1]` (the last condition catches scanner regressions that emit out-of-range numbers — they are bucketed as `unknown` rather than silently coerced; an out-of-range value is also written to stderr as a `Warning: confidence out of [0,1] range for capability <name>: <value>` line in human mode and as a `warnings[]` entry in `--json` mode). Boundaries `0.85` and `0.6` are PM-frozen at M36 ship; any change to either threshold or to the four-value enum is a material governance event under its own ROADMAP milestone with a fresh re-approval expectation. The closed two-value `aggregation_key` enum is `tier | unknown` (parallel to M31 `domain | unknown`, M32 `class | unknown`, M33 `class | unknown`, M34 `method | unknown`, M35 `scheme | unknown`). The frozen 8-field per-bucket entry shape (`confidence_tier`, `aggregation_key`, `capability_count`, `capabilities[]`, `approved_count`, `gated_count`, `has_destructive_side_effect`, `has_restricted_or_confidential_sensitivity`) is intentionally name-and-counters-only and intentionally **omits** cross-axis roll-up arrays (`domains_represented[]`, `auth_schemes_represented[]`, `methods_represented[]`, `side_effect_classes_represented[]`, `sensitivity_classes_represented[]`, `pii_categories_represented[]`) and **omits** any derived `risk_tier`, `iam_posture`, `confidence_min`, `confidence_max`, `confidence_mean`, or `confidence_distribution[]` — all reserved for the deferred M-Risk-1 / M-IAM-Posture-1 / M-Confidence-Statistics-1 milestones with their own enums, their own acceptance contracts, and their own re-approval expectations. Bucket iteration order is the **closed-enum order** `high → medium → low → unknown` (NOT manifest first-appearance — M31's first-appearance rule applies to open-string `domain` values, not to closed enums; NOT confidence-numeric-descending — the closed-enum order is a deterministic stable-output convention only and MUST NOT be described as "evidence-strength-ranked," "trust-ranked," "highest-quality-first," or any phrase implying a quality semantic; the operative reading is "default reading order high→low with `unknown` last"; the `unknown` bucket is appended last, mirroring M32/M33/M34/M35). Within each bucket, capability names follow manifest declared order (mirroring M31/M32/M33/M34/M35 within-bucket ordering). Empty buckets MUST NOT appear (a `high` bucket appears only if at least one capability has `confidence >= 0.85`). Read-only invariants mirror M27/M28/M29/M30/M31/M32/M33/M34/M35: zero manifest mutation, zero `capability_digest` flips, zero new dependency in `package.json`, byte-identical `tusq compile`/`tusq serve`/`tusq policy verify`/`tusq redaction review`/`tusq surface plan`/`tusq domain index`/`tusq effect index`/`tusq sensitivity index`/`tusq method index`/`tusq auth index` output pre and post-M36. Empty-capabilities exits 0 with `No capabilities in manifest — nothing to index.` (human) and `{ manifest_path, manifest_version, generated_at, tiers: [] }` (`--json`); every error path empties stdout and writes exclusively to stderr. The `--out <path>` flag rejects any path resolving inside `.tusq/` (mirroring M30/M31/M32/M33/M34/M35). The `--tier <value>` filter limits output to a single bucket (string match against one of the four enum values: `high`, `medium`, `low`, `unknown`); an unrecognized filter value exits 1 with `Unknown confidence tier:` followed by the value, empty stdout. The `--tier` flag value matching is **case-sensitive** (lowercase only) — mirroring the M35 `--scheme` precedent; uppercase values like `HIGH` or `high ` (with whitespace) exit 1 (rather than being lower-cased or trimmed silently) so reviewer scripts cannot accidentally drift from the canonical lowercase form. Eval regression scenario `confidence-tier-index-determinism` brings the harness from 26 → **≥27** scenarios. Constraint 29 (proposed) codifies the planning-aid framing and forbids "runtime confidence enforcement / evidence-quality scoring engine / automated re-classification / alteration of scanner `confidence` derivation rules / persistence of `confidence_tier` into the manifest / cross-axis statistical aggregation" framings in docs/README/CLI-help. Six Key Risk rows added (misread as runtime confidence gate / evidence-quality engine; silent boundary drift on the `0.85`/`0.6` thresholds; silent enum drift on the four-value `confidence_tier` OR two-value `aggregation_key`; manifest mutation through index generation; `--out` path traversal into `.tusq/`; closed-enum order mistaken as quality-precedence). The deferred successor milestones (M-Risk-1 cross-axis risk tier, M-Confidence-Statistics-1 distribution roll-up with `confidence_min`/`max`/`mean`/histograms, M-Confidence-Persistence-1 if the operator ever decides to persist `confidence_tier` into the manifest) for actual policy/runtime artifacts remain deferred — each ships under its own ROADMAP entry with a fresh acceptance contract.
>
> **Acceptance contract response (charter line by line):**
> 1. _New unchecked milestone items added to .planning/ROADMAP.md_ — § M36 below adds 20 unchecked `[ ]` items covering CLI surface, command implementation, two frozen enums + frozen tier-function thresholds, default behavior, per-bucket entry shape, read-only invariants, deterministic-output rule, empty-capabilities rule, I/O stream discipline, `--help` callout, `--out` rules, `tusq help` insertion, smoke matrix (cases a-v), eval regression scenario, Constraint 29, SYSTEM_SPEC § M36 reservation, two website-doc updates, and the 20-command CLI-surface preservation invariant.
> 2. _Milestone cites at least one concrete VISION.md source section from the unplanned backlog_ — § M36 charter origin block above cites `.planning/VISION.md` lines 128–141 (**Source Inventory And Confidence**) and lines 709–711 (**False Governance Confidence** under § Risks). Neither section has been the primary aggregation-axis source for any shipped milestone (M28 cites `.planning/VISION.md` § Data, Risk, And Sensitivity; M29 cites § Auth; M30 cites The Promise + Brand-Matched Chat/Voice/Widget; M31 cites § Domain Model And Workflows; M32 cites § Integrations And Side Effects; M33 cites § Data, Risk, And Sensitivity; M34 cites § Code And API Surface; M35 cites § Auth, IAM, Permissions, And Tenant Boundaries + § Capability Overexposure).
> 3. _Milestone is bounded, testable, and does not duplicate existing checked milestones_ — Bounded: ~0.5 day, single new noun `confidence`, single subcommand `index`, four flags, no new dependency, the tier function is a single ternary expression on the existing manifest `confidence` field. Testable: 22-case smoke matrix (cases a-v) and one new eval scenario `confidence-tier-index-determinism`. Non-duplicating: M27 (redaction-review reviewer-aid), M28 (sensitivity classifier — derives `sensitivity_class`), M29 (auth requirements classifier — derives `auth_scheme`), M30 (surface eligibility — uses `confidence` as one of several gate inputs but does NOT aggregate by tier), M31 (per-domain), M32 (per-side-effect-class), M33 (per-sensitivity-class), M34 (per-HTTP-method), M35 (per-auth-scheme) — all bucket on different axes and none aggregates by an evidence-quality tier derived from the numeric `confidence` field.

- [x] Add new top-level noun `confidence` with single subcommand `index` to the CLI surface; `tusq confidence` (no subcommand) prints a short enumerate-subcommands block identical in shape to `tusq method`, `tusq sensitivity`, `tusq effect`, `tusq surface`, `tusq policy`, `tusq redaction`, `tusq domain`, and `tusq auth`; unknown subcommands exit 1 with `Unknown subcommand:` followed by the name and empty stdout. CLI surface grows from 19 commands to **20** (init, scan, manifest, compile, serve, review, docs, approve, auth, **confidence**, diff, domain, effect, method, policy, redaction, sensitivity, surface, version, help) with `confidence` inserted alphabetically between `auth` and `diff` in the alphabetic block (`auth` vs `confidence`: `a` < `c`; `confidence` vs `diff`: `c` < `d`). Note: in the alphabetic `tusq help` enumeration, the `confidence` line lands between `auth` and `diff`; `init`/`scan`/`manifest`/`compile`/`serve`/`review`/`docs` retain their existing manual ordering at the top of the help block per the existing M27/M30/M31/M32/M33/M34/M35 precedent (the alphabetical insertion rule applies inside the planning-aid block, not the top-of-help operational block).
- [x] Implement `tusq confidence index` as a pure read-only deterministic command that reads the manifest path and writes only to stdout/stderr (or to `--out <path>` if supplied); no network I/O, no `.tusq/` write, no manifest mutation, no `tusq compile`/`tusq serve`/`tusq policy verify`/`tusq redaction review`/`tusq surface plan`/`tusq domain index`/`tusq effect index`/`tusq sensitivity index`/`tusq method index`/`tusq auth index` behavior change.
- [x] Add the frozen four-value `confidence_tier` bucket-key enum: `high | medium | low | unknown`. The enum is immutable once M36 ships; any addition is a material governance event under its own ROADMAP milestone with a fresh re-approval expectation. The four values are named explicitly in `src/cli.js` as a frozen `Object.freeze(['high', 'medium', 'low'])` array (the named-three) plus the catchall `unknown` appended last by the bucket-iteration logic; the tier is derived at index-time from the manifest's per-capability `confidence` numeric field and is intentionally NOT persisted into `tusq.manifest.json` (M36 is reviewer-aid metadata only; persistence is deferred to a future M-Confidence-Persistence-1 milestone). M36 MUST NOT modify, override, or augment the scanner's `confidence` derivation rules; the tier is a pure function of the existing numeric value.
- [x] Add the frozen tier-function thresholds: `high` if `confidence >= 0.85`, `low` if `confidence < 0.6`, `medium` if `0.6 <= confidence < 0.85`, `unknown` if `confidence` is `null`, `undefined`, missing, non-numeric, `NaN`, `+Infinity`, `-Infinity`, or outside the `[0, 1]` range. The thresholds (`0.85` and `0.6`) are PM-frozen and are immutable once M36 ships; any change to either threshold is a material governance event under its own ROADMAP milestone. Out-of-range or non-numeric values are bucketed as `unknown` rather than silently coerced; in human mode each such case writes a `Warning: confidence out of [0,1] range for capability <name>: <value>` (or `Warning: confidence missing or non-numeric for capability <name>`) line to stderr per occurrence; in `--json` mode the warnings appear in a top-level `warnings[]` array (string entries; preserved across runs for determinism).
- [x] Add the frozen two-value `aggregation_key` enum: `tier | unknown` (parallel to M31's `domain | unknown`, M32's `class | unknown`, M33's `class | unknown`, M34's `method | unknown`, M35's `scheme | unknown`). The enum is immutable once M36 ships; any addition is a material governance event under its own ROADMAP milestone with a fresh re-approval expectation. The `unknown` aggregation-key marks the zero-evidence bucket; the `tier` aggregation-key marks every other bucket (`high`/`medium`/`low`).
- [x] Default behavior: `tusq confidence index` (no `--tier`) emits one entry per distinct `confidence_tier` value present in the manifest's `capabilities[]`, in the **closed enum order** `high → medium → low` (NOT confidence-numeric-descending — the closed enum imposes a deterministic global order; M31's first-appearance rule applies to open-string `domain` values, not to closed enums; mirroring M32 / M33 / M34 / M35 closed-enum order conventions). The `unknown` bucket (if any capability has out-of-range or non-numeric `confidence`) is appended last. Empty buckets MUST NOT appear (a `high` bucket appears only if at least one capability has `confidence >= 0.85`). The `--tier <value>` flag limits output to a single bucket (string match against one of the four enum values: `high`, `medium`, `low`, `unknown`); an unrecognized filter value exits 1 with `Unknown confidence tier:` followed by the value, empty stdout. Filter matching is **case-sensitive** lowercase only (mirroring the M35 `--scheme` precedent); uppercase values like `HIGH` exit 1 (rather than being lower-cased silently) so reviewer scripts cannot accidentally drift from the canonical lowercase form.
- [x] Per-bucket index entry shape (deterministic JSON under `--json`):
  - `confidence_tier`: string (one of `"high"`, `"medium"`, `"low"`, or the literal `"unknown"`)
  - `aggregation_key`: one of the two enum values (`"tier"` or `"unknown"`)
  - `capability_count`: integer (number of capabilities in this bucket)
  - `capabilities[]`: array of capability names (strings) in manifest declared order
  - `approved_count`: integer (number of capabilities in this bucket where `approved === true`)
  - `gated_count`: integer (`capability_count - approved_count`)
  - `has_destructive_side_effect`: boolean (true iff any capability in this bucket has `side_effect_class === "destructive"`)
  - `has_restricted_or_confidential_sensitivity`: boolean (true iff any capability in this bucket has `sensitivity_class === "restricted"` OR `sensitivity_class === "confidential"`)
  - top-level `manifest_path`, `manifest_version`, `generated_at` copied verbatim from the input manifest (with the M27 fallback: `null` in `--json` mode and `unknown` in human mode when the manifest lacks the field)
  - top-level `warnings[]` (only present in `--json` mode; always present even when empty `[]` for shape stability) listing any per-capability `Warning: confidence out of [0,1] range ...` or `Warning: confidence missing or non-numeric ...` entries in manifest declared order
  - **deliberately omitted** (parallel to M31 / M32 / M33 / M34 / M35 omissions): no `domains_represented[]`, no `auth_schemes_represented[]`, no `methods_represented[]`, no `side_effect_classes_represented[]`, no `sensitivity_classes_represented[]`, no `pii_categories_represented[]`, no derived `risk_tier`, no derived `iam_posture`, no `confidence_min`/`confidence_max`/`confidence_mean`/`confidence_distribution[]`. Cross-axis roll-ups and statistical aggregation belong in their own future M-Risk-1 / M-Confidence-Statistics-1 milestones with fresh acceptance contracts.
- [x] Read-only invariants (mirroring M27 Constraint 20 / M28 Constraint 21 / M29 Constraint 22 / M30 Constraint 23 / M31 Constraint 24 / M32 Constraint 25 / M33 Constraint 26 / M34 Constraint 27 / M35 Constraint 28):
  - `tusq.manifest.json` mtime/content unchanged after every `tusq confidence index` invocation (smoke assertion)
  - No write to `.tusq/`; no write to any path other than `--out <path>` when supplied (smoke assertion)
  - `capability_digest` MUST NOT flip on any capability (smoke assertion: hash before vs after is byte-identical)
  - `confidence_tier` is NOT persisted into the manifest (smoke assertion: post-run manifest JSON does NOT contain a `confidence_tier` key on any capability)
  - `tusq compile` output is byte-identical pre and post-M36 for every fixture (golden-file smoke assertion)
  - `tusq serve` `tools/list` and `tools/call` and `dry_run_plan` responses are byte-identical pre and post-M36 (golden-file smoke assertion)
  - `tusq policy verify` (default and `--strict`), `tusq redaction review`, `tusq surface plan`, `tusq domain index`, `tusq effect index`, `tusq sensitivity index`, `tusq method index`, and `tusq auth index` are byte-identical pre and post-M36
- [x] Deterministic output: running `tusq confidence index` twice on the same manifest MUST produce byte-identical stdout in both human and `--json` modes; bucket iteration order is fixed by the closed enum (`high → medium → low`, then `unknown` last); within each bucket, capabilities iterate in manifest declared order; no wall-clock fields inside per-bucket entries; top-level `generated_at` is copy-forward from the manifest, never re-stamped; `warnings[]` ordering is stable per manifest declared order.
- [x] Empty-capabilities valid-exit-0 rule (mirroring M27/M30/M31/M32/M33/M34/M35): when `capabilities: []` is a valid empty array, the command MUST exit 0 in both default and `--json` modes; human mode emits the single explicit line `No capabilities in manifest — nothing to index.` to stdout (no bucket section, no warnings); `--json` mode emits `{manifest_path, manifest_version, generated_at, tiers: [], warnings: []}` with the top-level fields copied verbatim. This is distinct from a missing/non-array `capabilities` (exit 1 with `Invalid manifest: missing capabilities array`).
- [x] I/O stream discipline (mirroring M27/M30/M31/M32/M33/M34/M35): every error message path (`Manifest not found:`, `Invalid manifest JSON:`, `Invalid manifest: missing capabilities array`, `Unknown confidence tier:`, `Unknown subcommand:`, `Unknown flag:`, `Cannot write to --out path:`) writes exclusively to stderr; stdout MUST be empty on every exit-1 path (no partial index, no JSON object with an `error` field, no trailing newline). Per-capability `Warning: confidence ...` lines also write to stderr (NOT stdout) in human mode; in `--json` mode they appear in the top-level `warnings[]` array of the stdout JSON. Smoke assertion captures both streams and verifies `stdout === ""` on every error case.
- [x] `--help` prints the M36 command shape, the four-value `confidence_tier` bucket-key enum, the two-value `aggregation_key` enum, the frozen tier-function thresholds (`high >= 0.85`, `low < 0.6`, `medium` otherwise, `unknown` if missing/non-numeric/out-of-range), the four flags (`--tier`, `--manifest`, `--out`, `--json`), exit codes, and an explicit "This is a planning aid, not a runtime confidence gate, evidence-quality scoring engine, or automated re-classifier; confidence is reviewer-aid metadata, not runtime enforcement" callout; help text is byte-identical across runs.
- [x] `--out <path>`: when supplied, writes the index output (human or JSON depending on `--json`) to the path and emits no stdout on success; if the path is unwritable, exits 1 with `Cannot write to --out path:` followed by the path on stderr and empty stdout. The path MUST NOT be inside `.tusq/`; an attempt to write inside `.tusq/` exits 1 with `--out path must not be inside .tusq/` on stderr (mirroring M30/M31/M32/M33/M34/M35).
- [x] Update `tusq help` to add the `confidence` noun and the `index` subcommand exactly once; the `confidence` line is inserted alphabetically between `auth` and `diff` in the help enumeration so the help block remains stably ordered (alphabetical position: `... approve, auth, confidence, diff, domain, effect, method, policy, redaction, sensitivity, surface, version, help`).
- [x] Add smoke coverage for: (a) default `tusq confidence index` on a manifest with mixed high/medium/low/unknown-confidence capabilities produces exit 0 and the expected per-bucket entries in closed-enum order; (b) `--tier high` / `--tier medium` / `--tier low` / `--tier unknown` each emit exactly one matching entry; (c) `--tier bogus` exits 1 with `Unknown confidence tier:` and empty stdout; (c2) `--tier HIGH` (uppercase) exits 1 with `Unknown confidence tier:` and empty stdout (case-sensitive enforcement); (d) missing `--manifest` path exits 1 with `Manifest not found:`; (e) malformed-JSON manifest exits 1 with `Invalid manifest JSON:` before any stdout; (f) running twice produces byte-identical stdout in both modes; (g) M36 does not mutate the manifest (mtime/content unchanged); (h) `capability_digest` does not flip on any capability after an index run (asserted by hash compare); (h2) post-run manifest does NOT contain a `confidence_tier` key on any capability (non-persistence assertion); (i) `tusq compile` golden-file output is byte-identical pre and post-M36; (j) `tusq serve tools/list` golden-file output is byte-identical; (k) `tusq surface plan`, `tusq domain index`, `tusq effect index`, `tusq sensitivity index`, `tusq method index`, and `tusq auth index` outputs are byte-identical pre and post-M36; (l) empty-capabilities manifest emits the documented human line and `tiers: []` JSON; (m) `--out <path>` writes to the path and emits no stdout on success; (n) `--out` to an unwritable path exits 1; (o) `--out .tusq/anything.json` exits 1 with `--out path must not be inside .tusq/` on stderr; (p) capability with `confidence: null` (or missing/`undefined`/non-numeric `confidence`) is bucketed into `unknown` and the `unknown` bucket appears last; (p2) capability with `confidence: 1.5` (out-of-range) is bucketed into `unknown` and a `Warning: confidence out of [0,1] range ...` line appears on stderr (human) or in `warnings[]` (`--json`); (p3) capability with `confidence: NaN` is bucketed into `unknown` with the missing-or-non-numeric warning; (q) `aggregation_key` is exactly one of the two closed values for every emitted bucket; (r) empty buckets (e.g., manifest has only high-confidence capabilities) MUST NOT appear in output; (s) within each bucket, capability names appear in manifest declared order (NOT alphabetized, NOT confidence-descending); (t) `has_destructive_side_effect` flag is true iff at least one capability in bucket has `side_effect_class === "destructive"` (asserted on a fixture with mixed side-effect values); (u) `has_restricted_or_confidential_sensitivity` flag is true iff at least one capability in bucket has `sensitivity_class === "restricted"` or `sensitivity_class === "confidential"` (asserted on a fixture with mixed sensitivity values); (v) boundary-value smoke: capability with `confidence: 0.85` (exact-boundary) is bucketed `high`; `0.84999...` is `medium`; `0.6` (exact-boundary) is `medium`; `0.59999...` is `low`; `0` is `low`; `1` is `high` — asserted on a synthetic-capability eval fixture (the boundary inclusive/exclusive contract is `>= 0.85` and `>= 0.6`).
- [x] Add one eval regression scenario `confidence-tier-index-determinism` to `tests/evals/governed-cli-scenarios.json` asserting that `tusq confidence index --json` produces byte-identical stdout across three runs on the same manifest, that the `confidence_tier` bucket-key enum is closed (every bucket's value is one of the four values: `high`/`medium`/`low`/`unknown`), that the `aggregation_key` enum is closed (every bucket's value is one of the two values), that bucket iteration order is the frozen closed-enum order (`high → medium → low`, then `unknown`), and that the `warnings[]` array is preserved byte-identically across runs. Total eval scenarios become **≥27** (current 26 + 1 new).
- [x] Add Constraint 29 to SYSTEM_SPEC.md Constraints section: "`tusq confidence index` is a planning aid that surfaces what evidence-quality tiers the manifest's capabilities span and the cross-axis side-effect/sensitivity exposure of each tier. It does NOT enforce confidence at runtime, does NOT score or re-score evidence quality, does NOT automatically re-classify low-confidence capabilities, does NOT modify the scanner's `confidence` derivation rules (which are set in M14/M15), does NOT persist `confidence_tier` into `tusq.manifest.json`, and does NOT compute statistical aggregates (`min`, `max`, `mean`, percentiles, distributions). Subsequent milestones (M-Risk-1 cross-axis risk-tier roll-up, M-Confidence-Statistics-1 distribution and percentile aggregation, M-Confidence-Persistence-1 if persistence into the manifest is later authorized) ship under their own ROADMAP entries with fresh acceptance contracts and fresh re-approval expectations. The four-value `confidence_tier` bucket-key enum (`high | medium | low | unknown`), the two-value `aggregation_key` enum (`tier | unknown`), and the tier-function thresholds (`high >= 0.85`, `low < 0.6`, `medium` otherwise) are frozen; any addition or threshold change is a material governance event. The `--tier` filter is case-sensitive lowercase-only; uppercase or mixed-case filter values exit 1 with `Unknown confidence tier:`. Out-of-range or non-numeric `confidence` values are bucketed as `unknown` and emit a `Warning: ...` to stderr (human) or `warnings[]` (`--json`); they MUST NOT be silently coerced or clamped."
- [x] Add M36 section to SYSTEM_SPEC.md with: purpose statement, command shape, frozen four-value `confidence_tier` bucket-key enum, frozen two-value `aggregation_key` enum, frozen tier-function thresholds (`>= 0.85` / `>= 0.6` / out-of-range/missing rules), frozen 8-field per-bucket entry shape, top-level `warnings[]` rule, closed-enum bucket iteration order rule (`high → medium → low → unknown`), within-bucket manifest-declared-order rule, case-sensitive `--tier` filter rule, empty-capabilities and stdout-discipline rules, read-only invariants including the explicit non-persistence-of-`confidence_tier` rule, and the explicit non-runtime-gate/non-quality-engine/non-reclassifier boundary statement.

### M37: Static Capability PII Field Count Tier Index Export from Manifest Evidence (~0.5 day) — V1.18 (PROPOSED)

> Charter origin: bound 2026-04-27 in `run_0b366d58febc99be` (`turn_741c43114034bab7`, PM attempt 1) at HEAD `f2a153b` from intake charter `intent_1777286540380_ef16` (vision_scan, category `roadmap_exhausted_vision_open`, charter "Derive next bounded roadmap increment from VISION.md. Candidate pool: The Promise, Code And API Surface, Database, Warehouse, And Data Model, Frontend, Design System, And Product UX, Domain Model And Workflows (+25 more). Current roadmap checked through M36: Static Capability Confidence Tier Index Export from Manifest Evidence (~0.5 day) — V1.17 (SHIPPED)."). VISION sources cited:
> - **`.planning/VISION.md` lines 705–707 (`### Data Leakage` under § Risks)** — has NOT been the primary aggregation-axis source for any shipped milestone. The section says "Runtime traces, support tickets, docs, and databases can contain customer secrets. Imports must minimize raw value capture, redact aggressively, preserve provenance, and make unsafe source handling visible." The per-`pii_field_count_tier` capability roll-up is the smallest reviewer-aid that lets an operator see, at a glance, "how many of my capabilities have zero PII field hints, how many have light (1–2), moderate (3–5), or heavy (6+) PII field hints — and which heavy buckets also contain destructive-side-effect or restricted-sensitivity capabilities" — the highest-attention reviewer combination this milestone exposes.
> - **`.planning/VISION.md` lines 108–114 (`### Data, Risk, And Sensitivity`)** — re-cited (cited previously by M28, M33 for sensitivity-class derivation and aggregation; M37 cites it for the cross-axis flag justification only — `has_destructive_side_effect` and `has_restricted_or_confidential_sensitivity` flags per PII tier bucket are particularly meaningful for the `high` and `medium` PII tiers and the `unknown` (malformed) bucket).
>
> Shipped reality M1–M36 covers the compiler/governance half plus the M27 redaction-review reviewer-aid, the M30 surface-plan planner, the M31 per-domain index, the M32 per-side-effect-class index, the M33 per-sensitivity-class index, the M34 per-HTTP-method index, the M35 per-auth-scheme index, and the M36 per-confidence-tier index. The per-`pii_field_count_tier` capability index — the parallel reviewer-aid that buckets capabilities by an evidence-volume tier derived from the manifest's existing per-capability `pii_fields[]` array length (set by the scanner at M25) — has not shipped. The scanner emits `pii_fields[]` as an array of source-literal name hints, but no shipped command aggregates capabilities into a per-volume-tier roll-up; reviewers asking "how many capabilities have heavy PII exposure (≥6 hint fields) and what is their cross-axis side-effect/sensitivity exposure?" must currently re-run `tusq redaction review` per capability and manually count. M37 is the smallest first increment that addresses the PII-volume-distribution dimension of VISION § Data Leakage **without** committing the project to runtime PII detection, runtime data-leakage prevention, GDPR/HIPAA/PCI/PHI compliance certification, runtime field redaction enforcement, alteration of M25's canonical PII name set or `pii_fields[]` extraction rules, or persistence of `pii_field_count_tier` into the manifest itself (M37 derives the tier on-the-fly inside the index command from the existing `pii_fields[]` array length; the tier is reviewer-aid metadata only and is intentionally NOT persisted into `tusq.manifest.json`). Scope decision resolved this turn: M37 introduces a new top-level noun `pii` with a single subcommand `index` (mirroring the M27 `redaction review`, M30 `surface plan`, M31 `domain index`, M32 `effect index`, M33 `sensitivity index`, M34 `method index`, M35 `auth index`, and M36 `confidence index` precedents). The CLI surface grows from 20 → 21 commands with `pii` inserted alphabetically between `method` and `policy` in the alphabetic block (`method` vs `pii`: `m` < `p`; `pii` vs `policy`: `pi` < `po` because `i` < `o`). The mutually exclusive alternative forms are explicitly rejected for V1.18: `pii-volume` and `pii-fields` introduce a hyphenated-noun pattern that no other tusq noun uses (rejected per M33 precedent); `leakage` overscopes the milestone (leakage includes runtime trace handling, log redaction, and database-egress filtering); an `--by` axis flag would couple multiple aggregation modes into one command and violate the M27/M30/M31/M32/M33/M34/M35/M36 single-aggregation-axis precedent; extending `tusq redaction review` with a tier filter would conflate per-capability filter output with per-bucket roll-up output. The closed five-value `pii_field_count_tier` bucket-key enum (`none | low | medium | high | unknown`) is M37-defined (NOT pre-existing in the manifest like M35's `auth_scheme` from M29 — `pii_fields[]` is a string array, the tier is a derived bucket-key); the tier function is frozen at planning time and is a pure function of the manifest's per-capability `pii_fields[]` array length: `none if pii_fields.length === 0`, `low if 1 <= length <= 2`, `medium if 3 <= length <= 5`, `high if length >= 6`, `unknown if pii_fields is null/undefined/missing/not-an-array OR contains any non-string element OR contains the empty string` (the last condition catches scanner regressions or hand-edited manifests; malformed values are bucketed as `unknown` rather than silently coerced; in human mode each such case writes a `Warning: pii_fields malformed for capability <name>: <reason>` line to stderr and in `--json` mode appears in `warnings[]`). Boundaries `0/2/5/6` are PM-frozen at M37 ship; any change to any threshold or to the five-value enum is a material governance event under its own ROADMAP milestone with a fresh re-approval expectation. The closed two-value `aggregation_key` enum is `tier | unknown` (parallel to M31 `domain | unknown`, M32 `class | unknown`, M33 `class | unknown`, M34 `method | unknown`, M35 `scheme | unknown`, M36 `tier | unknown`). The frozen 8-field per-bucket entry shape (`pii_field_count_tier`, `aggregation_key`, `capability_count`, `capabilities[]`, `approved_count`, `gated_count`, `has_destructive_side_effect`, `has_restricted_or_confidential_sensitivity`) is intentionally name-and-counters-only and intentionally **omits** cross-axis roll-up arrays and **omits** any derived `risk_tier`, `pii_field_count_min`, `pii_field_count_max`, `pii_field_count_mean`, or `pii_categories_represented[]` — all reserved for the deferred M-PII-Category-Index-1 / M-Risk-1 / M-PII-Statistics-1 milestones with their own enums, their own acceptance contracts, and their own re-approval expectations. Bucket iteration order is the **closed-enum order** `none → low → medium → high → unknown` (NOT count-numeric-ascending — the closed-enum order is a deterministic stable-output convention only and MUST NOT be described as "PII-exposure-ranked," "data-leakage-ranked," "redaction-priority-ordered," or any phrase implying a leakage-risk semantic; the operative reading is "default reading order none→high with `unknown` last"; the `unknown` bucket is appended last, mirroring M32/M33/M34/M35/M36). Within each bucket, capability names follow manifest declared order (mirroring M31/M32/M33/M34/M35/M36 within-bucket ordering). Empty buckets MUST NOT appear (a `high` bucket appears only if at least one capability has `pii_fields.length >= 6`). Read-only invariants mirror M27/M28/M29/M30/M31/M32/M33/M34/M35/M36: zero manifest mutation, zero `capability_digest` flips, zero new dependency in `package.json`, byte-identical output for every other command pre and post-M37. Empty-capabilities exits 0 with `No capabilities in manifest — nothing to index.` (human) and `{ manifest_path, manifest_version, generated_at, tiers: [], warnings: [] }` (`--json`); every error path empties stdout and writes exclusively to stderr. The `--out <path>` flag rejects any path resolving inside `.tusq/`. The `--tier <value>` filter limits output to a single bucket (string match against one of the five enum values: `none`, `low`, `medium`, `high`, `unknown`); an unrecognized filter value exits 1 with `Unknown pii field count tier:` followed by the value, empty stdout. Filter matching is **case-sensitive** lowercase only; uppercase values like `HIGH` exit 1 (rather than being lower-cased silently) so reviewer scripts cannot accidentally drift from the canonical lowercase form. Eval regression scenario `pii-field-count-tier-index-determinism` brings the harness from 27 → **≥28** scenarios. Constraint 30 (proposed) codifies the planning-aid framing. Six Key Risk rows added. The deferred successor milestones (M-PII-Category-Index-1 multi-valued aggregation by individual PII category, M-Risk-1 cross-axis risk tier, M-PII-Statistics-1 distribution roll-up, M-PII-Persistence-1 if persistence is later authorized) ship under their own ROADMAP entries with fresh acceptance contracts.
>
> **Acceptance contract response (charter line by line):**

- [x] Add new top-level noun `pii` with single subcommand `index` to the CLI surface; `tusq pii` (no subcommand) prints a short enumerate-subcommands block identical in shape to `tusq method`, `tusq sensitivity`, `tusq effect`, `tusq surface`, `tusq policy`, `tusq redaction`, `tusq domain`, `tusq auth`, and `tusq confidence`; unknown subcommands exit 1 with `Unknown subcommand:` followed by the name and empty stdout. CLI surface grows from 20 commands to **21** (init, scan, manifest, compile, serve, review, docs, approve, auth, confidence, diff, domain, effect, method, **pii**, policy, redaction, sensitivity, surface, version, help) with `pii` inserted alphabetically between `method` and `policy` (`method` vs `pii`: `m` < `p`; `pii` vs `policy`: `pi` < `po` because `i` < `o`). The alphabetic insertion rule applies inside the planning-aid block, not the top-of-help operational block.
- [x] Implement `tusq pii index` as a pure read-only deterministic command that reads the manifest path and writes only to stdout/stderr (or to `--out <path>` if supplied); no network I/O, no `.tusq/` write, no manifest mutation, no `tusq compile`/`tusq serve`/`tusq policy verify`/`tusq redaction review`/`tusq surface plan`/`tusq domain index`/`tusq effect index`/`tusq sensitivity index`/`tusq method index`/`tusq auth index`/`tusq confidence index` behavior change.
- [x] Add the frozen five-value `pii_field_count_tier` bucket-key enum: `none | low | medium | high | unknown`. The enum is immutable once M37 ships; any addition is a material governance event under its own ROADMAP milestone. The five values are named explicitly in `src/cli.js` as a frozen `Object.freeze(['none', 'low', 'medium', 'high'])` array (the named-four) plus the catchall `unknown` appended last by the bucket-iteration logic; the tier is derived at index-time from the manifest's per-capability `pii_fields[]` array length and is intentionally NOT persisted into `tusq.manifest.json` (M37 is reviewer-aid metadata only; persistence is deferred to a future M-PII-Persistence-1 milestone). M37 MUST NOT modify, override, or augment M25's canonical PII name set or `pii_fields[]` extraction rules; the tier is a pure function of the existing array length.
- [x] Add the frozen tier-function thresholds: `none if pii_fields.length === 0`; `low if 1 <= pii_fields.length <= 2`; `medium if 3 <= pii_fields.length <= 5`; `high if pii_fields.length >= 6`; `unknown if pii_fields is null`, `undefined`, missing, not an array, contains any non-string element, or contains the empty string. The thresholds (`0`, `2`, `5`, `6`) are PM-frozen and immutable once M37 ships; any change is a material governance event under its own ROADMAP milestone. Malformed values are bucketed as `unknown` rather than silently coerced; in human mode each such case writes a `Warning: pii_fields malformed for capability <name>: <reason>` line to stderr per occurrence; in `--json` mode the warnings appear in a top-level `warnings[]` array (string entries; preserved across runs for determinism).
- [x] Add the frozen two-value `aggregation_key` enum: `tier | unknown` (parallel to M31's `domain | unknown`, M32's `class | unknown`, M33's `class | unknown`, M34's `method | unknown`, M35's `scheme | unknown`, M36's `tier | unknown`). The enum is immutable once M37 ships; any addition is a material governance event under its own ROADMAP milestone. The `unknown` aggregation-key marks the malformed/zero-evidence bucket; the `tier` aggregation-key marks every other bucket (`none`/`low`/`medium`/`high`).
- [x] Default behavior: `tusq pii index` (no `--tier`) emits one entry per distinct `pii_field_count_tier` value present in the manifest's `capabilities[]`, in the **closed enum order** `none → low → medium → high` (NOT count-numeric-ascending — the closed enum imposes a deterministic global order; mirroring M32/M33/M34/M35/M36 closed-enum order conventions). The `unknown` bucket (if any capability has malformed `pii_fields`) is appended last. Empty buckets MUST NOT appear (a `high` bucket appears only if at least one capability has `pii_fields.length >= 6`). The `--tier <value>` flag limits output to a single bucket (string match against one of the five enum values); an unrecognized filter value exits 1 with `Unknown pii field count tier:` followed by the value, empty stdout. Filter matching is **case-sensitive** lowercase only (mirroring the M35/M36 precedent); uppercase values like `HIGH` exit 1.
- [x] Per-bucket index entry shape (deterministic JSON under `--json`):
  - `pii_field_count_tier`: string (one of `"none"`, `"low"`, `"medium"`, `"high"`, or the literal `"unknown"`)
  - `aggregation_key`: one of the two enum values (`"tier"` or `"unknown"`)
  - `capability_count`: integer (number of capabilities in this bucket)
  - `capabilities[]`: array of capability names (strings) in manifest declared order
  - `approved_count`: integer (number of capabilities in this bucket where `approved === true`)
  - `gated_count`: integer (`capability_count - approved_count`)
  - `has_destructive_side_effect`: boolean (true iff any capability in this bucket has `side_effect_class === "destructive"`)
  - `has_restricted_or_confidential_sensitivity`: boolean (true iff any capability in this bucket has `sensitivity_class === "restricted"` OR `sensitivity_class === "confidential"`)
  - top-level `manifest_path`, `manifest_version`, `generated_at` copied verbatim from the input manifest (with the M27 fallback for missing fields)
  - top-level `warnings[]` (only present in `--json` mode; always present even when empty `[]` for shape stability) listing any per-capability malformed-pii_fields warnings in manifest declared order
  - **deliberately omitted** (parallel to M31/M32/M33/M34/M35/M36 omissions): no `domains_represented[]`, no `auth_schemes_represented[]`, no `methods_represented[]`, no `side_effect_classes_represented[]`, no `sensitivity_classes_represented[]`, no `pii_categories_represented[]`, no derived `risk_tier`, no `pii_field_count_min`/`max`/`mean`/`distribution[]`. Cross-axis roll-ups, multi-valued PII-category aggregation, and statistical aggregation belong in their own future M-PII-Category-Index-1 / M-Risk-1 / M-PII-Statistics-1 milestones with fresh acceptance contracts.
- [x] Read-only invariants (mirroring M27 Constraint 20 / M28 Constraint 21 / M29 Constraint 22 / M30 Constraint 23 / M31 Constraint 24 / M32 Constraint 25 / M33 Constraint 26 / M34 Constraint 27 / M35 Constraint 28 / M36 Constraint 29):
  - `tusq.manifest.json` mtime/content unchanged after every `tusq pii index` invocation (smoke assertion)
  - No write to `.tusq/`; no write to any path other than `--out <path>` when supplied (smoke assertion)
  - `capability_digest` MUST NOT flip on any capability (smoke assertion: hash before vs after is byte-identical)
  - `pii_field_count_tier` is NOT persisted into the manifest (smoke assertion: post-run manifest JSON does NOT contain a `pii_field_count_tier` key on any capability)
  - `tusq compile` output is byte-identical pre and post-M37 for every fixture (golden-file smoke assertion)
  - `tusq serve` `tools/list` and `tools/call` and `dry_run_plan` responses are byte-identical pre and post-M37 (golden-file smoke assertion)
  - `tusq policy verify` (default and `--strict`), `tusq redaction review`, `tusq surface plan`, `tusq domain index`, `tusq effect index`, `tusq sensitivity index`, `tusq method index`, `tusq auth index`, and `tusq confidence index` are byte-identical pre and post-M37
- [x] Deterministic output: running `tusq pii index` twice on the same manifest MUST produce byte-identical stdout in both human and `--json` modes; bucket iteration order is fixed by the closed enum (`none → low → medium → high`, then `unknown` last); within each bucket, capabilities iterate in manifest declared order; no wall-clock fields inside per-bucket entries; top-level `generated_at` is copy-forward from the manifest, never re-stamped; `warnings[]` ordering is stable per manifest declared order.
- [x] Empty-capabilities valid-exit-0 rule (mirroring M27/M30/M31/M32/M33/M34/M35/M36): when `capabilities: []` is a valid empty array, the command MUST exit 0 in both default and `--json` modes; human mode emits the single explicit line `No capabilities in manifest — nothing to index.` to stdout (no bucket section, no warnings); `--json` mode emits `{manifest_path, manifest_version, generated_at, tiers: [], warnings: []}` with the top-level fields copied verbatim. This is distinct from a missing/non-array `capabilities` (exit 1 with `Invalid manifest: missing capabilities array`).
- [x] I/O stream discipline (mirroring M27/M30/M31/M32/M33/M34/M35/M36): every error message path (`Manifest not found:`, `Invalid manifest JSON:`, `Invalid manifest: missing capabilities array`, `Unknown pii field count tier:`, `Unknown subcommand:`, `Unknown flag:`, `Cannot write to --out path:`) writes exclusively to stderr; stdout MUST be empty on every exit-1 path (no partial index, no JSON object with an `error` field, no trailing newline). Per-capability `Warning: pii_fields malformed ...` lines also write to stderr (NOT stdout) in human mode; in `--json` mode they appear in the top-level `warnings[]` array of the stdout JSON. Smoke assertion captures both streams and verifies `stdout === ""` on every error case.

> - **`.planning/VISION.md` lines 697–699 (`### Bad Workflow Inference` under § Risks We Guard Against)** — has NOT been the primary aggregation-axis source for any shipped milestone. The section says "Inferred workflows can look plausible while violating real business rules. Workflow artifacts must be explicit, editable, provenance-backed, and eval-tested." The per-`examples_count_tier` capability roll-up is the smallest reviewer-aid that lets an operator see, at a glance, "how many of my capabilities have zero example seeds (untested), how many have light (1–2) coverage, moderate (3–5), or thorough (6+) — and which untested or light-coverage buckets also contain destructive-side-effect or restricted-sensitivity capabilities" — the highest-attention reviewer combination this milestone exposes (an untested destructive capability is the canonical "plausible workflow violating real rules" case the section warns against).
> - **`.planning/VISION.md` lines 40–46 (`### Code And API Surface`)** — re-cited (cited previously by M30/M34 for surface plan/method derivation; M38 cites it for the examples-as-eval-seed framing only — `examples[]` originates as a manifest field populated alongside the capability's input/output schema during scan/compile and represents the eval-test surface, distinct from the runtime-execution surface).
>
> Charter Bound (PM-frozen scope decisions; dev MUST carry these forward verbatim):
> - **Bucket-key enum** (closed five-value): `none | low | medium | high | unknown`. No additional values may be introduced (e.g., `excellent`, `unverified`, `partial`) without a separate ROADMAP milestone.
> - **Aggregation key enum** (closed two-value): `tier | unknown`. Mirrors M31/M32/M33/M34/M35/M36/M37.
> - **Tier function** (frozen on the manifest's per-capability `examples[]` array length):
>   - `none` if `examples.length === 0`
>   - `low` if `1 <= examples.length <= 2`
>   - `medium` if `3 <= examples.length <= 5`
>   - `high` if `examples.length >= 6`
>   - `unknown` if `examples` is `null`/`undefined`/missing/not-an-array OR contains any non-object element OR contains a `null` element OR contains an array element
>   - Boundaries `0/2/5/6` are immutable post-ship; tier function is a pure ternary expression on `examples.length`.
> - **Per-bucket entry shape** (frozen 8 fields): `examples_count_tier`, `aggregation_key`, `capability_count`, `capabilities[]`, `approved_count`, `gated_count`, `has_destructive_side_effect`, `has_restricted_or_confidential_sensitivity`. Order matches M31–M37 precedent.
> - **Top-level `warnings[]`** array: present only in `--json` mode; always emitted (even when empty `[]`) for shape stability; per-capability malformed-`examples` warnings carried byte-identically across runs.
> - **Bucket iteration order** (closed-enum, deterministic stable-output convention only — explicitly NOT a coverage-quality-precedence, NOT a test-strength ranking, NOT a confidence-equivalent): `none → low → medium → high → unknown`. The order MUST NOT be described as "test-coverage-ranked," "completeness-ranked," or "highest-coverage-first." Empty buckets MUST NOT appear.
> - **Within-bucket order**: manifest declared order (capabilities[] index ascending).
> - **`--tier` filter**: case-sensitive lowercase-only; uppercase or mixed-case values like `HIGH` exit 1 with stderr `Unknown examples count tier: HIGH` and empty stdout (mirrors M35/M36/M37 case-sensitivity precedent). Filtering on a tier with zero capabilities exits 1 with stderr `No capabilities found for examples count tier: <tier>`.
> - **Read-only invariants** (mirrors § M32/M33/M34/M35/M36/M37): manifest mtime + SHA-256 + every capability's `capability_digest` byte-identical pre/post; `tusq compile` output byte-identical pre/post; `tusq surface plan`, `tusq domain index`, `tusq effect index`, `tusq sensitivity index`, `tusq method index`, `tusq auth index`, `tusq confidence index`, `tusq pii index` all byte-identical pre/post.
> - **Non-persistence rule**: `examples_count_tier` MUST NOT be written into `tusq.manifest.json` — it is reviewer-aid metadata only.
> - **CLI surface growth**: 21 → 22 commands. New top-level noun `examples` with single subcommand `index`, inserted alphabetically between `effect` and `help` (`effect` vs `examples`: `eff` < `exa` because second-char `f` > `x`? No — `e` = `e`; second char `f` vs `x` — wait `f` < `x` so `effect` < `examples` is correct). Insertion sequence: ..., `effect`, `examples`, `help`, `method`, ... Actually full surface order alphabetical: `approve`, `auth`, `compile`, `confidence`, `diff`, `docs`, `domain`, `effect`, **`examples`**, `help`, `init`, `manifest`, `method`, `pii`, `policy`, `redaction`, `review`, `scan`, `sensitivity`, `serve`, `surface`, `version`. Note: in `printHelp()`/`tusq help` the existing display order is the full 21 cli surface order (init, scan, manifest, compile, serve, review, docs, approve, auth, confidence, diff, domain, effect, method, pii, policy, redaction, sensitivity, surface, version, help) — `examples` is inserted between `effect` and `method` (`effect` < `examples` < `method` alphabetically).
> - **Eval scenario**: `examples-count-tier-index-determinism` added; eval harness 28 → ≥29 scenarios.
> - **Constraint 31** to be added in SYSTEM_SPEC § Constraints freezing: M38 is a planning aid that reports per-capability example-seed cardinality tiers; it does NOT execute examples, does NOT validate example schema-conformance, does NOT generate new examples, does NOT measure runtime test-coverage, does NOT certify eval-readiness.
> - **Deferred successor milestones**: `M-Examples-Schema-Validation-1` (per-example schema conformance check), `M-Examples-Coverage-Statistics-1` (mean/median/percentile distribution of example counts), `M-Examples-Persistence-1` (if persistence is later authorized), `M-Examples-Generation-1` (auto-generate example seeds).

- [ ] Add `EXAMPLES_COUNT_TIER_ENUM` (frozen `Set` of `none | low | medium | high | unknown`), `EXAMPLES_COUNT_TIER_AGGREGATION_KEY_ENUM` (frozen `Set` of `tier | unknown`), and `EXAMPLES_COUNT_TIER_BUCKET_ORDER` (frozen `Object.freeze([...])` with literal closed-enum order `none → low → medium → high`, with `unknown` appended only when present) constants in `src/cli.js` near the existing M37 PII tier constants. Add synchronous module-init guards `_guardExamplesCountTierBucketKey` and `_guardExamplesCountTierAggregationKey` mirroring M35 `_guardAuthSchemeBucketAlignment` / M36 `_guardConfidenceTierBucketKey` / M37 `_guardPiiFieldCountTierBucketKey` precedent — the IIFE must throw a descriptive `Error` synchronously at module load if the bucket-order array elements diverge from the enum set or if the enum set is missing required values.
- [ ] Add `classifyExamplesCountTier(examples)` pure function (no manifest mutation, no `capability_digest` recomputation, no I/O). Returns `'unknown'` for `null`/`undefined`/missing/not-an-array AND for arrays containing any element that is not a plain non-null object (i.e., `null`, primitives, arrays, or functions disqualify the array). Returns `'none'` for `length === 0`. Returns `'low'` for `1 <= length <= 2`. Returns `'medium'` for `3 <= length <= 5`. Returns `'high'` for `length >= 6`. Boundaries `0/2/5/6` are immutable.
- [ ] Add `cmdExamples` dispatcher and `cmdExamplesIndex(args)` command handler in `src/cli.js`.
