The handler MUST: (a) call `parseExamplesIndexArgs` first; (b) detect `--out` path validity (rejected: paths under `.tusq/`, paths in non-existent or non-writable parent directories) BEFORE reading the manifest, with stderr `--out path must not be inside .tusq/` or `--out parent directory does not exist or is not writable` and exit 1, empty stdout; (c) read and parse the manifest from `--manifest <path>` (default `tusq.manifest.json` in cwd) with stderr `Manifest file not found: <path>` for missing, `Failed to parse manifest JSON: <message>` for malformed, `Manifest is missing capabilities array` for missing/non-array `capabilities` field, each exit 1 with empty stdout; (d) apply case-sensitive `--tier <value>` filter against the closed five-value enum, with stderr `Unknown examples count tier: <value>` and exit 1 for any value not in `{none, low, medium, high, unknown}`; (e) build the index via `buildExamplesCountTierIndex(manifest)`; (f) emit per-capability malformed warnings to stderr in human mode (one `Warning: capability '<name>' has malformed examples (...)` per malformed capability) and to `warnings[]` in `--json` mode; (g) format via `formatExamplesCountTierIndex` (human) or `JSON.stringify(..., null, 2)` (`--json`).
- [ ] Add `parseExamplesIndexArgs(args)` accepting exactly four flags: `--tier <value>`, `--manifest <path>`, `--out <path>`, `--json`. Reject any unknown flag with stderr `Unknown flag: <flag>` and exit 1, empty stdout. Reject `--tier` with no value (stderr `--tier requires a value`), `--manifest` with no value, `--out` with no value, each exit 1.
- [ ] Add `buildExamplesCountTierIndex(manifest, options = {})` returning `{ manifest_path, manifest_version, generated_at, tiers, warnings }`. Iteration: for each capability in `manifest.capabilities[]` (preserving manifest declared order), compute `tier = classifyExamplesCountTier(capability.examples)`; if tier is `'unknown'`, append a warning entry of the form `{ capability: <name>, reason: 'examples_field_missing' | 'examples_field_not_array' | 'examples_array_contains_non_object_element' | 'examples_array_contains_null_element' | 'examples_array_contains_array_element' }`. Group capabilities by tier, then emit buckets in closed-enum order (`none → low → medium → high`), with `unknown` appended last only if the bucket is non-empty. Empty buckets MUST NOT appear. Each per-bucket entry contains the frozen 8 fields (`examples_count_tier`, `aggregation_key: 'tier'` for known tiers / `'unknown'` for unknown bucket, `capability_count`, `capabilities[]` of capability names in manifest order, `approved_count` (count of `approved === true`), `gated_count` (count of `approved !== true`), `has_destructive_side_effect` (true iff any capability in bucket has `side_effect_class === 'destructive'`), `has_restricted_or_confidential_sensitivity` (true iff any capability in bucket has `sensitivity_class === 'restricted'` or `sensitivity_class === 'confidential'`)). `warnings[]` is always present (empty `[]` when no malformed capabilities) for `--json` shape stability.
- [ ] Add `formatExamplesCountTierIndex(index)` returning a human-readable multi-line string with: `Examples Count Tier Index — <manifest_path>` header; per-bucket section showing `<TIER>: <capability_count> capabilit{y|ies}` followed by indented capability names and `(approved: <n>, gated: <n>, destructive: <yes|no>, restricted_or_confidential: <yes|no>)` summary line; `Planning aid: this index reports per-capability example-seed cardinality tiers; it does NOT execute examples, validate schema-conformance, generate examples, or certify eval-readiness. Tiers are deterministic stable-output ordering only (NOT coverage-quality-ranked).` callout at the bottom; `Tier function: none if examples.length === 0; low if 1-2; medium if 3-5; high if >= 6; unknown if missing/not-array/non-object-element/null-element/array-element.` line; `Bucket order: none → low → medium → high → unknown` line.
- [ ] Wire `examples` into the `dispatch` table in `src/cli.js` between `effect` and `help` (alphabetical). The `examples` enumerator (no subcommand) prints a help block listing `tusq examples index` and exits 0.
- [ ] Update `printHelp()` to emit the 22-command CLI surface (init, scan, manifest, compile, serve, review, docs, approve, auth, confidence, diff, domain, effect, **examples**, method, pii, policy, redaction, sensitivity, surface, version, help) with `examples` inserted between `effect` and `method`.
- [ ] Update `printCommandHelp()` to add `examples` and `examples index` entries with: command shape `tusq examples index [--tier <value>] [--manifest <path>] [--out <path>] [--json]`; the four-flag table; the closed five-value bucket-key enum; the closed two-value aggregation_key enum; the frozen tier-function thresholds; the bucket iteration order; the planning-aid framing callout; the case-sensitive lowercase-only `--tier` rule.
- [ ] Add 24-case smoke matrix to `tests/smoke.mjs` (cases a–x): (a) default closed-enum run on canonical fixture; (b) `--tier none`; (c) `--tier low`; (d) `--tier medium`; (e) `--tier high`; (f) `--tier unknown` with no malformed capabilities (exit 1 `No capabilities found for examples count tier: unknown`); (g) `--tier HIGH` (exit 1, case-sensitive); (h) `--tier xyz` (exit 1, unknown tier); (i) `--manifest <missing>` (exit 1, file not found); (j) `--manifest <malformed.json>` (exit 1, parse error); (k) `--manifest <no-capabilities>` (exit 1, missing capabilities); (l) `--unknown-flag` (exit 1, unknown flag); (m) `--tier` with no value (exit 1); (n) `--out <valid path>` writes correctly and stdout is empty; (o) `--out .tusq/foo.json` (exit 1, must not be inside .tusq/); (p) `--out <unwritable parent>` (exit 1); (q) `--json` outputs valid JSON with `tiers[]` and `warnings: []`; (r) determinism: three consecutive runs produce byte-identical stdout; (s) manifest mtime + SHA-256 + per-capability `capability_digest` invariant pre/post; (t) `examples_count_tier` MUST NOT appear in `tusq.manifest.json` after run (non-persistence); (u) `tusq compile` byte-identical pre/post; (v) `tusq surface plan`, `tusq domain index`, `tusq effect index`, `tusq sensitivity index`, `tusq method index`, `tusq auth index`, `tusq confidence index`, `tusq pii index` all byte-identical pre/post; (w) empty-capabilities exit 0 with stdout `No capabilities in manifest — nothing to index.` (human) or `{ manifest_path, manifest_version, generated_at, tiers: [], warnings: [] }` (`--json`); (x) malformed-examples capability produces stderr `Warning: capability '...' has malformed examples (...)` in human mode and matching `warnings[]` entry in `--json` mode. Update existing M35/M36/M37 help-count assertions from 21 to 22.
- [ ] Add `examples-count-tier-index-determinism` eval scenario to `tests/evals/governed-cli-scenarios.json` (eval count 28 → 29). Add `runExamplesCountTierIndexDeterminismScenario` handler to `tests/eval-regression.mjs` verifying byte-identical output across three runs, closed five-value tier enum, closed two-value aggregation_key enum, tier order determinism, `warnings[]` always present, manifest non-mutation, `examples_count_tier` non-persistence.
- [ ] Update `IMPLEMENTATION_NOTES.md` with this turn's M38 entry (challenge to PM turn, implementation details, verification evidence: `npm test` exit 0 with 29 scenarios, zero new dependencies, zero package drift, 22-command CLI surface confirmed, all M38 invariants verified).
- [ ] Add `### M38` detail block to `SYSTEM_SPEC.md` with: purpose statement, command shape, frozen five-value `examples_count_tier` bucket-key enum, frozen two-value `aggregation_key` enum, frozen tier-function thresholds (`length === 0` / `1-2` / `3-5` / `>= 6` / malformed rules), frozen 8-field per-bucket entry shape, top-level `warnings[]` rule, closed-enum bucket iteration order rule (`none → low → medium → high → unknown`), within-bucket manifest-declared-order rule, case-sensitive `--tier` filter rule, empty-capabilities and stdout-discipline rules, read-only invariants including the explicit non-persistence-of-`examples_count_tier` rule, and the explicit non-runtime-executor/non-schema-validator/non-generator/non-eval-certifier boundary statement.
- [ ] Add `### M38` Product CLI Surface block to `command-surface.md` with the two-row command table, four-flag table, bucket-key enum table, aggregation_key enum table, tier-function thresholds table, per-bucket entry shape table, bucket iteration order table, default-preservation table for the 21 unchanged commands, failure UX table, and local-only invariants table.
- [ ] Add Constraint 31 to SYSTEM_SPEC.md Constraints section: "`tusq examples index` is a planning aid that surfaces what example-cardinality tiers the manifest's capabilities span and the cross-axis side-effect/sensitivity exposure of each tier. It does NOT execute examples at runtime, does NOT validate per-example schema conformance against `input_schema`/`output_schema`, does NOT generate new examples, does NOT measure runtime test coverage, does NOT certify eval-readiness, does NOT alter M11's canonical examples extraction rules, does NOT persist `examples_count_tier` into `tusq.manifest.json`, and does NOT compute statistical aggregates (`min`, `max`, `mean`, percentiles, distributions). Subsequent milestones (M-Examples-Schema-Validation-1 per-example schema conformance check, M-Examples-Coverage-Statistics-1 distribution and percentile aggregation, M-Examples-Persistence-1 if persistence is later authorized, M-Examples-Generation-1 auto-generate example seeds) ship under their own ROADMAP entries with fresh acceptance contracts and fresh re-approval expectations. The five-value `examples_count_tier` bucket-key enum (`none | low | medium | high | unknown`), the two-value `aggregation_key` enum (`tier | unknown`), and the tier-function thresholds (`0`, `2`, `5`, `6`) are frozen; any addition or threshold change is a material governance event. The `--tier` filter is case-sensitive lowercase-only; uppercase or mixed-case filter values exit 1 with `Unknown examples count tier:`. Malformed `examples` arrays are bucketed as `unknown` and emit a `Warning: ...` to stderr (human) or `warnings[]` (`--json`); they MUST NOT be silently coerced or trimmed."
- [ ] Update `website/docs/cli-reference.md` to document the new `tusq examples index` command, the five-value bucket-key enum, the two-value aggregation_key enum, the frozen `0/2/5/6` tier thresholds, the four flags, exit codes, the case-sensitive lowercase-only `--tier` rule, the empty-capabilities behavior, the `warnings[]` rule, and the explicit "planning aid, not a runtime example executor, schema validator, example generator, or eval-readiness certifier" callout.
- [ ] Update `website/docs/manifest-format.md` with an "Examples Count Tier Index" subsection explaining how the manifest's per-capability `examples[]` array (M11-derived) drives per-bucket aggregation through the frozen tier function (`length === 0` → `none`, `1-2` → `low`, `3-5` → `medium`, `>= 6` → `high`, malformed → `unknown`), how malformed values produce a `Warning: ...` rather than silent coercion, that bucket iteration follows the closed-enum order (NOT count-numeric-ascending — explicitly a stable-output convention only), that within each bucket capability names follow manifest declared order, that the `--tier` filter is case-sensitive lowercase-only, that `examples_count_tier` is reviewer-aid metadata only and is NOT persisted into the manifest, and that the examples count tier index is read-only and never mutates the manifest.
- [ ] `npm test` continues to exit 0; no new dependency added to `package.json` (no JSON-schema validator, no eval-runner, no test-coverage library, no statistics library, no histogram library, no example-generation library); 22-command CLI surface preserved exactly (init, scan, manifest, compile, serve, review, docs, approve, auth, confidence, diff, domain, effect, examples, method, pii, policy, redaction, sensitivity, surface, version, help); only the new `tusq examples index` command is added; every existing command's stdout, stderr, and exit code is byte-identical pre and post-M38.

#### M38 Key Risks

| Risk | Impact | Mitigation |
|------|--------|------------|
| `examples_count_tier` accidentally persisted into manifest | Silent revocation of approval across capabilities (digest flip cascade), duplicates M30/M31/M32/M33/M34/M35/M36/M37 manifest-mutation risk | Read-only by design: `cmdExamplesIndex` never calls back into manifest builders or `computeCapabilityDigest`. Smoke test (s) captures manifest mtime + SHA-256 + every capability's `capability_digest` pre/post and asserts byte-identity; smoke test (t) reads manifest after run and asserts no capability has an `examples_count_tier` field. |
| Tier function thresholds get re-tuned post-ship under "feedback" pressure | Operators with frozen reviewer process must re-learn boundaries; downstream tools that hard-code tier semantics (e.g., dashboards filtering on `low` or `none`) silently shift their meaning | Boundaries `0/2/5/6` are PM-frozen at the planning_signoff gate and called out as immutable in this charter, in SYSTEM_SPEC § M38, in `cli-reference.md`, and in `manifest-format.md`. Any post-ship change requires a new ROADMAP milestone with explicit re-approval. |
| Bucket order described as "coverage-quality-ranked" or "test-completeness-ranked" | Reviewers misread the index as a runtime test-coverage gauge or eval-readiness score, leading to false confidence in untested `none`-bucket capabilities and false-pessimism on `high`-bucket capabilities that may have shallow examples | Bucket iteration order is explicitly framed as a deterministic stable-output convention only (NOT coverage-quality-ranked, NOT test-strength-ranked, NOT eval-readiness-ranked); SYSTEM_SPEC § M38 and `manifest-format.md` carry this disclaimer; the `formatExamplesCountTierIndex` callout reinforces "deterministic stable-output ordering only." |
| `--tier` filter silently lower-cases input | Operator typing `--tier HIGH` would unexpectedly succeed and the index output would mislead the operator about the case-sensitivity contract; later operators relying on case-insensitive UX would file bug reports | `--tier` is case-sensitive lowercase-only (mirrors M35 `--scheme`, M36 `--tier`, M37 `--tier`); uppercase or mixed-case values exit 1 with `Unknown examples count tier:`. Smoke case (g) asserts `--tier HIGH` exits 1. |
| Malformed `examples` (e.g., array of strings, array of nulls, `examples: "not-an-array"`) silently coerced to empty array | Operator's actual evidence of malformation gets swallowed; the capability appears in `none` bucket (zero coverage) when in fact the manifest is corrupted; downstream eval-runners hitting the same field would error inconsistently | Malformed `examples` values are bucketed as `unknown` and emit a `Warning: ...` to stderr (human) or `warnings[]` (`--json`); they are NOT silently coerced to `[]`. Smoke case (x) asserts the warning shape; `buildExamplesCountTierIndex` distinguishes five malform reasons (`examples_field_missing`, `examples_field_not_array`, `examples_array_contains_non_object_element`, `examples_array_contains_null_element`, `examples_array_contains_array_element`). |
| CLI surface alphabetical-insertion miscalculation | `examples` inserted in the wrong position between commands would break `printHelp()` byte-identity for the existing 21-command surface and produce noise in user-facing help output | Alphabetical insertion verified: `effect` < `examples` (`e` = `e`, `f` < `x` because `f` (102) < `x` (120) in ASCII); `examples` < `method` (`e` < `m`); insertion sequence in `printHelp()` is `..., effect, examples, method, ...`; smoke test asserts grep `-c` of `examples` in help output is 1 and total command-line count is 22. |

## Key Risks

| Risk | Impact | Mitigation |
|------|--------|------------|
| Content drift from product truth | Overclaiming damages credibility | M7 audit against MESSAGING.md; PM review before merge |
| Docusaurus version/config issues | Build failures | Pin to latest stable 3.x; use default plugins only |
| Brand inconsistency with current site | Jarring visual transition | Migrate exact colors/fonts from existing CSS |
| Docs become stale as CLI evolves | User confusion | Docs are derived from spec; updating spec triggers doc update |
| M20 dry-run plan mistaken for live execution | Operator confusion, false safety expectations | Dry-run response carries an explicit `executed: false` marker and `V1_DRY_RUN_NOTE` string; docs reserve live execution for a later increment |
| Execution policy drift between manifest governance and serve | Approved capabilities could expose unvalidated plans if policy parser bypasses approval | `tools/list` and `tools/call` continue to filter by `approved: true`; policy mode never relaxes the approval gate |
| M21 default flipping operators into dry-run by accident | Operators expect describe-only semantics but get dry-run plan responses | `tusq policy init` defaults to `mode: "describe-only"`; switching to dry-run requires an explicit `--mode dry-run` flag and is echoed in stdout and `--json` confirmation |
| M21 generator drift from `loadAndValidatePolicy()` | Generated policy could fail validation at `tusq serve --policy` time, breaking operator onboarding | Smoke test performs a round-trip: generate → `loadAndValidatePolicy()`; any drift in the validator or generator surfaces as a failing test before merge |
| M22 verifier/server validator divergence | A `tusq policy verify` pass that `tusq serve --policy` rejects (or vice versa) would destroy the only governance contract the verifier ships | Dev MUST reuse `loadAndValidatePolicy()` — no standalone validator. Smoke parity fixtures assert identical exit code and error message for every failure case before merge (SYSTEM_SPEC Constraint 9) |
| M22 scope creep into manifest-aware strict mode | Adding manifest cross-reference in V1.3 would violate the local-only boundary and conflate policy-file validation with capability-approval validation | Scope boundary table explicitly reserves manifest-aware `--strict` for V2; V1.3 is strictly a policy-file validator; Constraint 10 forbids manifest reads under `policy verify` |
| M23 accidental strict-default / CI regression on existing `tusq policy verify` callers | If `--strict` is silently activated (e.g. auto-on when a manifest exists), every existing M22 CI job starts failing on pre-manifest scaffolds and pre-approval policies for no operator benefit | `--strict` is strictly opt-in (SYSTEM_SPEC Constraint 11); default `tusq policy verify` preserves M22 behavior byte-for-byte; a smoke test asserts the default path does not open `tusq.manifest.json` even when it exists |
| M23 strict PASS misread as runtime execution safety | Narrative drift: a passing `--strict` run could be framed as "safe to execute," causing operators to skip further review or tighten the approval gate prematurely | SYSTEM_SPEC Constraint 12 codifies strict PASS as a policy/manifest alignment statement only; docs/README/CLI-help forbid framings like "runtime check," "execution-safety gate," "pre-flight for serve," or any phrase that implies a PASS makes execution safe; launch artifacts inherit the forbidden-framing list |
| M24 schema-field extraction silently changes manifest shape for pre-M24 callers | If a Fastify route with a `schema` block starts emitting populated `input_schema.properties` and `additionalProperties: false`, existing agent consumers may begin rejecting requests that previously succeeded | Extraction is additive and opt-in on source-literal pattern match only; non-Fastify fixtures produce byte-identical manifests pre/post-M24 (smoke test asserts this); `additionalProperties: false` flip is observable in the manifest diff under `tusq diff`, so any regression surfaces as a reviewable change before merge |
| M24 extraction claims validator semantics it cannot prove | Fastify at runtime validates `body` against the declared schema, but the static extractor only reads the literal object; calling the extracted shape "validator-backed" would overclaim | SYSTEM_SPEC Constraint 13 codifies the extraction as "static literal-object extraction" — the manifest `source` tag is `fastify_schema_body`, docs name it as "what the source declares, not what runtime enforces"; no "validator-backed" framing is permitted in help text, docs, or launch artifacts |
| M24 regex fragility on non-literal schema expressions | A Fastify route that references a shared schema constant (`schema: userSchema`) or a computed object could trip a naive extractor and produce a malformed manifest | Extractor MUST gracefully degrade when the schema value is not a literal object — any parse ambiguity produces NO `schema_fields` and falls back to M15 behavior; a smoke test asserts byte-identical output for the non-literal-schema case |
| M25 PII field-name match framed as PII detection | A `redaction.pii_fields` entry only means the field's normalized key matches a well-known PII name; it does NOT prove the field carries PII at runtime (a field named `password` on a 2FA toggle would still be flagged). Overclaiming the hint as "PII detection" would invite operators to skip manual review | SYSTEM_SPEC Constraint 16 codifies the framing: `pii_fields` is a source-literal name hint, not a validation claim; docs/README/CLI-help MUST NOT describe M25 as "PII detection," "PII-validated," "GDPR-compliant," "HIPAA-compliant," or any phrase that implies regulatory compliance; `sensitivity_class` MUST NOT be auto-escalated; reviewers remain responsible for final redaction posture |
| M25 silent manifest shape change for previously-approved capabilities | Populating `redaction.pii_fields` on a capability that previously had `pii_fields: []` flips `capability_digest` under M13 and revokes effective approval (capability disappears from `tools/list` until re-approval). A large repo may see dozens of capabilities require re-approval in a single M25 upgrade | The M13 approval-gate semantics are the correct migration path — the diff is reviewable under `tusq diff`; SYSTEM_SPEC explicitly calls out that an M25-driven `redaction` change is a material governance event, not a silent upgrade; RELEASE_NOTES MUST document the re-approval implication before the M25 increment is consumed by downstream operators |
| M25 canonical-list drift between minor versions | Expanding the canonical PII name set in a future minor release would silently reclassify field names without operator consent, duplicating the risk above at every upgrade boundary | The V1.6 set is explicitly enumerated in SYSTEM_SPEC Constraint 15 and frozen in `src/cli.js`; any addition is a material governance event that MUST land under its own ROADMAP milestone (e.g., M25.1, M26) with a fresh re-approval expectation and a RELEASE_NOTES entry; no silent list mutation is permitted |
| M25 false negative from ambiguous field naming | A codebase that uses non-English field names (`correoElectronico`, `telefone`, `passwort`) or cryptic abbreviations (`usr_em`, `pswd`) will not match the V1.6 canonical set and will emit `pii_fields: []` even when PII is present | V1.6 accepts this as a known limitation; `sensitivity_class` remains `"unknown"` by default (not "none"), preserving the signal that redaction posture is unresolved; SYSTEM_SPEC documents the limitation and reserves multi-locale expansion for V2 under a plugin interface |
| M26 category labeling framed as retention-policy enforcement | A populated `redaction.pii_categories` array only labels the M25 canonical category for each matched field; it does NOT enforce any retention policy at runtime, does NOT auto-set `retention_days`, and does NOT prove regulatory compliance. Overclaiming the label as "auto-retention" or "retention-policy enforcement" would invite operators to skip manual retention review | SYSTEM_SPEC Constraint 18 codifies the framing: `pii_categories` is a source-literal category label, not a retention-policy enforcement; docs/README/CLI-help MUST NOT describe M26 as "auto-retention," "automated redaction," "GDPR-retention-compliant," or any phrase that implies runtime retention enforcement; `retention_days`/`log_level`/`mask_in_traces` keep existing defaults (`null`, `"full"`, `false`) and are owned by reviewers, not the extractor |
| M26 broad manifest shape flip on upgrade | Every capability (not just PII capabilities) sees a `redaction.pii_categories` field appear in the manifest on first post-M26 scan — both non-PII capabilities gaining `pii_categories: []` and PII capabilities gaining a populated array flip their `capability_digest` under M13 and revoke effective approval until re-approval. A repo with dozens of approved capabilities may require re-approval across the whole manifest in a single M26 upgrade | The M13 approval-gate is the correct migration path — the diff is reviewable under `tusq diff`; SYSTEM_SPEC calls out the first-scan digest flip as a one-time migration event affecting **every** capability; RELEASE_NOTES MUST document the broad re-approval requirement before M26 is consumed by downstream operators (narrower than M25's flip, which only affected capabilities with canonical-name body fields) |
| M26 silent category-set drift between minor releases | Adding a new category (e.g., `"biometric"`) or a new canonical name under an existing category in a future minor release would silently reclassify matched fields without operator consent, duplicating the silent-manifest-change risk at every upgrade boundary | The V1.7 nine-category mapping is explicitly enumerated in SYSTEM_SPEC Constraint 17 and frozen in `src/cli.js` as `PII_CATEGORY_BY_NAME`; any addition is a material governance event that MUST land under its own ROADMAP milestone (e.g., M26.1, M27) with a fresh re-approval expectation and a RELEASE_NOTES entry; M25 and M26 freeze together — an expansion of `PII_CANONICAL_NAMES` without a matching `PII_CATEGORY_BY_NAME` entry is an implementation-time error the defensive guard throws synchronously |
| M26 mistaken as runtime PII-category validator | A `pii_categories: ["secrets"]` label on a capability means its `pii_fields` entry's normalized name matched the canonical `secrets` category — NOT that the field carries a secret at runtime, NOT that the capability validates the field as a secret, and NOT that any retention policy is applied. A reviewer could mistake the label as runtime evidence | SYSTEM_SPEC Constraint 18 explicitly forbids runtime-enforcement framing; docs/README MUST state that `pii_categories` is a source-literal category label derived from M25's field-name match; `tusq serve` and `tusq policy verify --strict` behavior is unchanged by M26; no category-driven filtering or enforcement is added in V1.7 |
| M27 review report framed as automated compliance or retention enforcement | The review report aggregates M25/M26 data and attaches a frozen per-category advisory line; if that advisory is framed as "automatic PII compliance," "automated retention policy," "GDPR/HIPAA/PCI-ready," or "runtime PII safeguard" the operator may skip the manual reviewer step the report is explicitly designed to support | SYSTEM_SPEC Constraint 19 codifies M27 as a reviewer aid with advisory strings only; docs/README/CLI-help/launch artifacts MUST NOT describe `tusq redaction review` as "compliance," "automated enforcement," "runtime gate," "pre-flight check for serve," or any phrase that implies a run of the command makes a capability safer at runtime; advisory strings are explicitly framed as reviewer reminders that assume reviewer action |
| M27 surface creep into mutating the manifest or other commands | A command called "redaction review" could be read as a natural place to silently populate `retention_days`, auto-set `log_level`, flip `mask_in_traces`, escalate `sensitivity_class`, or change what `tusq policy verify --strict` / `tusq serve` filters at runtime | SYSTEM_SPEC Constraint 20 codifies M27 as strictly read-only: no manifest write, no policy file write, no scan re-run, no change to any other command's observable behavior; a smoke test asserts `tusq.manifest.json` mtime and content are unchanged after a review run, and that default/strict `tusq policy verify` stdout/exit code are unchanged |
| M27 advisory-string drift between minor releases | Editing the wording of a single advisory line in a future minor release would silently change the reviewer experience and cause CI diffs for teams that snapshot the report | The V1.8 advisory set is explicitly enumerated in SYSTEM_SPEC Constraint 19 and frozen in `src/cli.js` as `PII_REVIEW_ADVISORY_BY_CATEGORY`; any addition OR wording change is a material governance event that MUST land under its own ROADMAP milestone with a fresh re-approval expectation and a RELEASE_NOTES entry; the smoke suite's human-output fixture locks wording at merge time |
| M27 empty-capabilities manifest ambiguity | An implementer could reasonably read the plan as "treat `capabilities: []` as an error" (exit 1, `Invalid manifest:` message) OR as "exit 0 with zero sections" — both are defensible in the absence of an explicit rule, but the two produce different CI signal for a scaffold/init-new-repo workflow where the manifest exists but is empty; silent divergence between implementations would burn reviewer trust on the very first M27 invocation | ROADMAP § M27 now codifies the empty-capabilities-array case as exit 0 with an explicit `No capabilities in manifest — nothing to review.` human line and `capabilities: []` in `--json`, distinct from the `Invalid manifest: missing capabilities array` (exit 1) path for a manifest where the array is missing or non-array; SYSTEM_SPEC § M27 Edge-Case and Empty-Manifest Handling subsection enumerates the two paths side-by-side; smoke coverage adds both cases so the divergence cannot slip past merge |
| M27 stdout contamination on error paths | An operator who pipes `tusq redaction review > report.txt` expects an empty file when the command fails (so their file never contains a partial or misleading report); if error messages leak to stdout — or worse, a partial report is written before the error is detected — the pipe-to-file UX breaks silently and the operator may review a half-complete report as if it were authoritative | ROADMAP § M27 now codifies I/O stream discipline: every error path writes exclusively to stderr, stdout is empty-string on every exit-1 case, smoke assertion captures both streams and verifies `stdout === ""` on each error case; the detection-before-output invariant is already specified ("exits 1 before any stdout") but this item makes the stream-separation assertion explicit and testable |
| M28 sensitivity_class misread as runtime data-access control | A reviewer or downstream consumer could interpret `sensitivity_class: "restricted"` as runtime evidence that the capability is actually restricted from unauthorized callers, rather than as a static reviewer-aid label. This would cause operators to skip manual access-control review on the assumption the manifest enforces restrictions automatically | SYSTEM_SPEC Constraint 21 and the M28 non-compliance-certification boundary (§ M28 "Non-Compliance-Certification Boundary") codify the framing; docs/README/CLI-help MUST use the phrase "reviewer-aid" and MUST NOT use any phrase implying runtime enforcement; `tusq compile` byte-identity assertion confirms the sensitivity class has zero compile-time effect |
| M28 "public" silently assigned to zero-evidence capabilities | A naively implemented R6 default could emit `sensitivity_class: "public"` for capabilities with no verb, no route, no params, no redaction, no preserve flag, and no auth_required — overclaiming that such capabilities are safe to expose without review | The zero-evidence guard is the first check in `classifySensitivity`; SYSTEM_SPEC Constraint 21 and the AC-4 acceptance criterion both require `"unknown"` (not `"public"`) for zero-evidence capabilities; smoke case 8 asserts the empty-record → unknown invariant |
| M28 rule-table drift between releases | An implementer could silently change R2's verb set or R4's financial-route regex in a future minor release, reclassifying capabilities without operator consent and flipping capability_digest without an explicit governance milestone | The rule table is explicitly frozen in SYSTEM_SPEC § M28 and codified in Constraint 21; any rule change MUST land under its own ROADMAP milestone with fresh re-approval expectations and a RELEASE_NOTES entry; the eval regression scenarios (AC-8) lock the exact output of the three highest-precedence paths (R1>R3, R4 financial, zero-evidence unknown) at merge time |
| M29 auth_requirements misread as runtime authentication enforcement | A reviewer or downstream consumer could interpret `auth_scheme: "bearer"` as runtime evidence that the capability validates bearer tokens, rather than as a static reviewer-aid label derived from a middleware-name regex match. This would cause operators to skip manual AAA review on the assumption the manifest enforces authentication automatically | SYSTEM_SPEC Constraint 22 and the M29 non-attestation boundary (§ M29 "Non-Attestation Boundary") codify the framing; docs/README/CLI-help MUST use the phrase "reviewer-aid" and MUST NOT use any phrase implying runtime AAA enforcement, OAuth/OIDC/SAML compliance, or token-signature validation; `tusq compile` byte-identity assertion confirms `auth_requirements` has zero compile-time effect; `tusq serve` MCP surface is unchanged so no operator is misled at the runtime boundary |
| M29 "none" silently assigned to zero-evidence capabilities | A naively implemented R6 default could emit `auth_scheme: "none"` for capabilities with no middleware, no route prefix, no `auth_required` flag, and no `sensitivity_class` signal — overclaiming that such capabilities are safe to expose without authentication review | The zero-evidence guard is the first check in `classifyAuthRequirements`; SYSTEM_SPEC Constraint 22 and the AC-4 acceptance criterion both require `auth_scheme: "unknown"` (not `"none"`) for zero-evidence capabilities; smoke case 8 asserts the empty-record → unknown-with-empty-arrays invariant |
| M29 rule-table or scope-extraction drift between releases | An implementer could silently change the middleware regex set, the scope/role extraction regex, or the precedence order in a future minor release, reclassifying capabilities without operator consent and flipping `capability_digest` without an explicit governance milestone | The rule table and the scope/role extraction rules are explicitly frozen in SYSTEM_SPEC § M29 and codified in Constraint 22; any rule change MUST land under its own ROADMAP milestone with fresh re-approval expectations and a RELEASE_NOTES entry; eval regression scenarios (AC-9) lock bearer-precedence, scopes-extraction order/dedup, and zero-evidence-unknown paths at merge time |
| M30 surface plan misread as runtime surface generator | A reviewer or downstream consumer could interpret a `tusq surface plan --surface chat` JSON response as evidence that a chat client has been generated and is ready to deploy, rather than as a static reviewer-aid plan that lists which capabilities **would** be eligible for chat under current sensitivity/auth/side-effect posture. This would cause operators to skip the actual chat-generator milestone (M-Chat-1) on the assumption M30 already shipped a chat surface | SYSTEM_SPEC Constraint 23 (proposed) and the M30 "Non-Runtime-Generator Boundary" subsection codify the framing; docs/README/CLI-help MUST use the phrase "planning aid" and MUST NOT use any phrase implying runtime surface generation, brand certification, or accessibility certification; `brand_inputs_required[]` is a names-only list (no values, no template strings, no brand profile read) so the output cannot be misread as a render-ready bundle; `tusq compile` and `tusq serve` byte-identity assertions confirm M30 has zero runtime effect |
| M30 silent enum drift between releases | An implementer could silently add a new `surface` value (e.g., `email`, `slack-bot`) or a new `gated_reason` value in a future minor release, reclassifying capabilities without operator consent and changing the per-surface plan output without a corresponding governance event. Downstream consumers that snapshot the plan would see CI diffs without an explicit ROADMAP entry | The four-value `surface` enum and the six-value `gated_reason` enum are explicitly frozen in SYSTEM_SPEC § M30 and codified in Constraint 23; any addition is a material governance event that MUST land under its own ROADMAP milestone with a fresh re-approval expectation and a RELEASE_NOTES entry; an implementation-time guard (synchronous throw) MUST fire if `classifyGating(capability, surface)` ever returns a value outside the closed six-value set |
| M30 manifest mutation through plan generation | A naively implemented plan generator could attempt to write `eligible_capabilities`/`gated_capabilities` back into the manifest (e.g., as a new `surfaces` field on each capability), or could call back into `computeCapabilityDigest` in a way that flips digests for previously-approved capabilities. This would silently revoke approval across the manifest on first M30 invocation, duplicating M26's broad-shape-flip risk | M30 is read-only by design: the plan generator reads `capabilities[]` and never calls back into manifest builders or digest computation. SYSTEM_SPEC § M30 codifies the no-write invariant; a smoke assertion captures `tusq.manifest.json` mtime and SHA-256 before and after a plan run and asserts byte-identity; a separate smoke assertion captures every capability's `capability_digest` before and after and asserts no digest flips |
| M30 `--out` path traversal into `.tusq/` | An operator running `tusq surface plan --out .tusq/plan.json` could conflate the plan with a governance artifact (a real `.tusq/` artifact has approval implications and a different review pattern) or could overwrite a real `.tusq/` file (e.g., `.tusq/scan.json`, `.tusq/execution-policy.json`) and silently corrupt the governance state | `--out` rejects any path resolving inside `.tusq/` with `--out path must not be inside .tusq/` on stderr and exit 1; smoke coverage asserts the rejection path; operators wanting a planning artifact alongside other governance files keep it elsewhere on disk (the operator's choice, not a tusq.dev directory) |
| M31 domain index misread as skill-pack/rollout/workflow generator | A reviewer or downstream consumer could interpret a `tusq domain index --json` response as evidence that skill packs, rollout checklists, or workflow definitions have been generated and are ready to consume, rather than as a static reviewer-aid index that surfaces what domains the manifest already exposes. This would cause operators to skip the actual skill-pack milestone (M-Skills-1) on the assumption M31 already shipped a skills surface, mirroring the M30 misread risk for chat/widget/voice generators | SYSTEM_SPEC Constraint 24 (proposed) and the M31 "Non-Generator Boundary" subsection codify the framing; docs/README/CLI-help MUST use the phrase "planning aid" and MUST NOT use any phrase implying skill-pack generation, rollout-plan generation, workflow generation, agent-persona derivation, or domain-level access enforcement; the per-domain entry contains name-and-counters only (no advisory text, no entry points, no brand inputs) so the output cannot be misread as a render-ready bundle; `tusq compile`/`tusq serve`/`tusq surface plan` byte-identity assertions confirm M31 has zero runtime effect |
| M31 silent enum drift on `aggregation_key` between releases | An implementer could silently add a new `aggregation_key` value (e.g., `multi_domain`, `synthetic`) in a future minor release, reclassifying capabilities without operator consent and changing the per-domain index output without a corresponding governance event. Downstream consumers that snapshot the index would see CI diffs without an explicit ROADMAP entry, and the closed-enum invariant established by M30's `surface`/`gated_reason` enums would be silently broken | The two-value `aggregation_key` enum is explicitly frozen in SYSTEM_SPEC § M31 and codified in Constraint 24; any addition is a material governance event that MUST land under its own ROADMAP milestone with a fresh re-approval expectation and a RELEASE_NOTES entry; an implementation-time guard (synchronous throw) MUST fire if `bucketCapability(capability)` ever returns a value outside the closed two-value set; the eval regression scenario `domain-index-determinism` locks the enum-closure invariant at merge time |
| M31 manifest mutation through index generation | A naively implemented index generator could attempt to write `domain_index` back into the manifest (e.g., as a new top-level field), or could call back into `computeCapabilityDigest` in a way that flips digests for previously-approved capabilities. This would silently revoke approval across the manifest on first M31 invocation, duplicating M26's broad-shape-flip risk and the M30 manifest-mutation risk | M31 is read-only by design: the index generator reads `capabilities[]` and never calls back into manifest builders or digest computation. SYSTEM_SPEC § M31 codifies the no-write invariant; a smoke assertion captures `tusq.manifest.json` mtime and SHA-256 before and after an index run and asserts byte-identity; a separate smoke assertion captures every capability's `capability_digest` before and after and asserts no digest flips |
| M31 `--out` path traversal into `.tusq/` | An operator running `tusq domain index --out .tusq/index.json` could conflate the index with a governance artifact (a real `.tusq/` artifact has approval implications and a different review pattern) or could overwrite a real `.tusq/` file (e.g., `.tusq/scan.json`, `.tusq/execution-policy.json`) and silently corrupt the governance state | `--out` rejects any path resolving inside `.tusq/` with `--out path must not be inside .tusq/` on stderr and exit 1 (mirroring M30); smoke coverage asserts the rejection path; operators wanting a planning artifact alongside other governance files keep it elsewhere on disk (the operator's choice, not a tusq.dev directory) |
| M31 alphabetization-drift between releases | An implementer reading the spec as "group capabilities by domain" could naively `Object.keys(buckets).sort()` the output and ship an alphabetized index in V1.12.x, then a later release could revert to manifest first-appearance order, silently changing the output for any consumer that snapshots the index. Two manifests that swap the declared order of two domains would emit identical alphabetized output today and divergent output tomorrow | SYSTEM_SPEC § M31 explicitly freezes per-domain iteration order as the manifest's *first appearance* order (deterministic, never alphabetized); the `unknown` bucket is appended last; any change to ordering is a material governance event under its own ROADMAP milestone; the eval regression scenario `domain-index-determinism` and a dedicated smoke fixture lock the first-appearance ordering at merge time so a naive alphabetization slip cannot pass CI |
| M32 side-effect index misread as runtime side-effect enforcer or risk classifier | A reviewer or downstream consumer could interpret `tusq effect index --json` output as evidence that destructive capabilities are runtime-gated, that a composite risk score has been computed, or that confirmation-flow code has been generated, rather than as a static reviewer-aid bucket-roll-up of the manifest's existing `side_effect_class` evidence. This would cause operators to skip the actual M-Risk-1 / M-Confirm-1 milestones on the assumption M32 already shipped runtime side-effect safeguards, mirroring the M30/M31 misread risks for surface/skill-pack generators | SYSTEM_SPEC Constraint 25 (proposed) and the M32 "Non-Enforcer/Non-Risk-Classifier Boundary" subsection codify the framing; docs/README/CLI-help MUST use the phrase "planning aid" and MUST NOT use any phrase implying runtime side-effect enforcement, automatic confirmation flows, composite risk-tier classification, destructive-action safety certification, or alteration of the M30 `gated_reason: destructive_side_effect` surface-eligibility rule; the per-bucket entry contains name-and-counters only (no derived risk_tier, no cross-axis roll-up arrays, no advisory text) so the output cannot be misread as a render-ready risk dashboard; `tusq compile`/`tusq serve`/`tusq surface plan`/`tusq domain index` byte-identity assertions confirm M32 has zero runtime effect |
| M32 silent enum drift on `side_effect_class` bucket-key or `aggregation_key` between releases | An implementer could silently add a fifth `side_effect_class` bucket-key value (e.g., `financial`, `admin_only`, `security_sensitive` — pulled directly from VISION line 45's broader enumeration) or a third `aggregation_key` value in a future minor release, reclassifying capabilities without operator consent and changing the per-bucket index output without a corresponding governance event. Downstream consumers that snapshot the index would see CI diffs without an explicit ROADMAP entry, and the closed-enum invariant established by M30's `surface`/`gated_reason` enums and M31's `aggregation_key` enum would be silently broken. The risk is sharper for M32 than for M31 because VISION line 45 explicitly enumerates "read, write, destructive, financial, security-sensitive, and admin-only" — a naive implementer could read that as authorizing the broader six-value enum | The four-value `side_effect_class` bucket-key enum (`read | write | destructive | unknown`) and the two-value `aggregation_key` enum (`class | unknown`) are explicitly frozen in SYSTEM_SPEC § M32 and codified in Constraint 25 (proposed); the bucket-key enum aligns 1:1 with the existing manifest `side_effect_class` three-value classifier (`read | write | destructive`) plus the `unknown` zero-evidence catchall — extending the bucket-key enum to `financial`/`admin_only`/`security_sensitive` would require a corresponding extension to the manifest's `side_effect_class` classifier, which is itself a material governance event under its own ROADMAP milestone with a fresh re-approval expectation; an implementation-time guard (synchronous throw) MUST fire if `bucketByEffect(capability)` ever returns a value outside the closed four-value set; the eval regression scenario `effect-index-determinism` locks the enum-closure invariant at merge time |
| M32 manifest mutation through index generation | A naively implemented index generator could attempt to write `effect_index` back into the manifest (e.g., as a new top-level field), or could call back into `computeCapabilityDigest` in a way that flips digests for previously-approved capabilities. This would silently revoke approval across the manifest on first M32 invocation, duplicating the M26 broad-shape-flip risk and the M30/M31 manifest-mutation risks | M32 is read-only by design: the index generator reads `capabilities[]` and never calls back into manifest builders or digest computation. SYSTEM_SPEC § M32 codifies the no-write invariant; a smoke assertion captures `tusq.manifest.json` mtime and SHA-256 before and after an index run and asserts byte-identity; a separate smoke assertion captures every capability's `capability_digest` before and after and asserts no digest flips |
| M32 `--out` path traversal into `.tusq/` | An operator running `tusq effect index --out .tusq/effects.json` could conflate the index with a governance artifact (a real `.tusq/` artifact has approval implications and a different review pattern) or could overwrite a real `.tusq/` file (e.g., `.tusq/scan.json`, `.tusq/execution-policy.json`) and silently corrupt the governance state | `--out` rejects any path resolving inside `.tusq/` with `--out path must not be inside .tusq/` on stderr and exit 1 (mirroring M30/M31); smoke coverage asserts the rejection path; operators wanting a planning artifact alongside other governance files keep it elsewhere on disk (the operator's choice, not a tusq.dev directory) |
| M32 closed-enum order mistaken as risk-precedence | An implementer or reviewer could read the closed-enum iteration order `read → write → destructive → unknown` as a risk-precedence statement (low → high → highest → unknown) and start treating bucket position as a risk score, then later expand the enum and silently shift the risk-score interpretation. Downstream consumers could derive ad-hoc risk dashboards from bucket position rather than from explicit risk-tier fields that don't yet exist | SYSTEM_SPEC § M32 codifies the closed-enum order as a deterministic stable-output convention only — NOT a risk-precedence statement; docs/README/CLI-help MUST NOT describe the order as "risk-ascending," "low-to-high," "safety-ordered," or any phrase implying risk semantics; risk-tier composition is explicitly reserved for the deferred M-Risk-1 milestone with its own enum and its own acceptance contract; the `aggregation_key` field (`class | unknown`) carries the only semantic claim — that the bucket is a closed-enum class match or the zero-evidence catchall, NOT a risk level |
| M33 sensitivity index misread as runtime sensitivity enforcer or compliance certifier | A reviewer or downstream consumer could interpret `tusq sensitivity index --json` output as evidence that confidential or restricted capabilities are runtime-gated, that GDPR/HIPAA/SOC2/PCI compliance has been certified, that retention policy has been generated, or that data-class access enforcement has been wired up, rather than as a static reviewer-aid bucket-roll-up of the manifest's existing M28-classified `sensitivity_class` evidence. This would cause operators to skip the actual M-Risk-1 / M-Compliance-1 milestones on the assumption M33 already shipped runtime sensitivity safeguards or compliance attestation, mirroring the M30/M31/M32 misread risks for surface/skill-pack/risk generators | SYSTEM_SPEC Constraint 26 (proposed) and the M33 "Non-Enforcer/Non-Compliance-Certifier Boundary" subsection codify the framing; docs/README/CLI-help MUST use the phrase "planning aid" and MUST NOT use any phrase implying runtime sensitivity enforcement, automatic data-class enforcement, GDPR/HIPAA/SOC2/PCI compliance certification, automated retention policy, or alteration of the M30 `gated_reason: restricted_sensitivity`/`gated_reason: confidential_sensitivity` surface-eligibility rules; the per-bucket entry contains name-and-counters only (no derived risk_tier, no cross-axis roll-up arrays, no compliance attestation field, no advisory text) so the output cannot be misread as a render-ready compliance dashboard; `tusq compile`/`tusq serve`/`tusq surface plan`/`tusq domain index`/`tusq effect index` byte-identity assertions confirm M33 has zero runtime effect |
| M33 silent enum drift on `sensitivity_class` bucket-key or `aggregation_key` between releases | An implementer could silently add a sixth `sensitivity_class` bucket-key value (e.g., `pii`, `pci`, `phi` — pulled directly from VISION line 110's "PII, payment data, secrets, regulated data, and customer-sensitive fields" enumeration) or a third `aggregation_key` value in a future minor release, reclassifying capabilities without operator consent and changing the per-bucket index output without a corresponding governance event. Downstream consumers that snapshot the index would see CI diffs without an explicit ROADMAP entry, and the closed-enum invariant established by M30's `surface`/`gated_reason` enums, M31's `aggregation_key` enum, and M32's `side_effect_class`/`aggregation_key` enums would be silently broken. The risk is sharper for M33 than for M32 because the M28 classifier is itself the upstream source of `sensitivity_class` values — extending the bucket-key enum without first extending M28's classifier would produce zero-population buckets that never appear (since `EMPTY` buckets are omitted), masking the drift | The five-value `sensitivity_class` bucket-key enum (`public | internal | confidential | restricted | unknown`) and the two-value `aggregation_key` enum (`class | unknown`) are explicitly frozen in SYSTEM_SPEC § M33 and codified in Constraint 26 (proposed); the bucket-key enum aligns 1:1 with the M28 `SENSITIVITY_CLASSES` constant in `src/cli.js` plus the `unknown` zero-evidence catchall — extending the bucket-key enum to `pii`/`pci`/`phi` would require a corresponding extension to the M28 classifier, which is itself a material governance event under its own ROADMAP milestone with a fresh re-approval expectation; an implementation-time guard (synchronous throw) MUST fire if `bucketBySensitivity(capability)` ever returns a value outside the closed five-value set; the eval regression scenario `sensitivity-index-determinism` locks the enum-closure invariant at merge time |
| M33 manifest mutation through index generation | A naively implemented index generator could attempt to write `sensitivity_index` back into the manifest (e.g., as a new top-level field), or could call back into `computeCapabilityDigest` in a way that flips digests for previously-approved capabilities. This would silently revoke approval across the manifest on first M33 invocation, duplicating the M26 broad-shape-flip risk and the M30/M31/M32 manifest-mutation risks | M33 is read-only by design: the index generator reads `capabilities[]` and never calls back into manifest builders or digest computation. SYSTEM_SPEC § M33 codifies the no-write invariant; a smoke assertion captures `tusq.manifest.json` mtime and SHA-256 before and after an index run and asserts byte-identity; a separate smoke assertion captures every capability's `capability_digest` before and after and asserts no digest flips |
| M33 `--out` path traversal into `.tusq/` | An operator running `tusq sensitivity index --out .tusq/sensitivities.json` could conflate the index with a governance artifact (a real `.tusq/` artifact has approval implications and a different review pattern) or could overwrite a real `.tusq/` file (e.g., `.tusq/scan.json`, `.tusq/execution-policy.json`) and silently corrupt the governance state | `--out` rejects any path resolving inside `.tusq/` with `--out path must not be inside .tusq/` on stderr and exit 1 (mirroring M30/M31/M32); smoke coverage asserts the rejection path; operators wanting a planning artifact alongside other governance files keep it elsewhere on disk (the operator's choice, not a tusq.dev directory) |
| M33 closed-enum order mistaken as risk-precedence | An implementer or reviewer could read the closed-enum iteration order `public → internal → confidential → restricted → unknown` as a risk-precedence statement (low → high → highest → unknown) and start treating bucket position as a risk score (the misread is sharper for M33 than for M32 because the sensitivity domain has a culturally-conventional risk ordering: public < internal < confidential < restricted is the standard data-classification ladder), then later expand the enum and silently shift the risk-score interpretation. Downstream consumers could derive ad-hoc risk dashboards from bucket position rather than from explicit risk-tier fields that don't yet exist | SYSTEM_SPEC § M33 codifies the closed-enum order as a deterministic stable-output convention only — NOT a risk-precedence statement; the order matches the natural reading order of the M28 SENSITIVITY_CLASSES constant (with `unknown` appended last per M32 convention) but carries no risk semantic; docs/README/CLI-help MUST NOT describe the order as "risk-ascending," "low-to-high," "data-classification ladder," "safety-ordered," or any phrase implying risk semantics; risk-tier composition is explicitly reserved for the deferred M-Risk-1 milestone with its own enum and its own acceptance contract; the `aggregation_key` field (`class | unknown`) carries the only semantic claim — that the bucket is a closed-enum class match or the zero-evidence catchall, NOT a risk level |
| M33 bucket-key value drift relative to M28 SENSITIVITY_CLASSES | An implementer could implement the M33 bucket-key enum as an independent constant (e.g., `M33_SENSITIVITY_BUCKET_ENUM = ['public', 'internal', 'confidential', 'restricted', 'unknown']` redeclared in M33 code) rather than referencing the existing M28 `SENSITIVITY_CLASSES`. A future M28 classifier change (e.g., renaming `confidential` to `protected`) would silently produce M33 output that no longer matches manifest evidence, and the M33 bucket-key enum would silently drift relative to the manifest | M33 implementation MUST reference the M28 `SENSITIVITY_CLASSES` constant directly (or derive the bucket-key enum from it at module-load time with the `unknown` catchall added if not already present); SYSTEM_SPEC § M33 codifies the 1:1 alignment between the bucket-key enum and the M28 classifier; an implementation-time guard (synchronous throw) MUST fire if the bucket-key enum and the M28 classifier ever diverge; smoke coverage asserts that every value in `SENSITIVITY_CLASSES` appears in the bucket-key enum and vice versa |
| M34 method index misread as runtime HTTP-method router, REST-convention validator, or idempotency classifier | A reviewer or downstream consumer could interpret `tusq method index --json` output as evidence that HTTP methods are being routed at runtime, that idempotency has been certified per bucket, that REST conventions (safety, idempotency, cacheability) have been validated, or that destructive verbs have been auto-classified into the M32 destructive bucket, rather than as a static reviewer-aid bucket-roll-up of the manifest's existing verbatim `method` field. This would cause operators to skip the actual M-Idempotency-1 / M-RestConv-1 / M-Risk-1 milestones on the assumption M34 already shipped runtime HTTP safeguards, mirroring the M30/M31/M32/M33 misread risks for surface/skill-pack/effect/sensitivity generators | SYSTEM_SPEC Constraint 27 (proposed) and the M34 "Non-Router/Non-REST-Validator/Non-Idempotency-Classifier Boundary" subsection codify the framing; docs/README/CLI-help MUST use the phrase "planning aid" and MUST NOT use any phrase implying runtime HTTP-method routing, REST-convention validation (safety/idempotency/cacheability), idempotency certification, automatic destructive-verb classification, alteration of the M32 `side_effect_class` derivation rules, or alteration of the M30 `gated_reason: destructive_side_effect` surface-eligibility rule; the per-bucket entry contains name-and-counters only (no derived `idempotency_class`, no derived `risk_tier`, no cross-axis roll-up arrays, no advisory text) so the output cannot be misread as a render-ready REST-conformance dashboard; `tusq compile`/`tusq serve`/`tusq surface plan`/`tusq domain index`/`tusq effect index`/`tusq sensitivity index` byte-identity assertions confirm M34 has zero runtime effect; the `DELETE` bucket label is a static aggregation key, NOT a destructive-side-effect attestation (M32 owns the side-effect classification) |
| M34 silent enum drift on `http_method` bucket-key or `aggregation_key` between releases | An implementer could silently add a new `http_method` bucket-key value (e.g., `HEAD`, `OPTIONS`, `TRACE`, `CONNECT`, or non-standard verbs like `LINK`/`UNLINK`/`COPY`/`MOVE` from WebDAV/RFC 5789 extensions) or a third `aggregation_key` value in a future minor release, reclassifying capabilities without operator consent and changing the per-bucket index output without a corresponding governance event. Downstream consumers that snapshot the index would see CI diffs without an explicit ROADMAP entry, and the closed-enum invariant established by M30's `surface`/`gated_reason` enums, M31's `aggregation_key` enum, M32's `side_effect_class`/`aggregation_key` enums, and M33's `sensitivity_class`/`aggregation_key` enums would be silently broken. The risk is moderate for M34 because HTTP defines additional verbs beyond the canonical five (HEAD, OPTIONS, TRACE, CONNECT) — a naive implementer could read the manifest scanner's emission of HEAD/OPTIONS as authorizing a broader bucket-key enum | The five-value `http_method` bucket-key enum (`GET | POST | PUT | PATCH | DELETE`) plus the `unknown` zero-evidence catchall (six total) and the two-value `aggregation_key` enum (`method | unknown`) are explicitly frozen in SYSTEM_SPEC § M34 and codified in Constraint 27 (proposed); the bucket-key enum aligns with the canonical CRUD-mapping subset of HTTP verbs that REST APIs use as capability-bearing entry points — extending the bucket-key enum to `HEAD`/`OPTIONS`/`TRACE`/`CONNECT` (or to WebDAV/RFC 5789 verbs) would require a ROADMAP milestone with a fresh re-approval expectation, particularly because HEAD/OPTIONS/TRACE/CONNECT are protocol-control verbs that REST APIs rarely expose as capabilities; an implementation-time guard (synchronous throw) MUST fire if `bucketByMethod(capability)` ever returns a value outside the closed six-value set; the eval regression scenario `method-index-determinism` locks the enum-closure invariant at merge time |
| M34 manifest mutation through index generation | A naively implemented index generator could attempt to write `method_index` back into the manifest (e.g., as a new top-level field), or could call back into `computeCapabilityDigest` in a way that flips digests for previously-approved capabilities. This would silently revoke approval across the manifest on first M34 invocation, duplicating the M26 broad-shape-flip risk and the M30/M31/M32/M33 manifest-mutation risks | M34 is read-only by design: the index generator reads `capabilities[]` and never calls back into manifest builders or digest computation. SYSTEM_SPEC § M34 codifies the no-write invariant; a smoke assertion captures `tusq.manifest.json` mtime and SHA-256 before and after an index run and asserts byte-identity; a separate smoke assertion captures every capability's `capability_digest` before and after and asserts no digest flips |
| M34 `--out` path traversal into `.tusq/` | An operator running `tusq method index --out .tusq/methods.json` could conflate the index with a governance artifact (a real `.tusq/` artifact has approval implications and a different review pattern) or could overwrite a real `.tusq/` file (e.g., `.tusq/scan.json`, `.tusq/execution-policy.json`) and silently corrupt the governance state | `--out` rejects any path resolving inside `.tusq/` with `--out path must not be inside .tusq/` on stderr and exit 1 (mirroring M30/M31/M32/M33); smoke coverage asserts the rejection path; operators wanting a planning artifact alongside other governance files keep it elsewhere on disk (the operator's choice, not a tusq.dev directory) |
| M34 closed-enum order mistaken as CRUD-risk-precedence | An implementer or reviewer could read the closed-enum iteration order `GET → POST → PUT → PATCH → DELETE → unknown` as a destructive-ascending or risk-ascending statement (since DELETE is canonically destructive and lands last in the closed-enum block before `unknown`), and start treating bucket position as a risk score, then later expand the enum and silently shift the risk-score interpretation. Downstream consumers could derive ad-hoc risk dashboards from bucket position rather than from explicit risk-tier fields that don't yet exist. The misread is plausible because the order matches the conventional CRUD-mapping (GET=read/safe, POST=create/non-idempotent, PUT=replace/idempotent, PATCH=update/non-idempotent, DELETE=delete/destructive) — a reviewer could naively read this as a safety ladder | SYSTEM_SPEC § M34 codifies the closed-enum order as a deterministic stable-output convention only — NOT a CRUD-risk-precedence, NOT a destructive-ascending statement, NOT a safety ladder; the order matches the conventional REST CRUD reading order (GET=read, POST=create, PUT=replace, PATCH=update, DELETE=delete) but carries no risk semantic; docs/README/CLI-help MUST NOT describe the order as "destructive-ascending," "risk-ascending," "safety-ordered," "CRUD-risk-precedence," or any phrase implying risk semantics; risk-tier composition is explicitly reserved for the deferred M-Risk-1 milestone with its own enum and its own acceptance contract; idempotency-class composition is explicitly reserved for the deferred M-Idempotency-1 milestone; the `aggregation_key` field (`method | unknown`) carries the only semantic claim — that the bucket is a closed-enum method match or the zero-evidence catchall, NOT a risk or idempotency level |
| M34 case-folding drift on `--method` filter relative to manifest uppercase convention | An implementer could naively upper-case the `--method <value>` argument before bucket lookup (e.g., `value.toUpperCase()`) so that `tusq method index --method get` succeeds and emits the GET bucket; this would silently diverge from the manifest's verbatim uppercase `method` field convention and mask reviewer-script drift. A reviewer who scripts `--method ${process.env.HTTP_METHOD}` against an env-var that drifts to lowercase would get apparently-correct output, then later see different output if the implementation is hardened to case-sensitive matching, breaking CI silently | M34 implementation MUST match the `--method` argument **case-sensitively** against the closed six-value enum (`GET`/`POST`/`PUT`/`PATCH`/`DELETE`/`unknown`); lowercase or mixed-case values exit 1 with `Unknown method:` followed by the value, empty stdout (mirroring the manifest's uppercase verbatim convention); SYSTEM_SPEC § M34 codifies the case-sensitive rule; smoke case (c2) explicitly asserts `--method get` exits 1 (NOT exit 0 with the GET bucket); Constraint 27 (proposed) enumerates the case-sensitive rule as part of the planning-aid framing |
| M35 auth scheme index misread as runtime authentication enforcer, AAA validator, or OAuth/OIDC/SAML compliance certifier | A reviewer or downstream consumer could interpret `tusq auth index --json` output as evidence that capabilities are runtime-authenticated, that bearer tokens are validated, that OAuth/OIDC/SAML compliance has been certified, that auth-adapter code has been generated, or that IAM context has been derived, rather than as a static reviewer-aid bucket-roll-up of the manifest's existing M29-classified `auth_scheme` evidence. This would cause operators to skip the actual M-Auth-Adapter-1 / M-Runtime-Auth-1 / M-IAM-Posture-1 milestones on the assumption M35 already shipped runtime auth safeguards or compliance attestation, mirroring the M30/M31/M32/M33/M34 misread risks for surface/skill-pack/effect/sensitivity/method generators | SYSTEM_SPEC Constraint 28 (proposed) and the M35 "Non-Enforcer/Non-AAA-Validator/Non-Compliance-Certifier Boundary" subsection codify the framing; docs/README/CLI-help MUST use the phrase "planning aid" and MUST NOT use any phrase implying runtime authentication enforcement, AAA (authentication/authorization/auditing) validation, OAuth/OIDC/SAML compliance certification, generated auth-adapter code, IAM-context derivation, or alteration of the M30 `gated_reason: auth_scheme_unknown`/`gated_reason: auth_scheme_oauth_pending_v2` surface-eligibility rules; the per-bucket entry contains name-and-counters only (no derived `iam_posture`, no derived `risk_tier`, no cross-axis roll-up arrays, no compliance attestation field, no advisory text) so the output cannot be misread as a render-ready compliance dashboard; `tusq compile`/`tusq serve`/`tusq surface plan`/`tusq domain index`/`tusq effect index`/`tusq sensitivity index`/`tusq method index` byte-identity assertions confirm M35 has zero runtime effect |
| M35 silent enum drift on `auth_scheme` bucket-key or `aggregation_key` between releases | An implementer could silently add a new `auth_scheme` bucket-key value (e.g., `mtls`, `aws_sigv4`, `digest`, `hmac`, `webhook_signature` from the broader IAM ecosystem) or a third `aggregation_key` value in a future minor release, reclassifying capabilities without operator consent and changing the per-bucket index output without a corresponding governance event. Downstream consumers that snapshot the index would see CI diffs without an explicit ROADMAP entry, and the closed-enum invariant established by M30/M31/M32/M33/M34 would be silently broken. The risk is sharper for M35 than for M33 because the M29 classifier is itself the upstream source of `auth_scheme` values — extending the M35 bucket-key enum without first extending M29's classifier would produce zero-population buckets that never appear (since `EMPTY` buckets are omitted), masking the drift; conversely, extending M29's classifier without extending M35 would silently send new schemes into the `unknown` bucket, masking the M29 change | The seven-value `auth_scheme` bucket-key enum (`bearer | api_key | session | basic | oauth | none | unknown`) and the two-value `aggregation_key` enum (`scheme | unknown`) are explicitly frozen in SYSTEM_SPEC § M35 and codified in Constraint 28 (proposed); the bucket-key enum aligns 1:1 with the M29 `AUTH_SCHEMES` constant in `src/cli.js` plus zero zero-evidence catchall (the `unknown` value is already in M29 AUTH_SCHEMES) — extending the bucket-key enum to `mtls`/`aws_sigv4`/`digest`/`hmac`/`webhook_signature` would require a corresponding extension to the M29 classifier, which is itself a material governance event under its own ROADMAP milestone with a fresh re-approval expectation; an implementation-time guard (synchronous throw) MUST fire if `bucketByAuthScheme(capability)` ever returns a value outside the closed seven-value set; a second implementation-time guard MUST fire if the M35 bucket-key enum and M29 AUTH_SCHEMES ever diverge; the eval regression scenario `auth-scheme-index-determinism` locks the enum-closure invariant at merge time |
| M35 manifest mutation through index generation | A naively implemented index generator could attempt to write `auth_scheme_index` back into the manifest (e.g., as a new top-level field), or could call back into `computeCapabilityDigest` in a way that flips digests for previously-approved capabilities. This would silently revoke approval across the manifest on first M35 invocation, duplicating the M26 broad-shape-flip risk and the M30/M31/M32/M33/M34 manifest-mutation risks | M35 is read-only by design: the index generator reads `capabilities[]` and never calls back into manifest builders or digest computation. SYSTEM_SPEC § M35 codifies the no-write invariant; a smoke assertion captures `tusq.manifest.json` mtime and SHA-256 before and after an index run and asserts byte-identity; a separate smoke assertion captures every capability's `capability_digest` before and after and asserts no digest flips |
| M35 `--out` path traversal into `.tusq/` | An operator running `tusq auth index --out .tusq/auth.json` could conflate the index with a governance artifact (a real `.tusq/` artifact has approval implications and a different review pattern) or could overwrite a real `.tusq/` file (e.g., `.tusq/scan.json`, `.tusq/execution-policy.json`) and silently corrupt the governance state | `--out` rejects any path resolving inside `.tusq/` with `--out path must not be inside .tusq/` on stderr and exit 1 (mirroring M30/M31/M32/M33/M34); smoke coverage asserts the rejection path; operators wanting a planning artifact alongside other governance files keep it elsewhere on disk (the operator's choice, not a tusq.dev directory) |
| M35 closed-enum order mistaken as IAM-strength-precedence | An implementer or reviewer could read the closed-enum iteration order `bearer → api_key → session → basic → oauth → none → unknown` as a strength-ordering or trust-ranking statement (since `none` lands second-to-last and `unknown` lands last), and start treating bucket position as a security score, then later expand the enum and silently shift the security-score interpretation. Downstream consumers could derive ad-hoc IAM dashboards from bucket position rather than from explicit IAM-posture fields that don't yet exist. The misread is plausible because `bearer` (canonically OAuth-bearer-token-style) leading and `none` lagging visually suggests a strength ladder | SYSTEM_SPEC § M35 codifies the closed-enum order as a deterministic stable-output convention only — NOT an IAM-strength-precedence, NOT a trust-ranking, NOT a security-strength ladder; the order matches the natural reading order of the M29 `AUTH_SCHEMES` constant (with `unknown` appended last per M32/M33/M34 convention) but carries no security semantic; docs/README/CLI-help MUST NOT describe the order as "strength-ordering," "trust-ranking," "security-ascending," "IAM-strength-precedence," or any phrase implying security semantics; IAM-posture composition is explicitly reserved for the deferred M-IAM-Posture-1 milestone with its own enum and its own acceptance contract; the `aggregation_key` field (`scheme | unknown`) carries the only semantic claim — that the bucket is a closed-enum scheme match or the zero-evidence catchall, NOT a security level |
| M35 case-folding drift on `--scheme` filter relative to manifest lowercase convention | An implementer could naively lower-case the `--scheme <value>` argument before bucket lookup (e.g., `value.toLowerCase()`) so that `tusq auth index --scheme BEARER` succeeds and emits the bearer bucket; this would silently diverge from the manifest's verbatim lowercase `auth_scheme` field convention and mask reviewer-script drift. A reviewer who scripts `--scheme ${process.env.AUTH_SCHEME}` against an env-var that drifts to uppercase would get apparently-correct output, then later see different output if the implementation is hardened to case-sensitive matching, breaking CI silently | M35 implementation MUST match the `--scheme` argument **case-sensitively** against the closed seven-value enum (`bearer`/`api_key`/`session`/`basic`/`oauth`/`none`/`unknown`); uppercase or mixed-case values exit 1 with `Unknown auth scheme:` followed by the value, empty stdout (mirroring the manifest's lowercase verbatim convention); SYSTEM_SPEC § M35 codifies the case-sensitive rule; smoke case (c2) explicitly asserts `--scheme BEARER` exits 1 (NOT exit 0 with the bearer bucket); Constraint 28 (proposed) enumerates the case-sensitive rule as part of the planning-aid framing |
| M36 misread as runtime confidence gate / evidence-quality scoring engine / automated re-classifier | A reviewer reading the `tusq confidence index` output could mistake it for a runtime gate that auto-blocks low-confidence capabilities at execution time, an evidence-quality scoring engine that re-scores capabilities on each run, or an automated re-classifier that promotes capabilities into the `high` tier as evidence improves; this would imply runtime semantics M36 explicitly does NOT have. M36 is a **planning aid** that surfaces what evidence-quality tiers the manifest currently exposes — it does NOT enforce confidence at runtime, does NOT score or re-score evidence quality, does NOT re-classify capabilities, does NOT alter the scanner's `confidence` derivation rules (set in M14/M15), and does NOT persist `confidence_tier` into `tusq.manifest.json` | `--help` framing, SYSTEM_SPEC § M36, Constraint 29, `website/docs/cli-reference.md`, and `website/docs/manifest-format.md` all carry the explicit "planning aid, not a runtime confidence gate, evidence-quality scoring engine, or automated re-classifier" callout; smoke matrix proves zero manifest mutation, zero `capability_digest` flips, and explicitly asserts `confidence_tier` is NOT a key on any post-run capability (non-persistence assertion case h2); deferred successor milestones (M-Risk-1 cross-axis risk-tier, M-Confidence-Statistics-1 distribution roll-up, M-Confidence-Persistence-1 if persistence is later authorized) carry their own acceptance contracts |
| M36 silent threshold drift on `0.85` / `0.6` boundaries | A future implementer could "tune" the tier function thresholds (e.g., raise `0.85` to `0.9` because most express-extracted capabilities sit at `0.76`, or lower `0.6` to `0.5` to reduce the size of the `low` bucket) without realizing the boundary values are PM-frozen at M36 ship and any change is a material governance event. A silent threshold change would re-bucket every capability across every existing fixture overnight, breaking eval determinism and reviewer-aid stability — the same kind of silent reclassification that M28 sensitivity inference and M29 auth scheme classifier explicitly guard against | SYSTEM_SPEC § M36 codifies the boundary values (`>= 0.85` for `high`, `>= 0.6` for `medium`, `< 0.6` for `low`) as PM-frozen and immutable once M36 ships; Constraint 29 (proposed) enumerates threshold changes as material governance events; smoke case (v) explicitly asserts the boundary inclusive/exclusive contract on `0.85`, `0.84999...`, `0.6`, `0.59999...`, `0`, and `1`; the eval `confidence-tier-index-determinism` scenario asserts byte-identical bucket assignments across runs (any silent threshold drift would break this scenario before merge); a future change requires a new ROADMAP milestone with a fresh re-approval expectation |
| M36 silent enum drift on `confidence_tier` bucket-key OR `aggregation_key` | A future implementer could add a fifth value (e.g., `unknown_low`, `auto_classified`, `pending_review`) to the four-value `confidence_tier` enum, or a third value (e.g., `derived`, `inferred`) to the two-value `aggregation_key` enum, without going through a ROADMAP milestone. Reviewer scripts that switch on the closed-enum value would silently miss the new bucket, breaking governance behavior; eval determinism would break; downstream MCP/marketplace consumers (when those ship) would receive an unexpected enum value | M36 implementation guards against drift with a synchronous module-init check in `src/cli.js` that throws if `buildConfidenceIndex` produces a `confidence_tier` outside the four-value enum or an `aggregation_key` outside the two-value enum; SYSTEM_SPEC § M36 codifies both enums as frozen; the `confidence-tier-index-determinism` eval scenario asserts every emitted bucket's enum values are members of the closed sets; the eval would fail before merge if drift were introduced |
| M36 manifest mutation through index generation | A naive implementation could write the derived `confidence_tier` back into `tusq.manifest.json` (treating it as a "computed cache field" the way some indexers persist tier columns) — this would flip every `capability_digest` (because the digest is computed over the capability JSON) and silently break every governance signature, every M16 diff baseline, every M27 redaction-review baseline, every M30/M31/M32/M33/M34/M35 read-only invariant, and every reviewer's mental model that the index is reviewer-aid metadata only | M36 implementation MUST NOT persist `confidence_tier` into the manifest; the tier is computed at index time and discarded after stdout/stderr emission; smoke assertions (case g, h, h2) verify mtime/content/digest invariance AND that no `confidence_tier` key appears on any capability post-run; Constraint 29 codifies the non-persistence rule; the M-Confidence-Persistence-1 deferred successor milestone is the explicit channel for any future persistence decision (with its own enum re-approval, its own digest-flip impact analysis, and its own acceptance contract) |
