| M36 `--out` path traversal into `.tusq/` | An operator running `tusq confidence index --out .tusq/confidence.json` could conflate the index with a governance artifact (a real `.tusq/` artifact has approval implications and a different review pattern) or could overwrite a real `.tusq/` file (e.g., `.tusq/scan.json`, `.tusq/execution-policy.json`) and silently corrupt the governance state | `--out` rejects any path resolving inside `.tusq/` with `--out path must not be inside .tusq/` on stderr and exit 1 (mirroring M30/M31/M32/M33/M34/M35); smoke coverage asserts the rejection path; operators wanting a planning artifact alongside other governance files keep it elsewhere on disk (the operator's choice, not a tusq.dev directory) |
| M36 closed-enum order mistaken as quality-precedence / case-folding drift on `--tier` filter | An implementer or reviewer could read the closed-enum iteration order `high → medium → low → unknown` as a quality-strength-precedence statement (since `high` leads and `low` lags visually) and start treating bucket position as a quality score, then build dashboards on bucket position rather than the underlying numeric `confidence` field; or an implementer could naively lower-case the `--tier <value>` argument so that `--tier HIGH` succeeds and emits the high bucket, silently diverging from the canonical lowercase enum form and masking reviewer-script drift | SYSTEM_SPEC § M36 codifies the closed-enum order as a deterministic stable-output convention only — NOT a quality-precedence, NOT an evidence-strength ranking, NOT a trust-ranking; docs/README/CLI-help MUST NOT describe the order as "evidence-strength-ranked," "trust-ranked," "highest-quality-first," or any phrase implying a quality semantic; cross-axis risk-tier composition is explicitly reserved for the deferred M-Risk-1 milestone; M36 implementation MUST match the `--tier` argument **case-sensitively** against the closed four-value enum (`high`/`medium`/`low`/`unknown`); uppercase or mixed-case values exit 1 with `Unknown confidence tier:` followed by the value, empty stdout; SYSTEM_SPEC § M36 codifies the case-sensitive rule; smoke case (c2) explicitly asserts `--tier HIGH` exits 1 (NOT exit 0 with the high bucket); Constraint 29 (proposed) enumerates the case-sensitive rule as part of the planning-aid framing |
| M37 misread as runtime PII detector / data-leakage prevention engine / compliance certifier | A reviewer or operator could misread the per-`pii_field_count_tier` index as proof that "we have detected all PII at runtime," "we have prevented data leakage," or "we are GDPR/HIPAA/PCI/PHI compliant," and skip downstream review. The per-capability `pii_fields[]` value is a source-literal name hint extracted by M25 (e.g., a field named `password` flips the hint), NOT a runtime PII validation; a capability with `pii_fields.length === 0` may still carry PII at runtime, and a capability bucketed `high` may still be safe if the field names are false positives. The risk is sharper for M37 than for M28/M33 because the tier is numeric-derived and easily mistaken for a quantitative compliance score | SYSTEM_SPEC § M37 codifies the planning-aid framing; Constraint 30 (proposed) forbids "runtime PII detector," "data-leakage prevention engine," "runtime redaction enforcer," "GDPR/HIPAA/PCI/PHI compliance certifier," and any phrase implying runtime enforcement; CLI `--help` carries the explicit "planning aid only" callout naming the M25-name-hint provenance; docs/README/CLI-help MUST NOT describe the index as runtime PII detection or compliance certification; the eval regression scenario `pii-field-count-tier-index-determinism` does NOT validate runtime PII detection — only deterministic tier bucketing of the manifest's `pii_fields[]` array length |
| M37 silent threshold drift on the `0/2/5/6` tier-function boundaries between releases | An implementer could silently change the tier-function thresholds (e.g., raise the `medium` lower-bound from `3` to `4`, or lower the `high` lower-bound from `6` to `5`, or split `high` into `high`/`severe` at `>= 10`) in a future minor release, reclassifying capabilities without operator consent and changing the per-bucket index output. | M37 manifest mutation through index generation | A naively implemented index generator could attempt to write `pii_field_count_tier` back into the manifest (e.g., as a new top-level field on each capability), or could call back into `computeCapabilityDigest` in a way that flips digests for previously-approved capabilities. ## Run-Specific Re-Affirmation — run_2ee1a03651d5d485 / turn_2cc0b42362df3fd3

This roadmap is re-anchored unchanged in run `run_2ee1a03651d5d485` (turn `turn_2cc0b42362df3fd3`, planning phase, attempt 1) on HEAD `a46d3cb`. The M29 milestone (Static Auth Requirements Inference from Manifest Evidence — V1.10) and Constraint 22 carry forward verbatim. `npm test` exits 0 with `Eval regression harness passed (16 scenarios)`; the 13-command CLI surface (init, scan, manifest, compile, serve, review, docs, approve, diff, policy, redaction, version, help) is intact on HEAD; no new top-level noun, no new subcommand, no new dependency.

**Vision-derived charter received this turn (intent_1777171732846_289f, p2):** "[vision] The Promise: embeddable chat, widget, command-palette, and voice surfaces." The PM has materialized a charter sketch for a static, deterministic, manifest-only `tusq surface plan` command (proposed first V2 increment) in `.planning/ROADMAP_NEXT_CANDIDATES.md` § "Vision-Derived Charter Candidate: Static Embeddable-Surface Plan Export (V2 First Step)". The charter sketch enumerates: a new top-level noun `surface` with single subcommand `plan`, the frozen four-value `surface` enum (`chat`/`palette`/`widget`/`voice`), the four-flag surface (`--surface`/`--manifest`/`--out`/`--json`), the per-surface plan shape (eligible/gated capabilities, entry points, redaction/auth posture copy-forward, brand_inputs_required name-only list), the read-only/zero-digest-flip/byte-identical-MCP-and-compile invariants, the empty-capabilities valid-exit-0 rule with the explicit human line `No capabilities in manifest — nothing to plan.`, the empty-stdout-on-exit-1 rule, the closed six-value gating-reason enum, the 10-item acceptance contract (AC-1..AC-10), the determinism eval scenario `surface-plan-determinism` (eval harness 16 → ≥17), the proposed Constraint 23 reviewer-aid framing, the explicit non-goals list (no React/Vue/Lit/Web-Speech runtime; no chat/widget/voice/palette renderable code; no brand-profile read; no `.tusq/` write), and four deferred successor milestones (M-Chat-1, M-Palette-1, M-Widget-1, M-Voice-1) each with its own future acceptance contract.

**This re-affirmation makes no roadmap mutation.** The charter sketch is intentionally housed in the candidate backlog (not in this ROADMAP) because binding it to an M-number, freezing the acceptance contract, adding a SYSTEM_SPEC § Surface-Plan section, and adding Constraint 23 are scope decisions that require human approval at the planning_signoff gate. The four PM-owned planning_signoff gate artifacts remain anchored at the V1.10 boundary; this paragraph records this run's independent verification on HEAD a46d3cb and names the new candidate charter for audit continuity.

## Run-Specific Re-Affirmation — run_42732dba3268a739 / turn_1e0689ffd021d2d5

This roadmap is re-anchored unchanged in run `run_42732dba3268a739` (turn `turn_1e0689ffd021d2d5`, planning phase, attempt 1, runtime `local-pm`) on HEAD `1d3f074`. The M29 milestone (Static Auth Requirements Inference from Manifest Evidence — V1.10) and Constraint 22 carry forward verbatim. `npm test` exits 0 with `Smoke tests passed` and `Eval regression harness passed (16 scenarios)`; the 13-command CLI surface (init, scan, manifest, compile, serve, review, docs, approve, diff, policy, redaction, version, help) is intact on HEAD; no new top-level noun, no new subcommand, no new dependency.

**Vision-derived charter received this turn (intent_1777173722739_5899, p2):** "[vision] The Promise: a self-hostable runtime and MCP server." Distinct from the prior run's embeddable-surface charter; this run targets the runtime + MCP half of **The Promise** in VISION.md. The PM has materialized a charter sketch for a **Static MCP Server Descriptor Export** in `.planning/ROADMAP_NEXT_CANDIDATES.md` § "Vision-Derived Charter Candidate: MCP Server Static Descriptor Export (V2 Self-Host First Step)". The charter sketch acknowledges that the vision goal is **partially served at V1.10** — `tusq serve` already provides a describe-only local MCP endpoint (`tools/list` / `tools/call` / `dry_run_plan`) and the OSS is CLI-first / file-first / runs entirely locally. The unserved parts decompose into four future milestones: (1) static MCP server descriptor as a hashable/diffable/signable artifact; (2) generated auth adapters (deferred to M-Runtime-Auth-1); (3) execution runtime beyond describe-only (deferred to M-Runtime-Exec-1); (4) MCP marketplace packaging (deferred to M-MCP-Marketplace-1).

The charter sketch enumerates: an **open scope decision** the operator must resolve at the planning_signoff gate — noun-vs-flag form, with three candidate forms (A) new top-level noun `mcp` with subcommand `export`, (B) flag-only extension `tusq serve --export <path>`, (C) subcommand under a future `plan` hub (`tusq plan mcp`); the static descriptor output shape with frozen `schema_version` literal, copy-forward of `manifest_version`/`generated_at`/`mcp_server_name`/`mcp_server_version`, closed three-value `runtime_posture` boolean block (`describe_only_supported: true`, `execution_supported: false`, `auth_adapter_generation_supported: false`), `tools[]` for approved capabilities with M9 + M27 + M28 + M29 copy-forward fields plus `audit_required` deterministic derivation, `gated_tools[]` with closed six-value reason-code enum, `registry_metadata` frozen named-list (no values), `derived_from` deterministic pointer with manifest_sha256 and `capability_digest` copy-forward, `disclaimers` frozen literal text array; the read-only/zero-digest-flip/byte-identical-MCP-and-compile invariants; the empty-capabilities valid-exit-0 rule with the explicit human line `No capabilities in manifest — nothing to export.`; the empty-stdout-on-exit-1 rule; the determinism eval scenario `mcp-descriptor-determinism` (eval harness 16 → ≥17); the proposed Constraint 24 reviewer-aid framing forbidding "self-hostable runtime generator," "AI runtime engine," "MCP marketplace publisher," "auth adapter generator," "MCP execution runtime," "registry-certified output"; the explicit non-goals list (no execution beyond describe-only, no auth adapter code, no marketplace registry call, no new dependency in `package.json`, no network I/O, no `.tusq/` write unless `--out` given, no external schema validation at emit time); the 10-item acceptance contract (AC-1..AC-10); and four deferred successor milestones (M-Runtime-Auth-1, M-Runtime-Trace-1, M-Runtime-Exec-1, M-MCP-Marketplace-1) each with its own future acceptance contract.

**This re-affirmation makes no roadmap mutation.** The charter sketch is intentionally housed in the candidate backlog (not in this ROADMAP) because binding it to an M-number, choosing the form (A/B/C), freezing the acceptance contract, adding a SYSTEM_SPEC § MCP-Descriptor-Export section, and adding Constraint 24 are scope decisions that require human approval at the planning_signoff gate. The four PM-owned planning_signoff gate artifacts remain anchored at the V1.10 boundary; this paragraph records this run's independent verification on HEAD 1d3f074 and names the new candidate charter for audit continuity. Both vision-derived candidates (Static Embeddable-Surface Plan Export from `run_2ee1a03651d5d485` and Static MCP Server Descriptor Export from this run) coexist in `ROADMAP_NEXT_CANDIDATES.md` as mutually-independent operator-decision-pending items.
